</lightning-record-edit-form>
SOQL + SOSL — Complete Master Guide
Every query pattern you need for senior-level interviews — 30+ patterns with full working code
SOQL Complete Reference — all syntax patterns in one placeSOQL MASTER▼
// ─── BASIC SYNTAX ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
SELECT Id, Name, LoanAmount__c, Status__c
FROM Loan__c
WHERE Status__c = :statusVar          // bind variable — safe, prevents injection
AND LoanAmount__c > 200000
AND LoanType__c IN ('FHA', 'VA')
AND LoanOfficer__c != null
AND Name LIKE '%Smith%'              // % = any chars (wildcard)
ORDER BY CreatedDate DESC NULLS LAST
LIMIT 200 OFFSET 400               // pagination: skip 400, get next 200

// ─── CHILD-TO-PARENT (traverse UP) ───────────────────────────────────────────
List<Contact> contacts = [
    SELECT Id, FirstName, LastName,
           Account.Name,                   // parent — standard relationship
           Account.Phone,
           Account.Owner.Name,             // grandparent field
           Account.Parent.Industry         // great-grandparent (up to 5 levels)
    FROM Contact WHERE Account.Type = 'Broker'
];
// Custom object child-to-parent: use __r suffix
[SELECT Application__r.Name, Application__r.Status__c FROM Loan__c WHERE Id = :id]

// ─── PARENT-TO-CHILD (traverse DOWN — subquery) ──────────────────────────────
List<Account> accounts = [
    SELECT Id, Name,
        (SELECT Id, LoanAmount__c, Status__c FROM Loans__r ORDER BY CreatedDate DESC),
        (SELECT Id, FirstName, LastName, Email FROM Contacts WHERE IsActive__c = true)
    FROM Account WHERE Id IN :accountIds
];
for(Account a : accounts) {
    for(Loan__c l : a.Loans__r) { System.debug(l.LoanAmount__c); }
}

// ─── AGGREGATE QUERIES ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
List<AggregateResult> results = [
    SELECT LoanType__c, LoanOfficer__r.Name officerName,
           COUNT(Id) loanCount,
           SUM(LoanAmount__c) totalFunded,
           AVG(LoanAmount__c) avgLoan,
           MIN(LoanAmount__c) smallest,
           MAX(LoanAmount__c) largest
    FROM Loan__c
    WHERE Status__c = 'Funded'
    GROUP BY LoanType__c, LoanOfficer__r.Name
    HAVING COUNT(Id) > 3           // filter ON aggregated results
    ORDER BY SUM(LoanAmount__c) DESC
];
for(AggregateResult ar : results) {
    System.debug((String)ar.get('officerName') + ': ' + (Integer)ar.get('loanCount'));
}

// ─── SEMI-JOIN and ANTI-JOIN ──────────────────────────────────────────────────
// Semi-join (IN with subquery) — contacts who ARE borrowers on active loans
[SELECT Id, Name FROM Contact
 WHERE Id IN (SELECT Borrower__c FROM Loan_Borrower__c WHERE Loan__r.Status__c = 'Active')]

// Anti-join (NOT IN with subquery) — loans with NO documents uploaded
[SELECT Id, Name FROM Loan__c
 WHERE Id NOT IN (SELECT LinkedEntityId FROM ContentDocumentLink)]

// ─── DYNAMIC SOQL (safe patterns) ────────────────────────────────────────────
public static List<Loan__c> searchLoans(String status, String loanType) {
    // Whitelist allowed values — never trust user input directly
    Set<String> validStatuses = new Set<String>{'Active','Processing','Approved'};
    if(!validStatuses.contains(status)) throw new IllegalArgumentException('Invalid status');
    // Use bind variable :status — prevents injection even in dynamic SOQL
    String query = 'SELECT Id, Name FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c = :status';
    if(String.isNotBlank(loanType)) {
        String safeLoanType = String.escapeSingleQuotes(loanType);
        query += ' AND LoanType__c = \'' + safeLoanType + '\'';
    }
    query += ' WITH USER_MODE ORDER BY Name LIMIT 200';
    return Database.query(query);
}

// ─── SECURITY ENFORCEMENT ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// WITH USER_MODE — best modern approach (API 56+)
[SELECT Id, SSN__c FROM Loan__c WITH USER_MODE]
// Strips inaccessible fields silently — no error if user can't see SSN__c

// FOR UPDATE — row locking to prevent concurrent modification
List<Loan__c> loans = [SELECT Id, Status__c FROM Loan__c WHERE Id IN :ids FOR UPDATE];
// Locks records — other transactions must wait until this one commits
// Use for: financial state transitions, preventing double-processing

// ─── OFFSET PAGINATION ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
@AuraEnabled(cacheable=true)
public static Map<String,Object> getLoansPage(Integer pageNum, Integer pageSize) {
    Integer offset = (pageNum - 1) * pageSize;
    List<Loan__c> loans = [SELECT Id, Name, LoanAmount__c FROM Loan__c
                           ORDER BY Name LIMIT :pageSize OFFSET :offset];
    Integer total = [SELECT COUNT() FROM Loan__c];
    return new Map<String,Object>{'records'=>loans,'total'=>total,'hasMore'=>(offset+pageSize)<total};
}
// OFFSET limitation: max 2000. For larger data, use cursor-based pagination (by Id or Date)
SOSL Complete Reference — all syntax, search groups, when to use vs SOQLSOSL MASTER▼
// ─── SOSL BASICS ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// SOSL searches a Salesforce-maintained search index across MULTIPLE objects at once
// Use SOSL when: user types a search term + you want results from multiple objects
// Use SOQL when: exact field match, aggregates, relationship queries

FIND {Smith}               // search term — must be at least 2 characters
IN ALL FIELDS              // search scope: ALL, NAME, PHONE, EMAIL
RETURNING
    Account(Id, Name, Phone
            WHERE Industry = 'Financial Services'
            ORDER BY Name LIMIT 10),
    Contact(Id, FirstName, LastName, Email),
    Loan__c(Id, Name, LoanAmount__c, Status__c WHERE Status__c = 'Active')
LIMIT 200                  // global limit — applies across ALL objects

// ─── SOSL IN APEX ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
List<List<SObject>> results = [
    FIND :searchTerm             // bind variable works in SOSL too
    IN NAME FIELDS
    RETURNING Contact(Id, FirstName, LastName), Loan__c(Id, Name)
    LIMIT 50
];
List<Contact> contacts = (List<Contact>) results[0]; // index matches RETURNING order
List<Loan__c> loans = (List<Loan__c>) results[1];

// ─── SOSL WILDCARDS ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// * = zero or more chars (prefix/suffix): 'Smi*' matches Smith, Smithson, Smithy
// ? = exactly one char: 'Smi?h' matches Smith, Smieh, Smiyh
// NOTE: Wildcard ONLY queries like '*' are not allowed (must have chars before *)

String searchTerm = 'Smi*'; // prefix search
List<List<SObject>> r = Search.query('FIND {'+searchTerm+'} IN NAME FIELDS RETURNING Contact LIMIT 20');

// ─── SEARCH GROUPS ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// IN ALL FIELDS    — all text, phone, email, name fields
// IN NAME FIELDS   — Name, FirstName, LastName fields only (fastest)
// IN PHONE FIELDS  — phone number fields only
// IN EMAIL FIELDS  — email fields only
// IN SIDEBAR FIELDS — fields checked for global search sidebar

// ─── SOSL vs SOQL FOR TEXT SEARCH ────────────────────────────────────────────
// SOQL WHERE Name LIKE '%Smith%'  → full table scan → SLOW on large objects
// SOSL FIND {Smith} IN NAME FIELDS → uses search index → FAST

// ─── GOVERNOR LIMITS ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// SOSL: 20 queries per transaction (separate limit from SOQL's 100)
// SOSL returns max 2,000 records total (200 per object in RETURNING)
// SOSL does NOT count toward SOQL query limit
// Test SOSL in test classes:
Test.setFixedSearchResults(new List<Id>{ contact.Id, loan.Id });
// Forces SOSL to return specific records in test context
SOQL Aggregate Functions — complete reference with AggregateResultSOQL MASTER▼
// All aggregate functions
SELECT
  COUNT()                    cnt,      // count all rows (no field needed)
  COUNT(Id)                  cntId,    // count non-null values
  COUNT_DISTINCT(OwnerId)    owners,   // count unique owners
  SUM(Amount__c)             total,
  AVG(Amount__c)             average,
  MIN(CloseDate__c)          earliest,
  MAX(CloseDate__c)          latest
FROM Loan__c
WHERE Status__c = 'Active'
GROUP BY Status__c
HAVING COUNT(Id) > 10
ORDER BY SUM(Amount__c) DESC
LIMIT 10

// Access results
List<AggregateResult> results = [SELECT Status__c status, COUNT(Id) cnt, SUM(Amount__c) total FROM Loan__c GROUP BY Status__c];
for (AggregateResult ar : results) {
  String status = (String) ar.get('status');
  Integer count  = (Integer) ar.get('cnt');
  Decimal total  = (Decimal) ar.get('total');
}

// GROUP BY ROLLUP — adds subtotal rows
SELECT Branch__c, COUNT(Id) cnt FROM Loan__c GROUP BY ROLLUP(Branch__c)
// Returns: rows per branch + one grand total row (Branch__c = null)

// GROUP BY CUBE — all combination subtotals
SELECT Branch__c, Loan_Type__c, COUNT(Id) cnt FROM Loan__c GROUP BY CUBE(Branch__c, Loan_Type__c)
SOQL performance — indexing, selective queries, and Query Plan interpretationSOQL MASTER▼
// Run EXPLAIN on any SOQL in Developer Console
EXPLAIN SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c = 'Active' AND OwnerId = :userId

// EXPLAIN output:
// {
//   "plans": [{
//     "cardinality": 1500,      // estimated matching rows
//     "fields": ["OwnerId"],    // which index was chosen
//     "leading": "OwnerId",     // which field leads the index scan
//     "cost": 0.42,             // relative cost (lower = faster)
//     "sobjectCardinality": 50000, // total rows in the object
//     "tableEnumOrId": "Loan__c",
//     "type": "Index"           // Index = good. TableScan = investigate.
//   }]
// }

// Selectivity rule: index used only if indexed condition filters to small % of rows
// < 10% of rows for most objects
// < 5% of rows for objects with >100K records

// Default indexed fields: Id, Name, OwnerId, CreatedDate, LastModifiedDate, SystemModstamp,
//   all External ID fields, all MD relationship fields, Unique-checked fields

// Request custom index from Salesforce (for frequently queried non-indexed fields):
// Contact Salesforce Support → request selective index on Loan__c.Status__c
Security & Sharing — Complete Reference Guide
The complete 4-layer Salesforce security model — every concept with code examples for senior interviews
Complete Salesforce Security Model — all 4 layers with code enforcementSECURITY MASTER▼
// THE 4 LAYERS — must pass ALL to access a field value on a record
// Layer 1: ORG → Layer 2: OBJECT (CRUD) → Layer 3: FIELD (FLS) → Layer 4: RECORD (Sharing)

// ─── LAYER 2: OBJECT CRUD ENFORCEMENT IN APEX ─────────────────────────────────
public static void safeDML(List<Loan__c> loans, String operation) {
    Schema.DescribeSObjectResult describe = Loan__c.sObjectType.getDescribe();
    if(operation == 'insert' && !describe.isCreateable())
        throw new SecurityException('No Create permission on Loan__c');
    if(operation == 'update' && !describe.isUpdateable())
        throw new SecurityException('No Edit permission on Loan__c');
    if(operation == 'delete' && !describe.isDeletable())
        throw new SecurityException('No Delete permission on Loan__c');
}

// ─── LAYER 3: FLS ENFORCEMENT — 4 METHODS ────────────────────────────────────
// Method 1: WITH USER_MODE in SOQL (best — modern API 56+)
List<Loan__c> loans = [SELECT Id, SSN__c, LoanAmount__c FROM Loan__c WITH USER_MODE];
// SSN__c silently removed from results if user cannot see it — no error thrown
// Also enforces CRUD during DML in the same transaction

// Method 2: WITH SECURITY_ENFORCED (older — throws QueryException)
try { List<Loan__c> l = [SELECT Id, SSN__c FROM Loan__c WITH SECURITY_ENFORCED]; }
catch(QueryException e) { /* user cannot access SSN__c */ }
// Limitation: cannot use in subqueries, cannot use with GROUP BY/ROLLUP

// Method 3: stripInaccessible (for DML operations)
SObjectAccessDecision decision = Security.stripInaccessible(
    AccessType.CREATABLE, loansToInsert
);
insert decision.getRecords(); // SSN__c removed if user cannot create it
// AccessType: CREATABLE, UPDATABLE, READABLE, UPSERTABLE

// Method 4: Manual DescribeFieldResult (most granular control)
Schema.DescribeFieldResult dfr = Loan__c.SSN__c.getDescribe();
if(dfr.isAccessible()) { /* safe to read */ }
if(dfr.isUpdateable()) { /* safe to update */ }

// ─── LAYER 4: RECORD SHARING ──────────────────────────────────────────────────
// OWD → Role Hierarchy → Sharing Rules → Manual Sharing → Apex Sharing

// WITH SHARING vs WITHOUT SHARING vs INHERITED SHARING
public with sharing class LoanService {
    // SOQL returns ONLY records the running user can see (respects OWD + sharing rules)
    // DML on records the user has no Edit access to FAILS with "insufficient access"
}
public without sharing class AdminBatch {
    // SOQL returns ALL records regardless of sharing (system mode)
    // DML always works (system mode — no sharing enforcement)
    // RISK: can read/write records the running user normally cannot access
}
public inherited sharing class UtilHelper {
    // Inherits the sharing mode of the CLASS THAT CALLED IT
    // Best for: helper/utility classes that should adapt to their context
}

// ─── APEX MANAGED SHARING ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// Every custom object gets a __Share object automatically
// Loan__c → Loan__Share, Application__c → Application__Share
// Requires: custom Sharing Reason defined on the object in Setup

// Grant access:
Loan__Share share = new Loan__Share();
share.ParentId = loanId;
share.UserOrGroupId = brokerId;       // User Id or Group Id
share.AccessLevel = 'Read';          // 'Read' or 'Edit' (not 'Full' for custom)
share.RowCause = Schema.Loan__Share.RowCause.BrokerAccess__c;
Database.insert(share, false);

// Revoke access:
delete [SELECT Id FROM Loan__Share
        WHERE ParentId=:loanId AND UserOrGroupId=:brokerId
        AND RowCause=Schema.Loan__Share.RowCause.BrokerAccess__c];

// ─── PROFILE vs PERMISSION SET vs PSG ────────────────────────────────────────
// Profile: Every user has exactly ONE. Sets BASELINE restrictions.
// Permission Set: ADDITIVE. Users can have MANY. Adds access on top of Profile.
// Permission Set Group: Bundle of multiple PSs. Can include a Muting PS.
// Muting Permission Set: REMOVES specific permissions within a PSG (override).
// Direction: Profiles → minimal. All granular access via Permission Sets/Groups.
Permission Set Groups and Muting Permission Sets — modern permission architectureSECURITY FULL▼

Modern Salesforce orgs use Minimum Access profile + Permission Sets + Permission Set Groups. This is cleaner, more auditable, and easier to manage than complex profiles.

LayerRoleExample
Profile (Minimum Access)Gives baseline — login, object visibilityAll users get 'Minimum Access - Salesforce' profile
Permission SetAdds specific permissions'Loan Officer Permissions' — CRUD on Loan__c, Contact__c
Permission Set GroupBundles related permission sets'Loan Officer Group' = Loan Officer PS + Contact PS + DocuSign PS
Muting PSRemoves specific perms from a PSGRemove 'Delete Loan' from the Loan Officer Group for junior officers
// Check if user has a Permission Set via Apex
List<PermissionSetAssignment> assignments = [
  SELECT PermissionSet.Name FROM PermissionSetAssignment
  WHERE AssigneeId = :UserInfo.getUserId()
  AND PermissionSet.Name = 'Loan_Officer_Permissions'
];
Boolean hasPermSet = !assignments.isEmpty();

// Check Custom Permission (preferred approach)
Boolean canApproveJumbo = FeatureManagement.checkPermission('Approve_Jumbo_Loans');
Shield Platform Encryption — what it is, when you need it, what it breaksSECURITY FULL▼
  • What it does — encrypts field values at rest (in Salesforce's database storage) using AES-256
  • Required for — HIPAA, PCI-DSS, GLBA, SOC 2 compliance. Mortgage orgs: SSN, full account numbers, income data
  • Deterministic encryption — allows SOQL equality search on encrypted field. Non-deterministic = cannot query it.
  • Tenant Secret (BYOK) — you control the encryption key. Salesforce cannot read your data even internally.
  • What breaks — LIKE/contains queries on encrypted fields, >/< comparisons, duplicate rules on encrypted fields, some formula fields, calculated fields, workflow field updates that reference encrypted fields
Test first

Before encrypting a field in production: create a full sandbox (production data copy), enable encryption there, run ALL automation, flows, integrations, and SOQL that touch that field. Fix anything that breaks. Only then encrypt in production.

Agentforce — Complete Developer Guide
Everything a senior Salesforce developer needs for Agentforce interviews in 2025–2026
Agentforce Architecture — complete overview for senior developersAGENTFORCE▼

Agentforce is Salesforce's autonomous AI agent platform (GA: Fall 2024). Agents reason, act, and complete multi-step tasks without constant human input. As a developer, you extend agents by building custom Apex Actions, Flows, and Prompt Templates.

ComponentWhat It IsDeveloper Role
AgentThe autonomous AI entity with Role, Goals, InstructionsConfigure in Agent Builder
LLM (Large Language Model)The AI reasoning engine — GPT-4o, Claude, xGen etc.Select in LLM Gateway
TopicsLogical groupings of related Actions (e.g., "Loan Processing" topic)Define scope and Actions per topic
ActionsWhat the agent CAN do — Flow, Apex, Standard CRM, APIBuild Apex @InvocableMethod actions
GroundingHow agent accesses real data — Data Cloud, Knowledge, CRM recordsDesign data access strategy
Einstein Trust LayerSecurity wrapper — PII masking, zero data retention, audit trailConfigure masking rules
// Building a custom Apex Action for Agentforce
// The ACTION DESCRIPTION is what the LLM reads to decide WHEN to call this action
// Write it as: "Use this action when [intent]. Returns [what]. Requires [input]."

public class LoanStatusAgentAction {

    public class Request {
        @InvocableVariable(label='Borrower Email' required=true
            description='Email of the borrower asking about their loan')
        public String borrowerEmail;
    }

    public class Response {
        @InvocableVariable(label='Status Summary')
        public String statusSummary;
        @InvocableVariable(label='Next Steps')
        public String nextSteps;
    }

    @InvocableMethod(
        label='Get Loan Status for Borrower'
        description='Use this when a borrower asks about their loan status, progress, or next steps. Requires borrower email. Returns current status and what happens next.'
        category='Loan Processing'
    )
    public static List<Response> getLoanStatus(List<Request> requests) {
        List<Response> responses = new List<Response>();
        for(Request req : requests) {
            Response resp = new Response();
            List<Loan__c> loans = [SELECT Id, Name, Status__c, Next_Steps__c
                FROM Loan__c WHERE BorrowerEmail__c = :req.borrowerEmail
                AND Status__c != 'Closed' WITH USER_MODE LIMIT 1];
            resp.statusSummary = loans.isEmpty() ? 'No active loan found'
                : 'Your loan ' + loans[0].Name + ' is in ' + loans[0].Status__c;
            resp.nextSteps = loans.isEmpty() ? 'Contact your loan officer'
                : (loans[0].Next_Steps__c != null ? loans[0].Next_Steps__c : 'Watch for updates');
            responses.add(resp);
        }
        return responses;
    }
}
Key developer tips for Agentforce

1. Write action descriptions as the LLM will read them — be specific about WHEN to call. 2. Actions must be @InvocableMethod — same pattern you already use for Flow. 3. Always use WITH USER_MODE in actions — respect user permissions even in AI context. 4. The Trust Layer handles PII masking automatically — SSN and credit card numbers are masked before reaching the LLM.

Agentforce vs Einstein Copilot — what is the difference in 2025?AGENTFORCE▼
FeatureEinstein Copilot (legacy)Agentforce (current)
Target userInternal Salesforce users — sidebar assistantAny user — internal or external customers
AutonomyHuman-in-the-loop — user drives each actionAutonomous — agent decides and acts independently
TriggerUser asks a questionEvents, schedules, or user requests
ChannelsSalesforce UI sidebar onlyEmail, chat, Slack, voice, web, API
ConfigurationCopilot Builder (deprecated)Agent Builder (current)
Status (2025)Merging into AgentforceActive — all Salesforce AI investment here

In practice: As of 2025, Salesforce unified Copilot into Agentforce. A "Copilot" is simply a Salesforce-user-facing Agentforce agent. The distinction matters mainly for legacy configurations — all new AI builds use Agentforce and Agent Builder.

How do you build a custom Apex Action for Agentforce — complete implementation?AGENTFORCE▼

Apex Actions are Invocable methods that Agentforce agents call to take actions in Salesforce. They are the bridge between the AI reasoning layer and your business logic.

// Step 1: Create an Invocable Apex class
public class LoanStatusAction {
  public class LoanStatusRequest {
    @InvocableVariable(label='Loan Number' description='The loan number to check' required=true)
    public String loanNumber;
  }
  public class LoanStatusResponse {
    @InvocableVariable(label='Status') public String status;
    @InvocableVariable(label='Amount') public Decimal amount;
    @InvocableVariable(label='Borrower Name') public String borrowerName;
    @InvocableVariable(label='Next Steps') public String nextSteps;
  }

  @InvocableMethod(label='Get Loan Status' description='Returns current status and next steps for a loan')
  public static List<LoanStatusResponse> getLoanStatus(List<LoanStatusRequest> requests) {
    List<LoanStatusResponse> responses = new List<LoanStatusResponse>();
    for (LoanStatusRequest req : requests) {
      List<Loan__c> loans = [SELECT Name, Status__c, Amount__c, Account__r.Name
        FROM Loan__c WHERE Name = :req.loanNumber WITH SECURITY_ENFORCED LIMIT 1];
      LoanStatusResponse res = new LoanStatusResponse();
      if (loans.isEmpty()) { res.status = 'Not Found'; res.nextSteps = 'Verify the loan number and try again.'; }
      else {
        res.status = loans[0].Status__c;
        res.amount = loans[0].Amount__c;
        res.borrowerName = loans[0].Account__r.Name;
        res.nextSteps = getNextStepsForStatus(loans[0].Status__c);
      }
      responses.add(res);
    }
    return responses;
  }

  private static String getNextStepsForStatus(String status) {
    Map<String,String> nextSteps = new Map<String,String>{
      'Applied' => 'Application received. Credit check scheduled within 24 hours.',
      'Credit_Approved' => 'Credit approved. Underwriter review in progress.',
      'Approved' => 'Loan approved! Closing scheduled. Check documents tab.',
      'Funded' => 'Congratulations! Loan funded. First payment due next month.'
    };
    return nextSteps.get(status) ?? 'Contact your loan officer for status details.';
  }
}

// Step 2: Register as Agent Action in Setup → Agent Actions → New
// Step 3: Add to Agent Topic: "Loan Status Inquiries"
// Step 4: Write Topic Instructions for when agent should use this action
What are Prompt Templates — how do you build them for Agentforce?AGENTFORCE▼

Prompt Templates are reusable, merge-field-enabled prompts that agents use to generate consistent AI responses. They use Salesforce data as grounding context.

// Prompt Template structure (configured in Setup → Prompt Template Builder)
// Type: Flex Template (for agents) or Sales Email / Field Generation

// Example: Loan Summary Template
// Template Name: Loan Summary for Agent
// Object: Loan__c

// Template body (with merge fields):
/*
You are a helpful mortgage assistant. Summarize the following loan for the borrower.
Be professional, clear, and under 150 words.

Loan Details:
- Loan Number: {!Loan__c.Name}
- Borrower: {!Loan__c.Account__r.Name}
- Loan Amount: {!Loan__c.Amount__c}
- Interest Rate: {!Loan__c.Interest_Rate__c}%
- Status: {!Loan__c.Status__c}
- Estimated Closing Date: {!Loan__c.CloseDate__c}

Provide a clear summary of where this loan stands and what the borrower should expect next.
*/

// Invoke from Apex (in an Invocable method for an agent action)
ConnectApi.EinsteinLLM.generateMessagesForPromptTemplate(
  new ConnectApi.EinsteinLLMGenerateMessagesInput()
    .setPromptTemplateName('Loan_Summary_Template')
    .setInputParams(new Map<String,String>{ 'Loan__cId' => loanId })
);
Salesforce Flow — Complete Developer Guide
All 6 flow types, integration patterns, debugging, and decision framework for senior interviews
All 6 Flow types — when to use each, key differences, and example for eachFLOW MASTER▼
Flow TypeTriggerKey Use CaseCan Call Apex?
Record-Triggered (Before Save)Record DML — before commitSet default field values, simple validationYes (Invocable)
Record-Triggered (After Save)Record DML — after commitCreate related records, send emailsYes (Invocable)
Screen FlowUser clicks button / launches manuallyGuided wizard, multi-step data entryYes
Schedule-Triggered FlowTime-based schedule (daily, weekly)Nightly reminders, cleanup jobsYes
Autolaunched FlowApex, REST API, another Flow (subflow)Reusable logic modulesYes
Platform Event-TriggeredPlatform Event publishedReact to events declarativelyYes
// Calling a Flow from Apex (Autolaunched flow)
Map<String,Object> inputs = new Map<String,Object>{
    'loanId' => loanId,
    'newStatus' => 'Approved'
};
Flow.Interview.Loan_Status_Handler interview =
    new Flow.Interview.Loan_Status_Handler(inputs);
interview.start();
String result = (String) interview.getVariableValue('outputMessage');

// Decision rule: Flow vs Apex
// USE FLOW: simple field defaults, email sends, creating 1 related record,
// admin-maintainable logic, no complex bulk operations needed
// USE APEX: bulk operations (200+ records), complex SOQL, callouts,
// complex error handling, performance-critical operations
How do you create an @InvocableMethod for Flow — complete implementation with input/output?FLOW APEX▼
// Complete @InvocableMethod for Flow — mortgage credit check action
public class CreditCheckFlowAction {

    public class Request {
        @InvocableVariable(label='Loan ID' required=true
            description='Salesforce ID of the Loan record')
        public Id loanId;
        @InvocableVariable(label='Borrower SSN' required=true)
        public String ssn;
    }

    public class Result {
        @InvocableVariable(label='FICO Score') public Integer ficoScore;
        @InvocableVariable(label='Credit Decision') public String decision;
        @InvocableVariable(label='Is Approved') public Boolean isApproved;
        @InvocableVariable(label='Error Message') public String errorMessage;
    }

    // MUST return List<T> and accept List<T> — Flow calls in bulk
    @InvocableMethod(
        label='Pull Credit Report'
        description='Calls Experian to get FICO score. Use for credit check step in loan flow.'
        category='Loan Processing'
    )
    public static List<Result> pullCredit(List<Request> requests) {
        List<Result> results = new List<Result>();
        for(Request req : requests) {
            Result r = new Result();
            try {
                // For callouts from Flow: enqueue Queueable — cannot do direct callout
                Id jobId = System.enqueueJob(new CreditPullQueueable(req.loanId, req.ssn));
                r.decision = 'Credit check initiated. Job: ' + jobId;
                r.isApproved = true; // will be updated by Queueable when done
            } catch(Exception e) {
                r.errorMessage = e.getMessage(); r.isApproved = false;
            }
            results.add(r);
        }
        return results;
    }
}
Record-Triggered Flow vs Apex Trigger — when to use each?FLOW MASTER▼
ScenarioFlowApex Trigger
Simple field update on save✓ Before-Save flow — fastest, no extra DMLOverkill
Send email when status changes✓ After-Save flow + Email ActionPossible but more code
Complex validation with error messagesBoth work — Apex gives more control✓ for very complex rules
Callout to external system✓ After-Save + async path✓ @future or Queueable
Process 200 records in bulk✓ Flow is bulkified automatically✓ with bulkified handler
Complex logic with loops/mapsLimited✓ Apex is more powerful
Non-developer to maintain✓ Flow = clicksTechnical debt if non-developer edits Apex
Multi-object transaction with rollbackLimited✓ Apex Savepoint/try-catch
Default guidance

Salesforce recommends Flow-first for automation. Use Apex when logic is too complex for Flow, requires callouts, or has performance requirements Flow can't meet. Never mix — pick one approach per use case.

Flow debugging — how do you troubleshoot a failing Flow?FLOW MASTER▼
  • Debug button in Flow Builder — runs the flow in debug mode, shows each element's input/output values and which path was taken
  • Flow Error Emails — when a flow fails in production, Salesforce emails the running user and the flow's admin with the error and element that failed
  • Debug Logs — enable for the running user. Search for 'FLOW' in the log to see flow execution details
  • Paused Flow Interviews — Setup → Paused Flow Interviews. Flows waiting at Pause elements appear here. Can be resumed or deleted.
  • Flow Exception handling — add a Fault Path to every element that can fail (Get Records, Create Records, Apex Action calls). Fault Paths handle errors gracefully instead of showing the generic error to users.
// Common Flow failure causes:
// 1. Get Records element returns null — add null check branch
// 2. Required field not set before Create Records — validate all required fields
// 3. Apex Action throws exception — action must catch internally or flow gets fault path
// 4. DML on locked records — flow runs in user context by default
// 5. Governor limits — flows count against same limits as Apex in the same transaction
How do Screen Flows work — key elements and LWC integration?FLOW MASTER▼

Screen Flows are user-facing wizards that collect input and drive processes. They can embed standard Salesforce components or custom LWC components.

// Screen Flow → LWC component integration
// In LWC, expose @api properties that Flow passes data into, and fire events to pass data back

// loanApplicationScreen.js
import { LightningElement, api } from 'lwc';
export default class LoanApplicationScreen extends LightningElement {
  @api loanType = '';   // Flow passes data IN via these @api props
  @api minAmount = 0;

  // Flow reads data OUT via FlowAttributeChangeEvent
  handleAmountChange(event) {
    const amount = event.target.value;
    this.dispatchEvent(new FlowAttributeChangeEvent('loanAmount', amount));
  }

  // Signal Flow to navigate to next screen
  handleNext() {
    this.dispatchEvent(new FlowNavigationNextEvent());
  }
}

// Register LWC for Flow: in .js-meta.xml add:
// <targets><target>lightning__FlowScreen</target></targets>
// <targetConfigs><targetConfig targets="lightning__FlowScreen">
//   <property name="loanType" type="String" label="Loan Type"/>
//   <property name="loanAmount" type="String" label="Loan Amount" role="outputOnly"/>
// </targetConfig></targetConfigs>
Reports & Dashboards — Complete Developer Guide
Report types, Apex Analytics API, dynamic dashboards, scheduled reports — everything for senior interviews
Complete Reports & Dashboards reference — all types, filters, and Apex APIREPORTS MASTER▼
Report TypeStructureCharts?Best For
TabularSimple rows, like spreadsheetNoData export, simple lists
SummaryRows grouped by 1-5 fields with subtotalsYesPipeline by stage, totals by category
MatrixGrouped by row AND column (cross-tab)YesLoan amounts by type AND month
JoinedMultiple blocks from different objectsYes (per block)Side-by-side comparisons
// ─── READ REPORT FROM APEX ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// Synchronous run (max 2000 rows)
Reports.ReportResults results = Reports.ReportManager.runReport('00O...', true);
// true = include detail rows. false = summary only (faster)

// Get grand total fact (for Tabular and Summary reports)
Reports.ReportFactWithDetails grandTotal =
    (Reports.ReportFactWithDetails) results.getFactMap().get('T!T');

// Iterate rows and cells
for(Reports.ReportDetailRow row : grandTotal.getRows()) {
    List<Reports.ReportDataCell> cells = row.getDataCells();
    String loanName = cells[0].getLabel();  // formatted display value
    Object loanAmount = cells[1].getValue(); // raw value (Decimal, Date, Id etc)
}

// Override report filters at runtime (without changing saved report)
Reports.ReportMetadata meta = Reports.ReportManager.describeReport('00O...').getReportMetadata();
Reports.ReportFilter filter = new Reports.ReportFilter();
filter.setColumn('STATUS');
filter.setOperator('equals');
filter.setValue('Active');
meta.setReportFilters(new List<Reports.ReportFilter>{ filter });
Reports.ReportResults filtered = Reports.ReportManager.runReport(meta, true);

// ─── DYNAMIC DASHBOARD ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────
// "Run As": Logged-in user → each viewer sees THEIR OWN data
// Use case: Loan Officer Dashboard — Officer A sees their loans, Officer B sees theirs
// Limitation: Cannot be scheduled. Cannot use dashboard filters.
// Max: 10 dynamic dashboards per org (varies by edition)

// ─── SCHEDULED REPORT EMAIL FROM APEX ────────────────────────────────────────
public class ScheduledLoanReport implements Schedulable {
    public void execute(SchedulableContext ctx) {
        Reports.ReportResults r = Reports.ReportManager.runReport('00O...', true);
        Reports.ReportFactWithDetails fact =
            (Reports.ReportFactWithDetails) r.getFactMap().get('T!T');
        if(fact.getRows().size() == 0) return; // skip email if no data

        Messaging.SingleEmailMessage email = new Messaging.SingleEmailMessage();
        email.setToAddresses(new List<String>{'[email protected]'});
        email.setSubject('Daily Loan Pipeline — ' + Date.today().format());
        email.setHtmlBody('<p>' + fact.getRows().size() + ' active loans today.</p>');
        Messaging.sendEmail(new List<Messaging.SingleEmailMessage>{email});
    }
}
// Schedule: System.schedule('Daily Report', '0 0 7 * * ?', new ScheduledLoanReport());
Report Types — standard vs custom, joined reports, cross-filters?REPORTS MASTER▼

Custom Report Types (CRT) — define which objects and fields are available in a report. Necessary when standard report types don't include the fields or relationships you need.

  • Create CRT — Setup → Report Types → New. Define primary object, related objects, and which fields are available
  • One-to-many relationship — CRT can include parent + child in same report (Account with Loans)
  • Field availability — CRT controls which fields users see in the report builder — useful for hiding sensitive fields from non-admin report builders
  • Joined Reports — combine up to 5 report blocks with different report types. Each block is a separate dataset. Can show side-by-side comparisons (Loans by Status this quarter vs same quarter last year)
  • Cross-filters — filter a report based on related object criteria without showing the related object's fields. Example: Accounts WITH active Loans (without adding loan fields to the report)
// Access Reports via Apex Analytics API
Reports.ReportResults results = Reports.ReportManager.runReport('00O000000000001AAA', true); // true = detail rows
Reports.ReportMetadata meta = results.getReportMetadata();
Reports.ReportFactWithDetails facts = (Reports.ReportFactWithDetails) results.getFactMap().get('T!T');

for (Reports.ReportDetailRow row : facts.getRows()) {
  List<Reports.ReportDataCell> cells = row.getDataCells();
  String loanName   = (String) cells[0].getValue();
  Decimal amount    = (Decimal) cells[1].getValue();
}
Dynamic Dashboards and Dashboard Filters — how do they work?REPORTS MASTER▼
  • Dynamic Dashboards — show data as the viewing user (respects their sharing and visibility). Standard dashboards show data as the dashboard's running user (one fixed view for all).
  • When to use Dynamic — each user should see only their data (loan officers see their own loans). When to use Standard — executive dashboards where everyone needs the same org-wide view.
  • Dashboard Filters — add up to 3 filter options users can toggle without editing the dashboard. Example: filter by Branch, by Loan Type, by Date Range
  • Scheduled Reports — Setup → Report → Schedule. Sends report to email recipients on a schedule. Maximum 200 scheduled reports per org.
  • Analytics API — Reports.ReportManager.runReport() runs synchronously for <2,000 rows. Use Reports.ReportManager.runAsyncReport() for larger datasets.
Dashboard component limit

Each dashboard supports up to 20 components. For complex executive dashboards, use Analytics Studio (Einstein Analytics/CRM Analytics) which has no such limit and supports more chart types.

30-Day English Speaking Plan — Rewritten
Day-by-day structured exercises. Follow this during your 8:00 AM communication block (30 min) and 5:00 PM STAR practice block (1 hr) every single day.
WEEK 1 — DAYS 1–7: FOUNDATION (Voice, Pace, Filler Words)
Day 1Record your baseline — 2-minute self-introduction on videoSit, press record, introduce yourself as if in a real interview with NO preparation. Watch it completely. Write down: every filler word (um, uh, basically, right, like, you know), your pace (rushed or slow?), whether you had a clear beginning and end. Keep this recording — you will compare it on Day 30. This is your starting point, not a judgment of where you will be.
Day 2Read tech article aloud at 70% normal speedOpen Salesforce Developer Blog. Read one complete article out loud — every word — at intentionally slow pace. Record 3 minutes. Play back: could someone who speaks slowly understand every word? The sentences you rushed through most — repeat those 5 times slowly. Slow speech sounds like confidence. Fast speech sounds like nervousness.
Day 3Filler word elimination — ONE DAY CHALLENGEFrom Day 1 recording: identify your top 2 filler words. Today: every time you feel the urge to say that word — STOP, take one breath, then say the sentence without it. Do this in ALL conversations today, not just practice. Silence before a sentence is confidence — not weakness. Track how many times you catch yourself.
Day 4Explain governor limits to an imaginary non-technical personStand up. Pretend someone who has never coded is in front of you. Explain what governor limits are using a real-world analogy ONLY. No technical terms allowed. Try: "Imagine a restaurant that can only serve 100 customers per day..." Record 90 seconds. Play back. Did it make sense without ANY Salesforce knowledge? Try again until it does. This trains clarity of thinking.
Day 5Answer 3 questions recorded — watch — redo each immediatelyQuestions: "What is bulkification?" "What is a trigger handler?" "What is @wire?" Record each. Watch immediately after each one — not all three at end. For each: did you start directly with the answer? Did you give a real project example? Did you end cleanly without trailing off? Redo every answer once with improvements applied. 6 total recordings today.
Day 6The power pause drill — 10 questions, 3-second pause before eachAsk yourself 10 questions from this guide aloud. After EACH question — deliberately pause and count 3 full seconds before starting your answer. This feels very uncomfortable. That is correct. In a real interview this 3-second pause tells the interviewer: "This person thinks before they speak." Do this 10 times until it starts feeling normal.
Day 7Self-introduction × 5 with different energy levelsRecord your self-introduction 5 times consecutively. Version 1: completely flat and monotone. Version 2: your normal way. Version 3: confident and direct. Version 4: enthusiastic. Version 5: warm, natural, like talking to a colleague you respect. Watch all 5. Which sounds like someone you would want on your team? That energy is your target. Practice that version 3 more times.
WEEK 2 — DAYS 8–14: STRUCTURE (PREP Framework, STAR, Clean Endings)
Day 8Learn PREP framework — practice with 5 technical answersPREP = Point → Reason → Example → Point again. For "What is bulkification?" — POINT: "Bulkification means writing Apex that processes multiple records at once within governor limits." REASON: "Salesforce can pass 200 records to a trigger at once — SOQL inside a loop hits the 100-query limit." EXAMPLE: "In my mortgage trigger, I collect all Account IDs in a Set, query once outside the loop, process from a Map." POINT AGAIN: "Rule: never put SOQL or DML inside a for loop." Practice 5 different answers using this structure today.
Day 9Project bridge drill — connect EVERY answer to your projectTake 5 technical questions. Answer with PREP. Then FORCE yourself to end every single answer with: "...and I used this exact pattern in my Loan Officer Campaign Platform when building the OpenAI integration" or "...this came up specifically in the Mortgage Origination Platform with the Experian callout." Answers connected to your real work score 3x higher in interviews than textbook answers.
Day 10STAR method — 2 complete stories timedOpen Behavioral section. Pick 2 STAR stories. Read once. Close guide. Tell the complete story out loud from memory — all 4 parts: Situation, Task, Action, Result. Set stopwatch. Target: 2 to 2.5 minutes each. Under 90 seconds: your Situation and Action need more detail. Over 3 minutes: trim the Action section — it is too long. Result MUST contain a number or measurable outcome.
Day 11Self-introduction × 10 variations — own every versionSay your self-introduction 10 times today. Each time change ONE element: what you open with, which project you highlight, which skill you emphasize, what domains you mention, how you close. By attempt 10, the introduction is so thoroughly practiced it sounds completely natural — not memorized — because you have practiced every variation. This is how professional speakers prepare.
Day 12"I don't know" recovery framework — 5 practice scenariosPick 5 topics from this guide you are genuinely less confident about. For each, practice this structure aloud: "That is a good area — I have not worked with [topic] directly in production. However, based on my experience with [related thing I know well], I would expect this to work by [reasoning]. I would verify this in the documentation before implementing." Never stop at "I don't know." Always bridge to what you DO know.
Day 13Vocabulary: 3 words × 10 sentences each spoken aloudPick 3 words from the Vocabulary section. For each word: make 10 different sentences using it in a Salesforce or interview context. Say all 10 sentences aloud for each word. 30 total spoken sentences. By the end of the day these 3 words must feel completely natural in your speaking — not like vocabulary words you are trying to use, but like words you actually use.
Day 14Week 2 recording — compare to Day 1Record: 2-minute self-intro + answer to "What is a trigger handler pattern?" + one full STAR story. Watch all three recordings. Now immediately watch your Day 1 recording. Write 5 specific improvements you can see and hear. Write 3 things still to work on. Seeing tangible progress is psychologically important — do not skip this comparison step.
WEEK 3 — DAYS 15–21: DEPTH (Senior English, Tradeoffs, Technical Clarity)
Day 15"Yes, and..." upgrade — make 5 short answers senior-levelTake 5 simple yes/no questions. Practice upgrading each from junior to senior. Junior: "Yes, I use with sharing." Senior: "Yes, I always declare sharing explicitly. I use with sharing for service classes that run in user context, without sharing for batch jobs needing unrestricted access, and inherited sharing for utility classes that should adapt to their caller. Being explicit about sharing intent makes code immediately readable to any reviewer." Practice 5 upgrades today.
Day 16"It depends — here is how I decide" — tradeoff thinkingSenior developers never give one absolute answer to comparison questions. Pick 5 comparison questions (wire vs imperative, Future vs Queueable, Flow vs Trigger). For each, practice: "It depends on the specific context. Here is how I decide..." then give a clear decision framework. An interviewer hearing "it depends + clear reasoning" gives you senior credit. "Always use X" without nuance suggests limited experience.
Day 17Architecture whiteboard explanation — 10 full minutes aloudTake paper. Draw the Mortgage Origination Platform architecture: objects, LWC components, integrations (Experian, DocuSign, OFAC, Platform Events, LOS sync). While drawing, explain every component aloud — what it is, why it exists, what it connects to, why you designed it that way. Do not stop. 10 full minutes of continuous spoken explanation. This is exactly what "walk me through your architecture" means in senior final rounds.
Day 1890-second timer drill — answer under time pressurePick 5 complex scenario questions. Set a phone timer for 90 seconds. Start answering. Stop when timer beeps — even mid-sentence. Play back: did you lead with the most important point? Did you get to an example? This trains you to front-load your highest-value information — critical when an interviewer interrupts or redirects you mid-answer.
Day 19Confidence phrase replacement — start answers professionallyToday start EVERY answer with one of these (rotate through them): "In my experience building mortgage systems..." / "What I have found in production is..." / "The approach I take is..." / "Let me give you a concrete example from my project..." Record 5 answers with these openers. Compare to answers starting with "So basically..." The difference in professional authority is immediately audible — even to yourself.
Day 20Handle challenges gracefully — 5 difficult scenariosPractice aloud: A) "Your answer was vague — be more specific." Respond: "You are right — let me be more precise: [add code, number, or project detail]." B) "That approach seems overcomplicated." Respond: "That is fair — the simpler approach would be X, but the tradeoff is Y. For our use case, the complexity was justified because..." C) "I disagree with that design." Respond: "I appreciate that perspective. Could you tell me what concern you have? That would help me address it specifically." Practice each 5 times.
Day 21Full 30-minute mock interview — Week 3 checkpointSet a 30-minute timer. Ask yourself 8 questions from different sections. For each: power pause → PREP structure → project connection → clean ending. Record all 30 minutes. Watch completely. Score yourself 1–5 on each: pace, filler words, structure, project examples, confidence, clean endings. Total target by Week 3: average 4.0 or higher on all dimensions.
WEEK 4 — DAYS 22–30: POLISH (Interview-Ready Performance)
Day 22Active listening drill — confirm before answeringFor every question today: before answering, say "Just to confirm — you are asking about [X] in the context of [Y]? Good. So..." Then answer. This demonstrates that you listened carefully, think before speaking, and answer the actual question not a related one you assumed. Practice with 10 questions. Most candidates skip this — it immediately signals senior communication maturity.
Day 23Professional closing — practice 5 times until completely naturalPractice this exact closing 5 times until it sounds like your own words: "Thank you — I genuinely enjoyed this conversation. Learning about [specific technical challenge or project they mentioned] has reinforced my excitement about this role. I have one question: based on what you have heard today, do you have any concerns about my fit that I can address? And what are the next steps?" The "concerns" question separates the most confident candidates from everyone else.
Day 24STAR story marathon — all 6 stories back to back from memoryTell ALL 6 STAR stories from the Behavioral section consecutively — no guide, no notes, from memory only. Each one 2–2.5 minutes. Total time approximately 15 minutes. Then pick the 2 that sounded weakest. Redo those 2 stories 3 more times each until they sound as strong as your best story. By Day 30 every story must be equally strong and natural.
Day 25Mortgage domain vocabulary in English — 5 concepts explained clearlyFor each of these terms: DTI, LTV, TRID, ECOA, OFAC — explain in clear confident English sentences: what it means, why it matters for mortgage lending, and how your Salesforce system handled it. Record 5 explanations. A domain-specialist interviewer at a mortgage company will ask about these — your domain knowledge must sound as natural as your Salesforce knowledge.
Day 26Weakness audit — targeted drilling on YOUR specific weak spotsReview your last 5 recordings. Identify the 3 weakest specific moments — a specific answer that still rambles, a specific technical term you still stumble over, a specific question type that still makes you rush. Spend today's ENTIRE communication practice on ONLY those 3 things. Targeted drilling on specific weaknesses is 10x more effective than general review at this stage.
Day 27Mirror practice — body language and voice togetherStand in front of a full-length mirror or phone camera facing you. Answer 5 questions while watching yourself. Notice: eye contact with yourself (practice looking at camera not down at notes), facial expression (engaged and warm, not flat or anxious), shoulder position (relaxed not raised with tension), and hand gestures (natural, supporting your words). Body language directly affects how your voice sounds. Relaxed body = more confident voice.
Day 28Speed variation — same answer at 3 different pacesPick one complex answer (your trigger handler explanation). Record it: Version 1 at your natural nervous speed. Version 2 at 20% slower. Version 3 at 40% slower than natural. Play all three back. Version 2 or 3 will sound most confident, clear, and authoritative. Version 1 will sound rushed. Train yourself to default to version 2 pace in all interviews.
Day 29Full dress rehearsal — 60 minutes, complete interview simulationSit at your desk. Dress appropriately — psychologically primes your brain for interview performance. Do the full 60-minute Mock Interview 3 from this guide. Record completely. Watch all of it without stopping. Write your honest assessment: what would make an interviewer hire you based on this recording, and what concerns would they still have. Fix those concerns — you have one day left.
Day 30Day 30 recording — compare to Day 1 — your transformationRecord the exact same scenario from Day 1: 2-minute self-intro + 3 technical Q&A answers. Watch this recording. Now immediately watch your Day 1 recording. The differences will be visible and audible: pace, clarity, structure, confidence, filler words. Write what you observe. This is 30 days of daily practice made visible and real. You are ready.
50 Sentence Starters for Technical Interviews
Use 5 different starters each day. Read them aloud every morning. By Day 30 they will feel completely natural — not rehearsed.
Starting a Technical Answer
  • "The way I think about this is..."
  • "In my experience building mortgage systems, what I have found is..."
  • "Let me walk you through how this works in practice..."
  • "The key distinction here is..."
  • "To answer directly: [answer]. The reason is..."
  • "There are two parts to this. First..."
  • "This is something I have worked with closely — let me be specific..."
  • "The short answer is [X]. Let me explain the reasoning..."
  • "In production code, the pattern I use is..."
  • "Let me give you a concrete example from my project..."
Explaining a Tradeoff
  • "It depends on the specific situation. Here is how I decide..."
  • "Both approaches work, but the tradeoff is..."
  • "I would choose [X] when [condition], and [Y] when [other condition]..."
  • "The advantage of [X] is [A], but the cost is [B]..."
  • "In theory [X] is simpler, but in production what I have seen is..."
  • "If performance is the priority, then [X]. If maintainability is the priority, then [Y]."
  • "My preference is [X] because [technical reason], though [Y] works well when..."
  • "The answer depends on your data volume. Below [N] records, [X] works fine. Above that..."
  • "From an architecture standpoint, I would weigh..."
  • "I have used both in production. The difference I noticed in real usage was..."
Connecting to Your Project
  • "I used this exact pattern in my Mortgage Origination Platform when..."
  • "This came up specifically when I was building the Experian integration..."
  • "A real example from my work: when I built the Loan Officer Campaign Platform..."
  • "In our five-person team project, I was responsible for this part..."
  • "The first time I encountered this in production was..."
  • "I built this from scratch in my solo project — let me walk you through my decisions..."
  • "This is something I dealt with in the DocuSign integration specifically..."
  • "We had a similar challenge with OFAC screening, where..."
When You Need a Moment to Think
  • "That is a good scenario — let me think through the approach..."
  • "Give me just a moment — I want to make sure I cover the most important parts..."
  • "There are a few ways to approach this — let me think which fits best..."
  • "Just to confirm — you are asking about [X] in the context of [Y]? Good, so..."
  • "Let me think through this the way I would in a real design session..."
  • "I want to give you a precise answer rather than a quick one..."
Ending an Answer Strongly
  • "...That is the core principle, and it is something I apply in every trigger I write."
  • "...The result was [measurable outcome]. That approach has served us well."
  • "...Does that answer your question, or would you like me to go deeper on any part?"
  • "...That is how I approach it — I can show you the actual code if useful."
  • "...That is my experience with this specifically in the US mortgage domain."
  • "...In summary: [one sentence]. That is the decision I would make."
Handling a Difficult Question
  • "I have not used that specific feature directly, but based on [related concept]..."
  • "That is a fair challenge — let me address it directly..."
  • "You raise a good point. The concern would be [X], and I would address it by [Y]..."
  • "I want to be honest: I have more experience with [similar thing]. Let me reason through it..."
  • "That is a scenario I would want to test in sandbox first, but my initial thinking is..."
  • "I appreciate the question — here is what I know and where I would verify further..."
Handling Difficult Interview Situations — 30 Scripts
Practice these aloud until they feel like your own natural words. These are for the moments when you are surprised, challenged, or unsure.
When You Do Not Know the Answer
  • "I have not worked with that specific feature in production. Let me reason through it: based on how [related concept] works, I would expect this to behave like [reasoning]. I would verify this in the documentation before implementing."
  • "Honestly, that is beyond what I have implemented directly. My experience is stronger in [related area]. Could you share more context? That would help me give you a more useful answer."
  • "I want to give you an accurate answer rather than guess. My understanding is [what I know]. The part I am less certain about is [specific gap]. How does your current team handle this?"
When the Interviewer Challenges Your Answer
  • "That is a fair point — I may have oversimplified. What I should add is [specific detail]..."
  • "You are right to push on that. The concern with my approach would be [acknowledge their point]. The reason I still chose it was [specific context from my project]."
  • "I see what you mean. For larger scale than I was dealing with, I would adjust by [modification]. Does that address your concern?"
  • "That is a good counterpoint. I would want to test that assumption — what has your team found in that scenario?"
When Asked About Salary
  • "Before I give a number, could you share the budgeted range? I want to make sure we are aligned before either of us invests more time."
  • "Based on my research into Senior Salesforce Developer rates for professionals with US mortgage domain experience in the Pune market, I am targeting [range]. I am flexible depending on the full package and growth opportunity."
  • "I would rather not anchor a number before understanding the full scope. Can you share what range the team is working with?"
When Clarifying a Vague Question
  • "Before I answer — are you asking about [Scenario A] or [Scenario B]? The approach differs significantly."
  • "When you say [term they used], do you mean [definition A] or [definition B]? I want to make sure I answer what you are actually asking."
  • "Could you give me a bit more context about the system you are describing? That would help me give a more specific answer."
  • "Is this a theoretical design question, or are you describing a real scenario you are trying to solve? I can go much deeper if there is a real problem behind it."
Closing the Interview
  • "Thank you — I genuinely enjoyed this conversation. The [specific thing they mentioned] really resonated with me — it maps closely to what I built in [your project]."
  • "I have one important question: based on what you have heard from me today, do you have any concerns about my fit for this role? I would rather address them now."
  • "What are the next steps and roughly what timeline are you working with?"
  • "Is there anything specific you would like me to prepare or demonstrate for the next round?"
English Confidence Reminders
  • Before any practice: say aloud — "I know this material. I have built these systems. I am ready." This changes your voice quality physiologically.
  • When you make a grammar mistake: keep going, do not apologize, do not restart. Interviewers focus on content and confidence — not grammar perfection.
  • When nervous: take one slow breath, look at the interviewer or camera, then start speaking at 70% of your normal speed. Slow IS confident.
  • When you trail off: say "Let me put that more clearly:" and restate the key point in one clean, direct sentence. Recovery from trailing off is itself a sign of maturity.
NavigationMixin — 10 Scenario Questions
Complete navigation patterns for LWC — record pages, new records, list views, external URLs, state passing
How do you import and use NavigationMixin in LWC — what is the basic pattern?NAVMIXIN▼
import { LightningElement, api } from 'lwc';
import { NavigationMixin } from 'lightning/navigation';

// ALWAYS extend NavigationMixin(LightningElement)
export default class MyNavComp extends NavigationMixin(LightningElement) {
    @api recordId;

    // Navigate to the current record's view page
    handleViewRecord() {
        this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
            type: 'standard__recordPage',
            attributes: {
                recordId: this.recordId,
                actionName: 'view'   // 'view', 'edit', 'clone'
            }
        });
    }

    // Generate a URL without navigating (for links, sharing)
    async handleGetUrl() {
        const url = await this[NavigationMixin.GenerateUrl]({
            type: 'standard__recordPage',
            attributes: { recordId: this.recordId, actionName: 'view' }
        });
        // url = '/lightning/r/Loan__c/001xxx/view'
        const fullUrl = window.location.origin + url;
        navigator.clipboard.writeText(fullUrl);
    }
}
How do you navigate to a New Record form with pre-populated default field values?NAVMIXIN▼
import { encodeDefaultFieldValues } from 'lightning/pageReferenceUtils';

handleCreateLoan() {
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
        type: 'standard__objectPage',
        attributes: {
            objectApiName: 'Loan__c',
            actionName: 'new'
        },
        state: {
            defaultFieldValues: encodeDefaultFieldValues({
                Application__c: this.applicationId,  // parent lookup
                LoanType__c: 'FHA',                   // picklist
                LoanAmount__c: 350000                 // number
            })
        }
    });
}

// List View
handleViewAllLoans() {

        type: 'standard__objectPage',
        attributes: { objectApiName: 'Loan__c', actionName: 'list' },
        state: { filterName: 'All' }  // 'All' or DeveloperName of list view
    });

// Home page

        type: 'standard__namedPage',
        attributes: { pageName: 'home' }
    });

handleOpenFredAPI() {
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
        type: 'standard__webPage',
        attributes: { url: 'https://fred.stlouisfed.org/series/MORTGAGE30US' }
    });
}

// External URL — open in NEW tab
async handleOpenNewTab() {
    const url = await this[NavigationMixin.GenerateUrl]({
        type: 'standard__webPage',
        attributes: { url: 'https://fred.stlouisfed.org' }
    });
    window.open(url, '_blank');
}

// Custom nav item / tab
handleGoToDashboard() {
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
        type: 'standard__navItemPage',
        attributes: { apiName: 'Loan_Dashboard' }
    });
}
How do you pass state/parameters between pages using NavigationMixin and CurrentPageReference?NAVMIXIN▼
// PUBLISHER — navigate with state params
handleNavigateWithState() {
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
        type: 'standard__component',
        attributes: { componentName: 'c__loanDetailPage' },
        state: {
            loanId: this.loanId,
            mode: 'review',
            sourceApp: 'pipeline'
        }
    });
}

// RECEIVER — read state from CurrentPageReference
import { CurrentPageReference } from 'lightning/navigation';

@wire(CurrentPageReference)
pageRef(ref) {
    if (ref) {
        this.loanId = ref.state?.loanId;
        this.mode = ref.state?.mode;
        this.sourceApp = ref.state?.sourceApp;
    }
}
State vs Attributes

state becomes query parameters in the URL (visible, bookmarkable). attributes is part of the route structure. Use state for optional context data, attributes for required routing parameters like recordId.

How do you navigate to a related record from a parent record page — get the related record ID first?NAVMIXIN▼
import { LightningElement, api, wire } from 'lwc';
import { NavigationMixin } from 'lightning/navigation';
import { getRecord, getFieldValue } from 'lightning/uiRecordApi';
import APPLICATION_FIELD from '@salesforce/schema/Loan__c.Application__c';
import APPLICATION_NAME from '@salesforce/schema/Loan__c.Application__r.Name';

export default class LoanParentNav extends NavigationMixin(LightningElement) {
    @api recordId;
    applicationId;

    @wire(getRecord, { recordId: '$recordId', fields: [APPLICATION_FIELD, APPLICATION_NAME] })
    wiredLoan({ data }) {
        if (data) {
            this.applicationId = getFieldValue(data, APPLICATION_FIELD);
        }
    }

    handleViewApplication() {
        if (!this.applicationId) return;
        this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
            type: 'standard__recordPage',
            attributes: {
                recordId: this.applicationId,
                objectApiName: 'Application__c',
                actionName: 'view'
            }
        });
    }
}
