How do you create a shareable link to a record and copy it to clipboard?NAVMIXIN▼
import { LightningElement, api } from 'lwc';
import { NavigationMixin } from 'lightning/navigation';
import { ShowToastEvent } from 'lightning/platformShowToastEvent';

export default class ShareLoanLink extends NavigationMixin(LightningElement) {
    @api recordId;
    shareableUrl = '';

    async connectedCallback() {
        try {
            const relativeUrl = await this[NavigationMixin.GenerateUrl]({
                type: 'standard__recordPage',
                attributes: { recordId: this.recordId, actionName: 'view' }
            });
            // GenerateUrl returns relative path — prepend origin for absolute URL
            this.shareableUrl = window.location.origin + relativeUrl;
        } catch(e) {
            console.error('URL generation failed:', e);
        }
    }

    handleCopyLink() {
        navigator.clipboard.writeText(this.shareableUrl).then(() => {
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Link Copied',
                message: 'Loan page link copied to clipboard',
                variant: 'success'
            }));
        });
    }
}
What happens when NavigationMixin.Navigate is called on a component not in Lightning Experience — how do you handle it?NAVMIXIN▼

NavigationMixin works in Lightning Experience, Salesforce Mobile App, and Experience Cloud sites. It does NOT work in Visualforce pages, standalone apps outside the Salesforce container, or in Jest tests without mocking.

// Guard navigation with a try-catch
handleNavigate() {
    try {
        this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
            type: 'standard__recordPage',
            attributes: { recordId: this.recordId, actionName: 'view' }
        });
    } catch(e) {
        // Fallback for non-Lightning contexts
        window.location.href = '/lightning/r/Loan__c/' + this.recordId + '/view';
    }
}

// In Jest tests — mock NavigationMixin
// jest.config.js moduleNameMapper:
// '@salesforce/schema': '/__mocks__/sfSchema.js'
// 'lightning/navigation': '/__mocks__/navigation.js'

// __mocks__/navigation.js:
const NavigationMixin = (Base) => {
    class NavigationMixinClass extends Base {
        navigate = jest.fn();
        [Symbol.hasInstance](instance) { return instance instanceof NavigationMixinClass; }
    }
    NavigationMixinClass.Navigate = Symbol('Navigate');
    NavigationMixinClass.GenerateUrl = Symbol('GenerateUrl');
    return NavigationMixinClass;
};
export { NavigationMixin };
How do you track page navigation in LWC — react when the user navigates to a different record?NAVMIXIN▼
// CurrentPageReference wire fires every time the page URL changes
import { CurrentPageReference } from 'lightning/navigation';

@wire(CurrentPageReference)
pageRef(newRef) {
    if (!newRef) return;
    const newRecordId = newRef.attributes?.recordId;
    if (newRecordId && newRecordId !== this.currentRecordId) {
        this.currentRecordId = newRecordId;
        this.handleRecordChange(newRecordId);
    }
}

handleRecordChange(recordId) {
    // Reload data for the new record
    this.isLoading = true;
    getLoanData({ loanId: recordId })
        .then(data => { this.loanData = data; })
        .catch(err => { this.error = err.body?.message; })
        .finally(() => { this.isLoading = false; });
}

// PageReference object structure:
// {
//   type: 'standard__recordPage',
//   attributes: { recordId: '001...', objectApiName: 'Loan__c', actionName: 'view' },
//   state: {} // query params
// }
How do you navigate programmatically after a successful record save in LWC?NAVMIXIN▼
import { LightningElement, api } from 'lwc';
import { NavigationMixin } from 'lightning/navigation';
import { createRecord } from 'lightning/uiRecordApi';
import { ShowToastEvent } from 'lightning/platformShowToastEvent';
import LOAN_OBJECT from '@salesforce/schema/Loan__c';
import LOAN_AMOUNT from '@salesforce/schema/Loan__c.LoanAmount__c';

export default class LoanCreator extends NavigationMixin(LightningElement) {
    @api applicationId;

    async handleSave() {
        try {
            const fields = {
                [LOAN_AMOUNT.fieldApiName]: this.loanAmount,
                'Application__c': this.applicationId
            };
            const newRecord = await createRecord({ apiName: LOAN_OBJECT.objectApiName, fields });

            // Show success toast
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Loan Created', variant: 'success',
                message: 'Loan ' + newRecord.id + ' created successfully'
            }));

            // Navigate to the new record immediately after creation
            this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
                type: 'standard__recordPage',
                attributes: {
                    recordId: newRecord.id,
                    objectApiName: 'Loan__c',
                    actionName: 'view'
                }
            });
        } catch(e) {
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Save Failed', message: e.body?.message, variant: 'error'
            }));
        }
    }
}
Validation — UI and Backend Scenarios
10 scenarios enforcing data quality from LWC form to Apex trigger to database — complete end-to-end
How do you validate a custom LWC form with multiple lightning-input fields before calling Apex?VALIDATION▼
// loanApplicationForm.js
import { LightningElement, track } from 'lwc';
import { ShowToastEvent } from 'lightning/platformShowToastEvent';
import saveLoanApplication from '@salesforce/apex/LoanController.saveLoanApplication';

export default class LoanApplicationForm extends LightningElement {
    @track formData = { loanAmount: '', loanType: '', borrowerName: '', fico: '' };

    handleFieldChange(event) {
        const field = event.target.dataset.field;
        this.formData = { ...this.formData, [field]: event.target.value };
    }

    handleSubmit() {
        // Step 1: Trigger built-in lightning-input validation
        const allInputs = this.template.querySelectorAll('lightning-input, lightning-combobox');
        let isValid = [...allInputs].every(input => {
            const valid = input.checkValidity();
            if (!valid) input.reportValidity();  // shows error UI on that field
            return valid;
        });

        // Step 2: Custom cross-field business rules
        if (isValid) {
            if (parseInt(this.formData.fico) < 500) {
                // Set error on specific field
                const ficoInput = this.template.querySelector('[data-field="fico"]');
                ficoInput.setCustomValidity('FICO score must be at least 500.');
                ficoInput.reportValidity();
                isValid = false;
            }
            if (parseFloat(this.formData.loanAmount) > 2000000 && this.formData.loanType === 'FHA') {
                this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                    title: 'Validation Error',
                    message: 'FHA loans cannot exceed $2,000,000.',
                    variant: 'error'
                }));
                isValid = false;
            }
        }

        if (!isValid) return;  // stop — do not call Apex

        // Step 3: Call Apex only when client validation passes
        this.saveForm();
    }

    async saveForm() {
        try {
            const result = await saveLoanApplication({ data: JSON.stringify(this.formData) });
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Saved', message: 'Application ID: ' + result.Id, variant: 'success'
            }));
        } catch (e) {
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Save Failed', message: e.body?.message, variant: 'error'
            }));
        }
    }
}
How does trigger addError() surface to LWC — show the complete flow from trigger to UI toast?VALIDATION▼
// APEX TRIGGER — addError prevents DML and returns error to caller
trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (before insert, before update) {
    for(Loan__c loan : Trigger.new) {
        if(loan.LoanAmount__c > 2000000 && loan.LoanType__c == 'FHA') {
            // Field-level error — highlights the LoanAmount field in red
            loan.LoanAmount__c.addError('FHA loans cannot exceed $2,000,000.');
        }
        if(loan.Status__c == 'Approved' && loan.FicoScore__c < 620) {
            // Record-level error — shows as banner at top of form
            loan.addError('Cannot approve loan with FICO score below 620.');
        }
    }
}

// LWC — updateRecord catches addError() automatically
async handleSaveLoan() {
    try {
        await updateRecord({ fields: { Id: this.recordId, LoanAmount__c: this.amount } });
        this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({ title: 'Saved', variant: 'success' }));
    } catch (error) {
        // error.body.output.fieldErrors — field-level errors keyed by field API name
        // error.body.output.errors — record-level errors array
        // error.body.message — overall error message
        const msg = error.body?.output?.errors?.[0]?.message
                 || error.body?.message
                 || 'Save failed';
        this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
            title: 'Validation Failed', message: msg, variant: 'error', mode: 'sticky'
        }));
    }
}

// With lightning-record-edit-form — addError() errors show AUTOMATICALLY
// Field errors highlight the specific field
// Record errors appear in lightning-messages component
// No extra error handling code needed for trigger validation!
Validation Rule vs Apex before trigger — which runs first and when to use each?VALIDATION▼
FeatureValidation RuleApex Before Trigger
Runs on ALL DML (API, UI, Data Loader)YesYes
Can query other objectsNo (formula only)Yes
Admin-maintainableYes — no deploymentNo — code deploy needed
Complex logicLimited (formula)Full Apex power
Execution orderAfter before triggersBefore validation rules
Can bypassYes (custom bypass field)Only with explicit Apex bypass
Execution order

Full Salesforce save order: System validation → Before triggers → Custom validation rules → Duplicate rules → After triggers → Workflow rules → Processes → Flows. Apex before trigger runs BEFORE validation rules — so if your trigger throws an error, validation rules never run for that record.

How do you prevent duplicate records using an Apex trigger — complete bulkified code?VALIDATION▼
trigger ContactDuplicateTrigger on Contact (before insert, before update) {

    // Step 1: Collect emails from new/updated records
    Set<String> emails = new Set<String>();
    for(Contact c : Trigger.new) {
        if(String.isNotBlank(c.Email)) emails.add(c.Email.toLowerCase());
    }
    if(emails.isEmpty()) return;

    // Step 2: One SOQL query outside the loop
    Map<String, Contact> existingByEmail = new Map<String, Contact>();
    for(Contact c : [SELECT Id, Email, FirstName, LastName FROM Contact
                     WHERE Email IN :emails]) {
        existingByEmail.put(c.Email.toLowerCase(), c);
    }

    // Step 3: Flag duplicates
    for(Contact c : Trigger.new) {
        if(String.isBlank(c.Email)) continue;
        Contact existing = existingByEmail.get(c.Email.toLowerCase());
        if(existing == null) continue;
        // For update: skip if it is the same record being updated
        if(Trigger.isUpdate && existing.Id == c.Id) continue;
        // Field-level error — highlights Email field in the UI
        c.Email.addError(
            'Duplicate: a Contact with this email already exists — '
            + existing.FirstName + ' ' + existing.LastName
        );
    }
}
How do you validate file uploads in LWC — restrict type and size before sending to server?VALIDATION▼
const MAX_SIZE = 10 * 1024 * 1024;  // 10 MB in bytes
const ALLOWED_EXTS = ['.pdf', '.jpg', '.jpeg', '.png'];

export default class FileValidator extends LightningElement {
    @api recordId;
    selectedFile = null;
    isValid = false;
    fileError = '';

    handleFileChange(event) {
        const file = event.target.files[0];
        if (!file) return;
        this.selectedFile = file;
        this.fileError = '';
        this.isValid = false;

        // Check extension
        const ext = '.' + file.name.split('.').pop().toLowerCase();
        if (!ALLOWED_EXTS.includes(ext)) {
            this.fileError = 'Only PDF, JPG, and PNG files are allowed.';
            return;
        }

        // Check size
        if (file.size > MAX_SIZE) {
            this.fileError = `File is ${(file.size/1024/1024).toFixed(1)}MB — maximum is 10MB.`;
            return;
        }

        this.isValid = true;
    }

    async handleUpload() {
        if (!this.isValid || !this.selectedFile) return;
        // Read as base64 for Apex
        const base64 = await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
            const reader = new FileReader();
            reader.onload = () => resolve(reader.result.split(',')[1]);
            reader.onerror = reject;
            reader.readAsDataURL(this.selectedFile);
        });
        // Pass base64, fileName, recordId to Apex
    }
}
How does lightning-record-edit-form handle validation automatically — show onsubmit, onsuccess, onerror pattern?VALIDATION▼
<!-- loanEditForm.html -->
<lightning-record-edit-form
    record-id={recordId}
    object-api-name="Loan__c"
    onsuccess={handleSuccess}
    onerror={handleError}
    onsubmit={handleSubmit}>

    <!-- Validation rule + trigger addError() messages auto-appear here -->
    <lightning-messages></lightning-messages>

    <!-- Field errors appear on each field automatically -->
    <lightning-input-field field-name="LoanAmount__c"></lightning-input-field>
    <lightning-input-field field-name="LoanType__c"></lightning-input-field>
    <lightning-button type="submit" label="Save"></lightning-button>
</lightning-record-edit-form>

// JS handlers:
handleSubmit(event) {
    event.preventDefault();  // stop default submit for custom pre-check
    const fields = event.detail.fields;

    // Custom pre-submit check
    if (parseFloat(fields.LoanAmount__c) < 50000) {
        this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
            title: 'Error', message: 'Minimum loan amount is $50,000', variant: 'error'
        }));
        return;  // do NOT submit
    }
    // Proceed with submit
    this.template.querySelector('lightning-record-edit-form').submit(fields);
}

handleSuccess(event) {
    const savedRecord = event.detail;
    this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({ title: 'Saved', variant: 'success' }));
}

handleError(event) {
    // Trigger addError() and Validation Rules auto-show on fields via lightning-messages
    // This handler catches SYSTEM errors (permissions, network, etc.)
    console.error('System error:', event.detail);
}
How do you handle Database.SaveResult errors in Apex and return them clearly to LWC?VALIDATION▼
// Apex — partial DML with error collection
@AuraEnabled
public static Map<String,Object> bulkSaveLoans(List<Loan__c> loans) {
    List<Database.SaveResult> results = Database.insert(loans, false); // partial mode
    List<Map<String,String>> errors = new List<Map<String,String>>();
    List<String> successIds = new List<String>();

    for(Integer i = 0; i < results.size(); i++) {
        if(results[i].isSuccess()) {
            successIds.add(results[i].getId());
        } else {
            for(Database.Error err : results[i].getErrors()) {
                errors.add(new Map<String,String>{
                    'record' => loans[i].Name,
                    'statusCode' => err.getStatusCode().name(),
                    'message' => err.getMessage(),
                    'fields' => String.join(err.getFields(), ', ')
                });
            }
        }
    }
    return new Map<String,Object>{
        'successCount' => successIds.size(),
        'errorCount' => errors.size(),
        'errors' => errors
    };
}

// LWC — display per-record errors
async handleBulkSave() {
    const result = await bulkSaveLoans({ loans: this.loanList });
    if (result.errorCount > 0) {
        const errMessages = result.errors.map(e =>
            `${e.record}: ${e.message} (fields: ${e.fields})`
        ).join('\n');
        this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
            title: `${result.successCount} saved, ${result.errorCount} failed`,
            message: errMessages,
            variant: 'warning', mode: 'sticky'
        }));
    } else {
        this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
            title: 'All Saved', message: result.successCount + ' loans saved', variant: 'success'
        }));
    }
}
How do you enforce FCRA compliance validation in Apex — credit pull requires signed authorization?VALIDATION▼
// FCRA Compliance — enforce in Apex trigger (cannot be bypassed by API/integrations)
trigger LoanFCRAComplianceTrigger on Loan__c (before insert, before update) {
    for(Loan__c loan : Trigger.new) {

        // Rule: Credit pull can ONLY happen if authorization date is set
        if(loan.CreditPullRequested__c == true) {
            // On update — check if CreditPullRequested just changed to true
            Boolean isNewRequest = Trigger.isInsert ||
                (Trigger.isUpdate && !Trigger.oldMap.get(loan.Id).CreditPullRequested__c);

            if(isNewRequest && loan.CreditAuthorizationDate__c == null) {
                loan.CreditPullRequested__c.addError(
                    'FCRA Violation: Written credit authorization must be obtained ' +
                    'and the authorization date recorded before initiating a credit pull. ' +
                    'Upload the signed authorization form and set the Credit Authorization Date.'
                );
            }
        }

        // Rule: Authorization date cannot be in the future
        if(loan.CreditAuthorizationDate__c != null &&
           loan.CreditAuthorizationDate__c > Date.today()) {
            loan.CreditAuthorizationDate__c.addError(
                'Credit authorization date cannot be a future date.'
            );
        }

        // Rule: Funding date cannot precede closing date (TRID compliance)
        if(loan.FundingDate__c != null && loan.ClosingDate__c != null) {
            if(loan.FundingDate__c < loan.ClosingDate__c) {
                loan.addError(
                    'TRID Violation: Funding date cannot be before the closing date. ' +
                    'Current funding: ' + loan.FundingDate__c.format() +
                    ' | Closing: ' + loan.ClosingDate__c.format()
                );
            }
        }
    }
}
How do you perform server-side validation in an @AuraEnabled method and return structured errors to LWC?VALIDATION▼
// Apex — throw AuraHandledException with structured message
@AuraEnabled
public static String submitLoanApplication(String loanDataJson) {
    // Deserialize and validate
    Map<String,Object> loanData = (Map<String,Object>) JSON.deserializeUntyped(loanDataJson);
    Decimal amount = (Decimal) loanData.get('loanAmount');
    String loanType = (String) loanData.get('loanType');

    // Server-side business rules (cannot be bypassed by client-side manipulation)
    if(amount == null || amount < 50000) {
        throw new AuraHandledException('Minimum loan amount is $50,000. Provided: $' + amount);
    }
    if(loanType == 'FHA' && amount > 1089300) {
        throw new AuraHandledException(
            'FHA loan limit for this area is $1,089,300. ' +
            'Consider Jumbo or Conventional for amounts above this limit.'
        );
    }

    // Check OFAC list (cannot be done client-side)
    if(OFACScreeningService.isFlagged((String)loanData.get('ssn'))) {
        throw new AuraHandledException(
            'OFAC screening match found. This application requires manual review. ' +
            'Please contact your compliance officer immediately.'
        );
    }

    // All validation passed — proceed with DML
    Loan__c loan = new Loan__c(
        LoanAmount__c = amount, LoanType__c = loanType, Status__c = 'Application'
    );
    insert loan;
    return loan.Id;
}

// LWC — catch AuraHandledException
async handleSubmitApplication() {
    try {
        const loanId = await submitLoanApplication({ loanDataJson: JSON.stringify(this.formData) });
        this.navigateToRecord(loanId);
    } catch (error) {
        // AuraHandledException message is in error.body.message
        this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
            title: 'Application Failed',
            message: error.body?.message || 'Unexpected error',
            variant: 'error',
            mode: 'sticky'
        }));
    }
}
What is the difference between AuraHandledException and a regular Exception thrown from @AuraEnabled?VALIDATION▼

AuraHandledException: wraps a custom error message that is safely returned to the LWC caller. The message you set is what appears in error.body.message. Use this for expected business rule failures you want to show to the user.

Regular Exception (DmlException, QueryException, etc.): when thrown from an @AuraEnabled method, Salesforce wraps it in a standard error response. The original exception message appears in error.body.message. Stack trace is in error.body.stackTrace. These typically indicate programming errors or unexpected failures.

// AuraHandledException — user-friendly message, no stack trace exposed
throw new AuraHandledException('Loan amount exceeds the maximum for this loan type.');
// error.body.message = 'Loan amount exceeds the maximum for this loan type.'

// Regular exception — technical message, may expose internal details
throw new DmlException('Insert failed — required field missing');
// error.body.message = 'Insert failed...' (DML error message)
// error.body.stackTrace = full stack trace (security concern in prod!)

// Best practice for @AuraEnabled methods:
@AuraEnabled
public static String processLoan(Id loanId) {
    try {
        // business logic
        return 'success';
    } catch(LoanProcessingException e) {
        // Known business rule failure — wrap in AuraHandledException
        throw new AuraHandledException(e.getMessage());
    } catch(Exception e) {
        // Unexpected error — log it, return generic message to user
        System.debug(LoggingLevel.ERROR, 'Unexpected: ' + e.getMessage() + '\n' + e.getStackTraceString());
        throw new AuraHandledException('An unexpected error occurred. Please contact your administrator.');
    }
}
Async Processing + Credit Pull — End-to-End Scenarios
10 scenarios implementing the complete credit pull flow from button click to external API to toast notification
Explain the complete architecture of the credit pull flow — LWC → Apex → Queueable → API → Platform Event → LWC updateASYNC FLOW▼

The 6-stage credit pull architecture:

  • Stage 1 — User action: User clicks "Pull Credit" button in LWC on the Loan record page
  • Stage 2 — Apex controller: LWC calls imperative Apex method. Apex validates FCRA authorization, updates Loan status to "In Progress", enqueues a Queueable job, returns job ID immediately
  • Stage 3 — Queueable runs async: Job calls Experian API (callout), saves FICO score to Loan__c, publishes a Credit_Pull_Complete__e Platform Event
  • Stage 4 — Platform Event fires: A trigger subscribes to Credit_Pull_Complete__e and processes the result — can update related records, create tasks, etc.
  • Stage 5 — LWC subscribed via LMS: LWC was subscribed to the Platform Event message channel since connectedCallback — receives the notification
  • Stage 6 — UI updates: LWC refreshes record data with refreshApex, shows success or error toast with FICO score and decision
Why this architecture

Callouts cannot happen in the same transaction as trigger DML (callout after uncommitted DML error). The Apex controller returns immediately (no timeout). The Queueable runs after the transaction commits. The Platform Event bridges the async job back to the UI without polling. This is "Fire and Forget with Event-Driven Notification" — the correct pattern for long-running operations in Salesforce.

Show complete LWC code for the credit pull button — spinner, toast, Platform Event subscriptionASYNC FLOW▼
// creditPullButton.js
import { LightningElement, api, wire } from 'lwc';
import { ShowToastEvent } from 'lightning/platformShowToastEvent';
import { subscribe, unsubscribe, APPLICATION_SCOPE, MessageContext } from 'lightning/messageService';
import { refreshApex } from '@salesforce/apex';
import initiateCreditPull from '@salesforce/apex/CreditPullController.initiateCreditPull';
import getLoanData from '@salesforce/apex/LoanController.getLoanData';
import CREDIT_DONE_CHANNEL from '@salesforce/messageChannel/CreditPullComplete__c';

export default class CreditPullButton extends LightningElement {
    @api recordId;
    isLoading = false;
    statusMessage = '';
    subscription = null;
    wiredLoanResult;
    @wire(MessageContext) messageContext;

    @wire(getLoanData, { loanId: '$recordId' })
    wiredLoan(result) { this.wiredLoanResult = result; }

    connectedCallback() {
        // Subscribe to Platform Event channel for job completion notification
        this.subscription = subscribe(
            this.messageContext, CREDIT_DONE_CHANNEL,
            (msg) => this.handleCreditComplete(msg),
            { scope: APPLICATION_SCOPE }
        );
    }

    disconnectedCallback() {
        unsubscribe(this.subscription);  // prevent memory leak
    }

    async handlePullCredit() {
        this.isLoading = true;
        this.statusMessage = 'Initiating credit pull...';
        try {
            const jobId = await initiateCreditPull({ loanId: this.recordId });
            this.statusMessage = 'Credit check in progress... (' + jobId.substring(0,8) + ')';
            // Now waiting for Platform Event — no polling needed
        } catch (error) {
            this.isLoading = false;
            this.statusMessage = '';
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Credit Pull Failed',
                message: error.body?.message || 'Could not initiate credit pull',
                variant: 'error', mode: 'sticky'
            }));
        }
    }

    async handleCreditComplete(message) {
        if (message.loanId !== this.recordId) return;  // not for this record
        this.isLoading = false;
        this.statusMessage = '';

        if (message.success) {
            await refreshApex(this.wiredLoanResult);  // refresh loan fields
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Credit Pull Complete',
                message: 'FICO Score: ' + message.ficoScore + ' — ' + message.decision,
                variant: message.ficoScore >= 620 ? 'success' : 'warning'
            }));
        } else {
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Credit Pull Failed',
                message: message.errorMessage,
                variant: 'error', mode: 'sticky'
            }));
        }
    }
}
Show complete Apex controller and Queueable for the credit pull — with FCRA check and error handlingASYNC FLOW▼
// CreditPullController.cls
public with sharing class CreditPullController {

    @AuraEnabled
    public static String initiateCreditPull(Id loanId) {
        Loan__c loan = [SELECT Id, SSN__c, BorrowerLastName__c,
                               CreditAuthorizationDate__c, CreditPullStatus__c
                        FROM Loan__c WHERE Id = :loanId WITH USER_MODE];

        // FCRA compliance check
        if(loan.CreditAuthorizationDate__c == null) {
            throw new AuraHandledException(
                'FCRA Violation: Written credit authorization is required. ' +
                'Upload the signed form and set the authorization date.'
            );
        }
        if(loan.CreditPullStatus__c == 'In Progress') {
            throw new AuraHandledException('A credit pull is already in progress for this loan.');
        }

        // Lock the record status before async job
        loan.CreditPullStatus__c = 'In Progress';
        update loan;

        // Enqueue async job — returns immediately with job ID
        Id jobId = System.enqueueJob(new CreditPullQueueable(loanId));
        return jobId;
    }
}

// CreditPullQueueable.cls
public class CreditPullQueueable implements Queueable, Database.AllowsCallouts {
    private Id loanId;
    public CreditPullQueueable(Id loanId) { this.loanId = loanId; }

    public void execute(QueueableContext ctx) {
        Loan__c loan;
        Boolean success = false;
        Integer ficoScore = null;
        String decision = '';
        String errorMsg = '';

        try {
            loan = [SELECT Id, SSN__c, BorrowerLastName__c FROM Loan__c WHERE Id = :loanId];

            // HTTP callout to Experian (safe — no uncommitted DML in this transaction)
            ExperianService.CreditResult result =
                ExperianService.pullCredit(loan.SSN__c, loan.BorrowerLastName__c);

            loan.FicoScore__c = result.ficoScore;
            loan.CreditPullStatus__c = 'Completed';
            loan.CreditPullDate__c = DateTime.now();
            loan.CreditDecision__c = result.ficoScore >= 620 ? 'Passed' : 'Review Required';
            update loan;

            success = true;
            ficoScore = result.ficoScore;
            decision = loan.CreditDecision__c;

        } catch(Exception e) {
            if(loan != null) {
                loan.CreditPullStatus__c = 'Failed';
                loan.CreditPullError__c = e.getMessage().abbreviate(255);
                update loan;
            }
            errorMsg = e.getMessage();
        } finally {
            // Always publish Platform Event — success or failure
            EventBus.publish(new Credit_Pull_Complete__e(
                LoanId__c = loanId,
                Success__c = success,
                FicoScore__c = ficoScore,
                Decision__c = decision,
                ErrorMessage__c = errorMsg
            ));
        }
    }
}
How do you show real-time progress using polling as an alternative to Platform Events?ASYNC FLOW▼
// Polling approach — check AsyncApexJob status every 3 seconds
import getJobStatus from '@salesforce/apex/AsyncJobController.getJobStatus';

pollingInterval = null;

startPolling(jobId) {
    this.pollingInterval = setInterval(async () => {
        try {
            const job = await getJobStatus({ jobId });
            this.statusMessage = `Status: ${job.Status}`;

            if(['Completed','Failed','Aborted'].includes(job.Status)) {
                clearInterval(this.pollingInterval);
                this.isLoading = false;
                if(job.Status === 'Completed') {
                    await refreshApex(this.wiredLoanResult);
                    this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({ title: 'Done', variant: 'success' }));
                } else {
                    this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                        title: 'Job Failed', message: job.ExtendedStatus, variant: 'error'
                    }));
                }
            }
        } catch(e) {
            clearInterval(this.pollingInterval);
            this.isLoading = false;
        }
    }, 3000);  // every 3 seconds
}

disconnectedCallback() {
    if(this.pollingInterval) clearInterval(this.pollingInterval);  // CRITICAL — prevent leak
}

// Apex — query AsyncApexJob
@AuraEnabled
public static Map<String,String> getJobStatus(Id jobId) {
    AsyncApexJob job = [SELECT Id, Status, ExtendedStatus, NumberOfErrors
                        FROM AsyncApexJob WHERE Id = :jobId];
    return new Map<String,String>{
        'Status' => job.Status, 'ExtendedStatus' => job.ExtendedStatus
    };
}
Polling vs Platform Events

Platform Events are preferred — real-time, no server load from polling, scales better. Use polling only when Platform Event infrastructure is not available or for simple one-off jobs where setting up a message channel is overkill.

How do you implement ShowToastEvent correctly — all variants, modes, and messageData?ASYNC FLOW▼
import { ShowToastEvent } from 'lightning/platformShowToastEvent';

// SUCCESS — auto-dismisses after 3 seconds
this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
    title: 'Credit Pull Complete',
    message: 'FICO Score: 742 — Approved for conventional lending',
    variant: 'success'
    // mode defaults to 'dismissible'
}));

// ERROR STICKY — stays until user closes (use for important errors)
this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
    title: 'Credit Pull Failed',
    message: 'Experian API unavailable. Please retry in 5 minutes.',
    variant: 'error',
    mode: 'sticky'
}));

// WARNING
this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
    title: 'Review Required',
    message: 'FICO score is below the recommended minimum for this loan type.',
    variant: 'warning'
}));

// INFO
this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
    title: 'In Progress',
    message: 'Credit check submitted. You will be notified when complete.',
    variant: 'info'
}));

// With messageData — parameterized message
this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
    title: 'Score Below Threshold',
    message: 'FICO {0} is below the {1} minimum for {2} loans.',
    messageData: [ficoScore, 620, loanType],  // {0},{1},{2} replaced in order
    variant: 'warning'
}));

// COMMON MISTAKES:
// ❌ variant: 'danger'  — WRONG. Correct is: 'error'
// ❌ Not wrapping in new ShowToastEvent() — must be an event object
// ❌ mode: 'auto' — only 'dismissible', 'sticky', 'pester' are valid
// ❌ Dispatching inside wire callback — must dispatch from user action or async handler
How do you test the credit pull Queueable in Apex — mock callout and verify Platform Event?ASYNC FLOW▼
@isTest
public class CreditPullTest {

    // Mock HTTP response from Experian
    public class ExperianMock implements HttpCalloutMock {
        public HttpResponse respond(HttpRequest req) {
            HttpResponse res = new HttpResponse();
            res.setStatusCode(200);
            res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');
            res.setBody('{"ficoScore": 720, "riskTier": "Good", "reportId": "EXP-001"}');
            return res;
        }
    }

    @TestSetup
    static void makeData() {
        Application__c app = new Application__c(Name = 'Test App');
        insert app;
        Loan__c loan = new Loan__c(
            Application__c = app.Id,
            SSN__c = '123-45-6789',
            BorrowerLastName__c = 'TestBorrower',
            CreditAuthorizationDate__c = Date.today(),
            CreditPullStatus__c = 'Not Started'
        );
        insert loan;
    }

    @isTest
    static void testSuccessfulPull() {
        Loan__c loan = [SELECT Id FROM Loan__c LIMIT 1];
        Test.setMock(HttpCalloutMock.class, new ExperianMock());

        Test.startTest();
        String jobId = CreditPullController.initiateCreditPull(loan.Id);
        Test.stopTest();  // Forces Queueable to complete synchronously in test

        // Verify results
        Loan__c updated = [SELECT FicoScore__c, CreditPullStatus__c, CreditDecision__c
                           FROM Loan__c WHERE Id = :loan.Id];
        System.assertEquals(720, updated.FicoScore__c);
        System.assertEquals('Completed', updated.CreditPullStatus__c);
        System.assertEquals('Passed', updated.CreditDecision__c);
        System.assertNotEquals(null, jobId, 'Should return a job ID');
    }

    @isTest
    static void testFCRAViolation() {
        Loan__c loan = [SELECT Id FROM Loan__c LIMIT 1];
        loan.CreditAuthorizationDate__c = null;
        update loan;

        Test.startTest();
        try {
            CreditPullController.initiateCreditPull(loan.Id);
            System.assert(false, 'Should have thrown AuraHandledException');
        } catch(AuraHandledException e) {
            System.assert(e.getMessage().contains('FCRA'), 'Should mention FCRA');
        }
        Test.stopTest();
    }
}
How do you handle Queueable job failures silently and notify users through Platform Events?ASYNC FLOW▼
// Pattern: ALWAYS publish Platform Event in finally block — never let Queueable fail silently
public void execute(QueueableContext ctx) {
    Boolean success = false;
    String errorMsg = '';
    Loan__c loan;

    try {
        loan = [SELECT Id, SSN__c FROM Loan__c WHERE Id = :loanId];
        // ... do work ...
        success = true;
    } catch(CalloutException e) {
        errorMsg = 'External API unavailable: ' + e.getMessage();
        // Specific handling for network errors
    } catch(DmlException e) {
        errorMsg = 'Database error: ' + e.getMessage();
    } catch(Exception e) {
        errorMsg = 'Unexpected error: ' + e.getMessage();
        // Log for debugging
        insert new Error_Log__c(
            Context__c = 'CreditPullQueueable',
            Message__c = e.getMessage(),
            StackTrace__c = e.getStackTraceString().abbreviate(32000),
            RecordId__c = loanId
        );
    } finally {
        // This ALWAYS runs — even if exception occurs
        // Keeps the UI informed regardless of what happened
        Credit_Pull_Complete__e evt = new Credit_Pull_Complete__e(
            LoanId__c = loanId,
            Success__c = success,
            ErrorMessage__c = errorMsg.abbreviate(255)
        );
        EventBus.publish(evt);
        // NOTE: EventBus.publish in finally is safe — publishes even after rollback
        // (if using PublishImmediately delivery)
    }
}
What is the difference between @future and Queueable for the credit pull — why Queueable is better here?ASYNC FLOW▼
Feature@future(callout=true)Queueable + AllowsCallouts
Pass sObject parametersNO — only primitives (Id, String, Integer)YES — full Loan__c object
Monitor job statusNO — no ID returnedYES — enqueueJob returns ID, query AsyncApexJob
Chain another jobNO — cannot call @future from @futureYES — enqueueJob inside execute()
Exception visibilitySwallowed — no notification unless you log manuallyMore visible — AsyncApexJob.ExtendedStatus
TestingTest.startTest/stopTest completes itSame — Test.startTest/stopTest
// @future — works but limited:
@future(callout=true)
public static void pullCreditFuture(Id loanId, String ssn) {
    // Can only accept Id and String — not Loan__c object
    // Cannot chain another job after this
    // Job ID not available for monitoring
}

// Queueable — better for credit pull:
public class CreditPullQueueable implements Queueable, Database.AllowsCallouts {
    private Loan__c loan;  // can store full sObject
    public CreditPullQueueable(Loan__c loan) { this.loan = loan; }
    public void execute(QueueableContext ctx) {
        // After credit check, chain OFAC screening:
        System.enqueueJob(new OFACCheckQueueable(this.loan));
    }
}
How do you store credit pull results securely in Salesforce — what fields and objects to use?ASYNC FLOW▼
// Summary fields on Loan__c (frequently accessed):
loan.FicoScore__c = result.ficoScore;          // Number — for quick display
loan.CreditDecision__c = result.decision;       // Picklist — Passed/Review Required
loan.CreditPullDate__c = DateTime.now();        // DateTime — for FCRA records
loan.CreditPullStatus__c = 'Completed';        // Picklist — tracks async state

ContentVersion cv = new ContentVersion();
cv.Title = 'Credit Report - ' + loan.Name + ' - ' + Date.today().format();
cv.PathOnClient = 'credit_report.json';
cv.VersionData = Blob.valueOf(rawJsonResponse);  // full Experian response
cv.FirstPublishLocationId = loan.Id;  // links file to loan record
insert cv;

);

How do Platform Event triggers handle errors — what prevents infinite retry loops?ASYNC FLOW▼
// Platform Event trigger — MUST handle errors carefully
// Throwing an unhandled exception causes Salesforce to RETRY the event delivery (up to 72 hours)
// This can create infinite retry loops for genuinely broken events

trigger CreditPullCompleteTrigger on Credit_Pull_Complete__e (after insert) {
    for(Credit_Pull_Complete__e evt : Trigger.new) {
        try {
            // Process each event individually in try-catch
            Loan__c loan = [SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Id = :evt.LoanId__c];
            loan.EventProcessed__c = true;
            update loan;
        } catch(QueryException e) {
            // Loan not found — this is NOT retryable, log and continue
            insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c = 'Loan not found: ' + evt.LoanId__c);
            // Do NOT throw — throwing here causes retry
        } catch(DmlException e) {
            // DML failed — might be retryable
            // Use EventBus.RetryableException to signal intentional retry:
            // throw new EventBus.RetryableException('Retry needed: ' + e.getMessage());
            // Without RetryableException: log and move on
            insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c = 'DML failed: ' + e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}

// Key rules for Platform Event trigger error handling:
// - Wrap each event in individual try-catch to isolate failures
// - Only throw EventBus.RetryableException when retry is genuinely the right action
// - Never throw regular exceptions — they cause indefinite retry
// - Log all errors to a custom object for debugging
// - Use Database.DML with allOrNone=false for partial success in subscriber

How do you use lightning-file-upload component — complete working example?FILE UPLOAD▼
<!-- documentUpload.html -->
<lightning-card title="Upload Loan Documents">
    <lightning-file-upload
        label="Upload Documents (PDF, max 10MB)"
        name="loanDocuments"
        accept=".pdf,.jpg,.png"
        record-id={recordId}
        multiple
        onuploadfinished={handleUploadFinished}>
    </lightning-file-upload>
</lightning-card>

// documentUpload.js
import { LightningElement, api, track } from 'lwc';
import { ShowToastEvent } from 'lightning/platformShowToastEvent';
import linkDocumentToLoan from '@salesforce/apex/DocumentController.linkDocumentToLoan';

export default class DocumentUpload extends LightningElement {
    @api recordId;
    @track uploadedFiles = [];

    async handleUploadFinished(event) {
        // event.detail.files = array of { documentId, name, contentVersionId }
        const files = event.detail.files;
        this.uploadedFiles = [...this.uploadedFiles, ...files];

        try {
            // Post-upload processing — tag files with document type
            for (const file of files) {
                await linkDocumentToLoan({
                    contentDocumentId: file.documentId,
                    loanId: this.recordId,
                    documentType: 'Supporting Document'
                });
            }
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Upload Complete',
                message: files.length + ' file(s) uploaded successfully',
                variant: 'success'
            }));
        } catch(e) {
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Post-Upload Processing Failed',
                message: e.body?.message, variant: 'error'
            }));
        }
    }
}
How do you upload a 12MB file using chunked upload — LWC + Apex complete code?FILE UPLOAD▼
// LWC — chunks the file client-side before sending
const CHUNK_SIZE = 3 * 1024 * 1024;  // 3MB per chunk (safe for Apex 6MB heap)

export default class ChunkedUpload extends LightningElement {
    @api recordId;
    isUploading = false;
    progressPercent = 0;

    async handleFileChange(event) {
        const file = event.target.files[0];
        if (!file) return;
        this.isUploading = true;
        const uploadId = 'UPL_' + Date.now() + '_' + Math.random().toString(36).substr(2,6);
        const totalChunks = Math.ceil(file.size / CHUNK_SIZE);

        try {
            for (let i = 0; i < totalChunks; i++) {
                const start = i * CHUNK_SIZE;
                const chunk = file.slice(start, Math.min(start + CHUNK_SIZE, file.size));
                const base64 = await this.readAsBase64(chunk);

                await uploadChunk({
                    uploadId, chunkNumber: i, totalChunks,
                    fileName: file.name, base64Data: base64, fileSize: file.size
                });
                this.progressPercent = Math.round(((i + 1) / totalChunks) * 90);
            }
            // Finalize — assemble chunks server-side
            const result = await finalizeUpload({
                uploadId, loanId: this.recordId, fileName: file.name
            });
            this.progressPercent = 100;
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Upload Complete', message: file.name + ' uploaded', variant: 'success'
            }));
        } catch(e) {
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({
                title: 'Upload Failed', message: e.body?.message, variant: 'error'
            }));
        } finally { this.isUploading = false; }
    }

    readAsBase64(blob) {
        return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
            const reader = new FileReader();
            reader.onload = () => resolve(reader.result.split(',')[1]);
            reader.onerror = reject;
            reader.readAsDataURL(blob);
        });
    }
}
// Apex — ChunkedUploadController.cls
public class ChunkedUploadController {

    @AuraEnabled
    public static void uploadChunk(String uploadId, Integer chunkNumber, Integer totalChunks,
                                   String fileName, String base64Data, Long fileSize) {
        insert new Upload_Chunk__c(
            UploadId__c = uploadId, ChunkNumber__c = chunkNumber,
            TotalChunks__c = totalChunks, FileName__c = fileName,
            ChunkData__c = base64Data, FileSize__c = fileSize
        );
    }

    @AuraEnabled
    public static Map<String,String> finalizeUpload(String uploadId, Id loanId, String fileName) {
        List<Upload_Chunk__c> chunks = [
            SELECT ChunkNumber__c, ChunkData__c FROM Upload_Chunk__c
            WHERE UploadId__c = :uploadId ORDER BY ChunkNumber__c ASC
        ];
        // Reassemble base64
        String combined = '';
        for(Upload_Chunk__c c : chunks) combined += c.ChunkData__c;
        Blob fileData = EncodingUtil.base64Decode(combined);

        // Save to Salesforce Files
        ContentVersion cv = new ContentVersion(
            Title = fileName, PathOnClient = fileName,
            VersionData = fileData, FirstPublishLocationId = loanId
        );
        insert cv;

        // Queue upload to Google Drive
        Id jobId = System.enqueueJob(new GoogleDriveUploadQueueable(cv.Id, loanId, fileName));

        // Cleanup temp chunks
        delete chunks;
        return new Map<String,String>{ 'contentVersionId' => cv.Id, 'jobId' => jobId };
    }
}
How do ContentDocument, ContentDocumentLink, and ContentVersion work together — query and manage files?FILE UPLOAD▼
// THREE OBJECTS in the Salesforce Files system:
// ContentVersion — the actual file binary (each version = separate record)
// ContentDocument — the logical file (parent of all ContentVersions)
// ContentDocumentLink — links a file to one or more Salesforce records

// CREATE a file and link to a record:
ContentVersion cv = new ContentVersion(
    Title = 'Loan Agreement 2024',
    PathOnClient = 'loan_agreement.pdf',
    VersionData = fileBlob,             // binary content
    FirstPublishLocationId = loanId     // auto-creates ContentDocumentLink
);
insert cv;

// Get the ContentDocumentId (created after insert):
cv = [SELECT ContentDocumentId FROM ContentVersion WHERE Id = :cv.Id];

// LINK the same file to additional records:
insert new ContentDocumentLink(
    ContentDocumentId = cv.ContentDocumentId,
    LinkedEntityId = applicationId,  // link to Application too
    ShareType = 'V',                 // V = viewer, C = collaborator, I = inferred
    Visibility = 'AllUsers'
);

// QUERY all files linked to a record:
List<ContentDocumentLink> links = [
    SELECT ContentDocument.Title, ContentDocument.FileExtension,
           ContentDocument.ContentSize, ContentDocument.LatestPublishedVersionId,
           ContentDocument.CreatedDate, ContentDocument.CreatedBy.Name
    FROM ContentDocumentLink
    WHERE LinkedEntityId = :loanId
    ORDER BY ContentDocument.CreatedDate DESC
];

// Download URL for a file:
// '/sfc/servlet.shepherd/version/download/' + contentVersionId

// DELETE a file (deletes all versions and all links):
delete [SELECT Id FROM ContentDocument WHERE Id = :contentDocumentId];
How do you send a file from Salesforce to Google Drive using a Queueable with OAuth2 Named Credential?FILE UPLOAD▼
// GoogleDriveUploadQueueable.cls
public class GoogleDriveUploadQueueable implements Queueable, Database.AllowsCallouts {
    private Id contentVersionId;
    private Id loanId;
    private String fileName;

    public GoogleDriveUploadQueueable(Id cvId, Id loanId, String fileName) {
        this.contentVersionId = cvId;
        this.loanId = loanId;
        this.fileName = fileName;
    }

    public void execute(QueueableContext ctx) {
        // Retrieve file binary from Salesforce Files
        ContentVersion cv = [SELECT Id, VersionData, FileExtension FROM ContentVersion WHERE Id = :contentVersionId];

        // Determine MIME type
        String mimeType = getMimeType(cv.FileExtension);

        // Upload to Google Drive via Named Credential (handles OAuth2 automatically)
        // Named Credential 'GoogleDriveAPI' configured with OAuth2 Client Credentials or JWT
        String boundary = 'sfdc_boundary_' + String.valueOf(DateTime.now().getTime());

        // Build multipart request body
        String metadata = '{"name":"' + fileName + '","parents":["' + getDriveFolderId(loanId) + '"]}';
        String body = '--' + boundary + '\r\n'
            + 'Content-Type: application/json; charset=UTF-8\r\n\r\n'
            + metadata + '\r\n'
            + '--' + boundary + '\r\n'
            + 'Content-Type: ' + mimeType + '\r\n'
            + 'Content-Transfer-Encoding: base64\r\n\r\n'
            + EncodingUtil.base64Encode(cv.VersionData) + '\r\n'
            + '--' + boundary + '--';

        HttpRequest req = new HttpRequest();
        req.setEndpoint('callout:GoogleDriveAPI/upload/drive/v3/files?uploadType=multipart');
        req.setMethod('POST');
        req.setHeader('Content-Type', 'multipart/related; boundary="' + boundary + '"');
        req.setTimeout(120000);  // 2 minutes for large files
        req.setBody(body);

        HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req);
        if(res.getStatusCode() == 200) {
            Map<String,Object> parsed = (Map<String,Object>) JSON.deserializeUntyped(res.getBody());
            String driveFileId = (String)parsed.get('id');
            // Save Google Drive file ID back to Loan record
            update new Loan__c(Id = loanId, GDrive_File_ID__c = driveFileId,
                               GDrive_Upload_Date__c = DateTime.now());
        } else {
            throw new GoogleDriveException('Upload failed: ' + res.getStatusCode() + ' ' + res.getBody());
        }
    }

    private String getMimeType(String ext) {
        Map<String,String> types = new Map<String,String>{
            'pdf'=>'application/pdf','jpg'=>'image/jpeg','jpeg'=>'image/jpeg','png'=>'image/png'
        };
        return types.containsKey(ext?.toLowerCase()) ? types.get(ext.toLowerCase()) : 'application/octet-stream';
    }

    public class GoogleDriveException extends Exception {}
}
How do you display uploaded files in an LWC component with download links and delete option?FILE UPLOAD▼
// fileList.js
import { LightningElement, api, wire } from 'lwc';
import { deleteRecord } from 'lightning/uiRecordApi';
import { refreshApex } from '@salesforce/apex';
import { ShowToastEvent } from 'lightning/platformShowToastEvent';
import getLinkedFiles from '@salesforce/apex/DocumentController.getLinkedFiles';

export default class FileList extends LightningElement {
    @api recordId;
    wiredFilesResult;
    files = [];

    @wire(getLinkedFiles, { recordId: '$recordId' })
    wiredFiles(result) {
        this.wiredFilesResult = result;
        if(result.data) {
            this.files = result.data.map(f => ({
                ...f,
                downloadUrl: '/sfc/servlet.shepherd/version/download/' + f.contentVersionId,
                iconName: this.getIcon(f.extension)
            }));
        }
    }

    getIcon(ext) {
        return { pdf:'doctype:pdf', jpg:'doctype:image', png:'doctype:image',
                 doc:'doctype:word', docx:'doctype:word' }[ext?.toLowerCase()] || 'doctype:unknown';
    }

    async handleDelete(event) {
        const docId = event.target.dataset.docid;
        if (!confirm('Delete this file permanently?')) return;
        try {
            await deleteRecord(docId);  // deletes ContentDocument + all links
            await refreshApex(this.wiredFilesResult);
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({ title: 'Deleted', variant: 'success' }));
        } catch(e) {
            this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({ title: 'Delete Failed', message: e.body?.message, variant: 'error' }));
        }
    }
}

// Apex:
@AuraEnabled(cacheable=true)
public static List<Map<String,Object>> getLinkedFiles(Id recordId) {
    List<Map<String,Object>> result = new List<Map<String,Object>>();
    for(ContentDocumentLink cdl : [
        SELECT ContentDocument.Title, ContentDocument.FileExtension,
               ContentDocument.ContentSize, ContentDocument.LatestPublishedVersionId,
               ContentDocument.Id, ContentDocument.CreatedDate, ContentDocument.CreatedBy.Name
        FROM ContentDocumentLink WHERE LinkedEntityId = :recordId
        ORDER BY ContentDocument.CreatedDate DESC
    ]) {
        Long bytes = cdl.ContentDocument.ContentSize;
        String size = bytes < 1048576 ? (bytes/1024) + ' KB' : String.valueOf((bytes/1048576.0).setScale(1)) + ' MB';
        result.add(new Map<String,Object>{
            'title' => cdl.ContentDocument.Title,
            'extension' => cdl.ContentDocument.FileExtension,
            'contentVersionId' => cdl.ContentDocument.LatestPublishedVersionId,
            'contentDocumentId' => cdl.ContentDocument.Id,
            'fileSize' => size,
            'uploadedBy' => cdl.ContentDocument.CreatedBy.Name,
            'uploadedDate' => cdl.ContentDocument.CreatedDate.format('MMM dd, yyyy')
        });
    }
    return result;
}

How do you validate file types and sizes before upload in LWC?FILE UPLOAD▼
// Client-side validation before upload
import { LightningElement } from 'lwc';
const MAX_FILE_SIZE = 5 * 1024 * 1024; // 5MB
const ALLOWED_TYPES = ['application/pdf', 'image/jpeg', 'image/png', 'application/vnd.openxmlformats-officedocument.wordprocessingml.document'];

export default class DocumentUploader extends LightningElement {
  handleFileChange(event) {
    const files = [...event.target.files];
    const errors = [];

    for (const file of files) {
      if (file.size > MAX_FILE_SIZE)
        errors.push(`${file.name} exceeds 5MB limit (${(file.size/1024/1024).toFixed(1)}MB)`);
      if (!ALLOWED_TYPES.includes(file.type))
        errors.push(`${file.name} is not an allowed file type. Use PDF, JPEG, PNG, or DOCX.`);
    }

    if (errors.length > 0) {
      this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({ title:'Upload Error', message:errors.join('\n'), variant:'error', mode:'sticky' }));
      event.target.value = ''; // clear the file input
      return;
    }

    // Valid files — proceed with upload
    this.uploadFiles(files);
  }
}
How do you upload files to Google Drive from Salesforce?FILE UPLOAD▼
// Pattern: Salesforce → Google Drive via Google Drive API
// Prerequisites: Connected App + Named Credential for Google OAuth2

public class GoogleDriveService {
  // Step 1: Get OAuth access token via Named Credential
  // Step 2: Create file in Drive
  public static String uploadToDrive(Blob fileContent, String fileName, String mimeType, String folderId) {
    // Multipart upload to Drive API
    String boundary = '---boundary' + String.valueOf(DateTime.now().getTime());

    // Build multipart body — metadata part + file content part
    String metadata = JSON.serialize(new Map<String,Object>{
      'name' => fileName,
      'parents' => new List<String>{ folderId },
      'mimeType' => mimeType
    });

    HttpRequest req = new HttpRequest();
    req.setEndpoint('callout:Google_Drive_NC/upload/drive/v3/files?uploadType=multipart');
    req.setMethod('POST');
    req.setHeader('Content-Type', 'multipart/related; boundary="' + boundary + '"');

    // Combine metadata + file bytes
    String body = '--' + boundary + '
Content-Type: application/json

' + metadata;
    body += '
--' + boundary + '
Content-Type: ' + mimeType + '

';
    Blob combinedBody = Blob.valueOf(body);
    // Note: for binary files, use EncodingUtil to handle the binary portion

    req.setBodyAsBlob(combinedBody);
    req.setTimeout(30000);

    HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req);
    if (res.getStatusCode() == 200) {
      Map<String,Object> result = (Map<String,Object>) JSON.deserializeUntyped(res.getBody());
      return (String) result.get('id'); // Google Drive file ID
    }
    throw new IntegrationException('Drive upload failed: ' + res.getStatusCode() + ' ' + res.getBody());
  }
}
How do you generate a download link for a Salesforce file in LWC?FILE UPLOAD▼
// Generate download URL for ContentVersion
// URL pattern: /sfc/servlet.shepherd/document/download/{ContentDocumentId}
// OR for version: /sfc/servlet.shepherd/version/download/{ContentVersionId}

// In Apex — return file metadata with download URL
@AuraEnabled(cacheable=true)
public static List<Map<String,Object>> getLoanDocuments(Id loanId) {
  String baseUrl = URL.getOrgDomainUrl().toExternalForm();
  List<Map<String,Object>> files = new List<Map<String,Object>>();
  for (ContentDocumentLink cdl : [SELECT ContentDocumentId, ContentDocument.Title,
      ContentDocument.LatestPublishedVersionId, ContentDocument.ContentSize
      FROM ContentDocumentLink WHERE LinkedEntityId=:loanId]) {
    files.add(new Map<String,Object>{
      'id'          => cdl.ContentDocumentId,
      'title'       => cdl.ContentDocument.Title,
      'downloadUrl' => baseUrl + '/sfc/servlet.shepherd/document/download/' + cdl.ContentDocumentId,
      'size'        => cdl.ContentDocument.ContentSize
    });
  }
  return files;
}

// In LWC template — clickable download link
// <a href={file.downloadUrl} target="_blank">{file.title}</a>
How do you delete Salesforce Files programmatically?FILE UPLOAD▼
// Delete ContentDocument (deletes all versions and all links)
// Must have Delete permission on ContentDocument
public static void deleteLoanDocument(Id contentDocumentId, Id loanId) {
  // Verify the file is linked to this loan (security check)
  List<ContentDocumentLink> link = [SELECT Id FROM ContentDocumentLink
    WHERE ContentDocumentId=:contentDocumentId AND LinkedEntityId=:loanId];
  if (link.isEmpty()) throw new SecurityException('File not linked to this loan');

  // Check if file is linked to other records too
  Integer linkCount = [SELECT COUNT() FROM ContentDocumentLink WHERE ContentDocumentId=:contentDocumentId];
  if (linkCount > 1) {
    // Only unlink from this record — don't delete the file (it's shared with other records)
    delete link[0]; // delete the ContentDocumentLink, not the ContentDocument
  } else {
    // Only linked to this record — safe to delete entirely
    delete new ContentDocument(Id=contentDocumentId);
  }
}
Salesforce Flow — 10 Scenario Questions
When to use Flow, how to build invocable actions, debug, and integrate with Apex
Flow vs Apex Trigger — the complete decision framework with examplesFLOW▼

Use Flow when:

  • Logic must be admin-maintainable without code deployment
  • Before Save field defaults or simple same-object updates (faster than After Save)
  • Sending email alerts, creating one related record (task, chatter post)
  • Calling an @InvocableMethod Apex action for a single step
  • Processing small record sets (under 50 records at once)

Use Apex Trigger when:

  • Bulk operations — triggers safely handle 200 records; Flow has governor limit risk at scale
  • Complex cross-object SOQL with multiple relationship levels
  • External API callouts required (Flow cannot make callouts natively)
  • Complex error handling — partial DML, retry logic
  • Performance-critical path — Apex triggers run faster than equivalent Flow for bulk
  • Logic that must be bullet-proof against governor limits regardless of data volume
Rule of thumb for interviews

"If a Salesforce admin should be able to understand and modify the logic without a code deployment, and it doesn't involve bulk operations or callouts, I use Flow. For everything that touches large data volumes, external APIs, or complex Apex logic — I use a trigger with handler pattern. The two approaches are complementary, not competing."

Before Save Flow vs After Save Flow — when to use each and what each can do?FLOW▼
FeatureBefore Save FlowAfter Save Flow
Update same record fieldsYES — directly, no DMLNO — causes recursion
Create related recordsNO — no Id on insert yetYES — record Id available
Send emailsNOYES
Call Apex actionYES (Invocable)YES (Invocable)
PerformanceFaster — same DML transactionSlightly slower
Record Id availableNO for new records on insertYES always
// Before Save Flow use case: Set LoanCategory__c based on LoanAmount__c
// Flow: Record-Triggered → Before Save on Insert/Update
// Decision: IF LoanAmount__c <= 417000 → Set LoanCategory__c = 'Conforming'
//           IF LoanAmount__c <= 1089300 → Set LoanCategory__c = 'High Balance'
//           ELSE → Set LoanCategory__c = 'Jumbo'
// No DML needed — field set directly in Before Save context

// After Save Flow use case: Create a Task when loan status changes to Underwriting
// Flow: Record-Triggered → After Save on Update
// Condition: Prior Value of Status__c != 'Underwriting' AND Status__c = 'Underwriting'
// Action: Create Records (Task) — Subject = 'Underwriting Review', WhatId = LoanId
How do you create an @InvocableMethod for Flow — complete code with input and output variables?FLOW▼
// Complete InvocableMethod — Flow calls this as an Apex Action
public class LoanStatusNotificationAction {

    public class NotifyRequest {
        @InvocableVariable(label='Loan ID' required=true
            description='Salesforce record ID of the Loan__c to notify about')
        public Id loanId;

        @InvocableVariable(label='New Status' required=true)
        public String newStatus;

        @InvocableVariable(label='Send Email' description='Set to true to send borrower email')
        public Boolean sendEmail;
    }

    public class NotifyResult {
        @InvocableVariable(label='Notification Sent')
        public Boolean notificationSent;

        @InvocableVariable(label='Error Message')
        public String errorMessage;
    }

    // MUST accept and return List<T> — Flow can call in bulk
    @InvocableMethod(
        label='Send Loan Status Notification'
        description='Sends email/SMS to borrower when loan status changes. Use in Record-Triggered Flow after save.'
        category='Loan Processing'
    )
    public static List<NotifyResult> sendNotification(List<NotifyRequest> requests) {
        List<NotifyResult> results = new List<NotifyResult>();
        for(NotifyRequest req : requests) {
            NotifyResult result = new NotifyResult();
            try {
                if(req.sendEmail == true) {
                    NotificationService.sendStatusEmail(req.loanId, req.newStatus);
                }
                result.notificationSent = true;
            } catch(Exception e) {
                result.notificationSent = false;
                result.errorMessage = e.getMessage();
            }
            results.add(result);
        }
        return results;
    }
}

// In Flow Builder:
// Add "Action" element → Search "Send Loan Status Notification"
// Map: {!$Record.Id} → loanId, {!$Record.Status__c} → newStatus, {!true} → sendEmail
// Capture output: notificationSent → {!notificationSent} variable for downstream logic
How do you debug a Flow that fails in production — what tools and approach?FLOW▼
  • Flow Builder Debug Button: Click Debug in Flow Builder → enter input values manually → step through element by element — see variable values at each step, error message at failing element
  • Debug Logs: Setup → Debug → Apex Debug Logs → Add trace for the user. Set FLOW = FINEST. Filter log for FLOW_ELEMENT_ERROR to find exact failure point and variable values
  • Send Flow Error Emails: Setup → Process Automation Settings → "Send Flow Error Emails" — admins receive an email with which flow, which element, the error message, and variable values at time of failure. HIGHLY recommended for production
  • Fault Paths: Every element that can fail (Get Records, Send Email, Apex Action) should have a Fault path. In the fault path: assign {!$Flow.FaultMessage} to a text variable, create an Error_Log__c record. Without fault paths, Flow fails silently
  • Rollback Mode: Debug → Run with Rollback Mode — tests the flow logic without actually committing DML. Safe for testing on real records
Production debugging tip

Never debug a failing Flow directly on production data. Reproduce the exact record state in Full Sandbox, debug there, fix, then deploy. If you must debug in production, use Rollback Mode to avoid unintended data changes.

What are the Flow governor limit pitfalls — when does Flow become dangerous at scale?FLOW▼
  • Get Records inside a Loop: Every iteration of a Loop with a Get Records element = one SOQL query. 100 loop iterations = 100 queries = governor limit hit. Solution: Get all records BEFORE the loop into a collection variable
  • Update Records inside a Loop: Every iteration = one DML. 150 iterations = limit hit. Solution: Add records to a collection variable inside the loop, Update Records AFTER the loop with the collection
  • After Save Flow on a frequently-updated object: If 1000 records are updated via Bulk API, the After Save Flow fires 1000 times. Each run shares the org's transaction limits. Solution: use "Only when a record is created or when a record meets/stops meeting filter conditions" to limit trigger firing
  • Recursive Flow: Flow updates a field on the record, which re-triggers the Record-Triggered Flow. Use entry conditions carefully. Use "Only when a record is created or meets criteria for the first time" (entry type) to prevent reentry
// BAD pattern in Flow loop — SOQL per iteration:
// Loop: For each Loan in Loan_Collection
//   Get Records: Get Contact WHERE Id = {!Current_Loan.BorrowerContact__c}  ← SOQL per iteration!

// GOOD pattern:
// Before loop: Get Records: Get all Contacts WHERE Id IN {!Loan_BorrowerContact_IDs}
// Loop: For each Loan in Loan_Collection
//   Decision: Find matching Contact in the collection (no SOQL inside loop)
How do you call a Flow from Apex — and from LWC?FLOW SCENARIOS▼
// Call a Screen Flow from LWC — lightning-flow component
// <lightning-flow flow-api-name="Loan_Application_Flow" flow-input-variables={flowInputs} onstatuschange={handleFlowChange}></lightning-flow>

// Flow input variables
get flowInputs() {
  return [{ name: 'recordId', type: 'String', value: this.recordId },
          { name: 'loanType', type: 'String', value: this.loanType }];
}
handleFlowChange(event) {
  if (event.detail.status === 'FINISHED') this.dispatchEvent(new RefreshEvent());
}

// Invoke an autolaunched Flow from Apex
Map<String,Object> inputs = new Map<String,Object>{ 'loanId' => loan.Id, 'newStatus' => 'Approved' };
Flow.Interview interview = Flow.Interview.createInterview('Loan_Status_Update_Flow', inputs);
interview.start();
// Get output variables after completion:
String result = (String) interview.getVariableValue('outputMessage');
What are Flow best practices for governor limit management?FLOW SCENARIOS▼
  • Before-Save flows have no governor limit impact — they run in same transaction as the save, no extra DML. Prefer Before-Save for simple field updates.
  • After-Save flows get 2,000 DML rows — but still count against the transaction's DML statement limit (150). Multiple After-Save flows on the same object share the limit.
  • Avoid loops that do DML inside — same rule as Apex. Use Collection variables to collect records, then a single Create/Update Records element outside the loop.
  • Scheduled Paths (async) — After-Save flows can have async paths that run after a delay. These get a fresh governor limit set — good for time-delayed actions.
  • Flow + Apex hybrid — complex logic goes in Apex @InvocableMethod, Flow handles the user interaction and orchestration. Each keeps to what it does best.
What are the differences between Flow variables, resources, and collections?FLOW SCENARIOS▼
Resource TypeWhat it storesExample
VariableSingle value — text, number, boolean, recordloanId, statusValue, isApproved
Record VariableSingle SObject record with its fieldscurrentLoan (Loan__c)
Record Collection VariableList of SObject recordsselectedLoans (List<Loan__c>)
Text TemplateReusable formatted text with merge fieldsEmail body with {!currentLoan.Name}
FormulaCalculated value{!TODAY() + 30} for close date
ConstantFixed value used across the flowMAX_LOAN_AMOUNT = 2000000
StageCurrent position in a Screen Flow wizardStage 1 of 4
Collection performance

Use Record Collection Variables to batch DML in flows. Loop over records → add to collection variable → after loop use one Create/Update Records element on the whole collection. Never use DML elements inside loops.

How do sub-flows work — when should you extract logic into a sub-flow?FLOW SCENARIOS▼

Sub-flows are reusable flow components. Call them from a parent flow the same way you call a method — pass inputs, get outputs back.

// When to extract to sub-flow:
// 1. Same logic reused in 3+ flows
// 2. A logical unit that can be tested independently
// 3. Complex branching that makes the parent hard to read

// Sub-flow pattern:
// Parent flow: Loan Application Flow
//   → Sub-flow: Credit Check Sub-Flow (inputs: SSN, loanAmount. outputs: score, approved)
//   → Sub-flow: OFAC Check Sub-Flow (inputs: borrowerName, SSN. outputs: clear, matchFound)
//   → Sub-flow: Document Generation Sub-Flow (inputs: loanId, loanType)

// Benefits: each sub-flow can be updated independently without touching the parent
// Risk: deeply nested sub-flows are hard to debug — limit to 2 levels deep
Sub-flow governor limits

Sub-flows run in the SAME transaction as the parent. They share the same governor limit pool — a sub-flow that does 50 DML statements counts against the parent's 150-statement limit.

What is the Flow Orchestration — how does it differ from regular Flows?FLOW SCENARIOS▼

Flow Orchestration (formerly Orchestrator) enables multi-step, multi-user approval and review processes with assigned steps, stages, and work items.

  • Stages — phases of the orchestration (Application Review, Underwriting, Approval, Funding)
  • Steps — individual tasks within a stage. Can be assigned to specific users, roles, or queues
  • Interactive Steps — require a human to complete a screen flow (review and approve a document)
  • Background Steps — run automation automatically (call Apex, run a sub-flow) without human interaction
  • Sequential vs Parallel — steps in the same stage can run in sequence or in parallel
  • Work Items — tasks created for assigned users. Appear in the Salesforce To-Do list and Inbox
vs Standard Approval Process

Use Flow Orchestration when: multiple sequential approvers with different tasks, mixed human review and automated steps, need to track progress through stages, need complex routing logic. Use Standard Approval Process when: simple 1-3 level approval chain, no custom steps between approvals.

Reports & Dashboards — 10 Scenarios
Practical reporting scenarios for senior Salesforce developers — from report types to Apex Analytics API
What are the 4 types of Salesforce reports — when do you use each with mortgage examples?REPORTS▼
TypeStructureCharts?Mortgage Use Case
TabularSimple rows — no groupingNoExport all active loans with contact info for mail merge
SummaryRows grouped by field(s) with subtotalsYesTotal funded loans per loan officer per month
MatrixGrouped by row AND column cross-tabYesLoan count by status (rows) vs loan type (columns)
JoinedMultiple blocks from different objectsYes per blockNew applications this week (block 1) next to loans closing this week (block 2)

Custom Report Types: When standard report types don't show the objects/fields you need, create a Custom Report Type. Example: "Loans with Borrowers and Documents" — Loan__c primary + Loan_Borrower__c related + ContentDocumentLink related. Makes all three objects' fields available in one report.

How do you read a Salesforce report from Apex using the Reports API?REPORTS▼
// Synchronous report run — returns up to 2000 rows, immediate response
Reports.ReportResults results = Reports.ReportManager.runReport('00O5g...', true);
// true = include detail rows; false = summary only (faster)

// Access the fact map
// Key format: 'rowGroupIndex!colGroupIndex' or 'T!T' for grand total
Reports.ReportFactWithDetails grandTotal =
    (Reports.ReportFactWithDetails) results.getFactMap().get('T!T');

Integer rowCount = grandTotal.getRows().size();
for(Reports.ReportDetailRow row : grandTotal.getRows()) {
    List<Reports.ReportDataCell> cells = row.getDataCells();
    String loanName = cells[0].getLabel();   // formatted display value
    Object amount = cells[1].getValue();     // raw value (Decimal, Id, String)
    System.debug(loanName + ': ' + amount);
}

// Get column names from metadata
List<String> columns = results.getReportMetadata().getDetailColumns();

// Override filters at runtime (no change to saved report)
Reports.ReportMetadata meta = Reports.ReportManager.describeReport('00O...').getReportMetadata();
Reports.ReportFilter filter = new Reports.ReportFilter();
filter.setColumn('STATUS');
filter.setOperator('equals');
filter.setValue('Active');
meta.setReportFilters(new List<Reports.ReportFilter>{ filter });
Reports.ReportResults filtered = Reports.ReportManager.runReport(meta, true);

// Asynchronous run (for reports over 2000 rows)
Reports.ReportInstance instance = Reports.ReportManager.runAsyncReport('00O...', true);
String instanceId = instance.getId();
// Poll: Reports.ReportManager.getReportInstance('00O...', instanceId).getStatus()
What is a Dynamic Dashboard — how does it work and what are the limitations?REPORTS▼

A Dynamic Dashboard uses "Run As: Logged-in user" instead of a fixed user. Each person who opens the dashboard sees data filtered by their own permissions and record ownership — everyone sees their own data from the same dashboard.

Mortgage use case: One "Loan Officer Performance Dashboard" showing My Active Loans, My Pipeline Value, My Closing This Week. Loan Officer A sees their 15 loans. Officer B sees their 8 loans. Admin sees all.

  • Cannot be scheduled for email refresh (only static dashboards can be scheduled)
  • Cannot be combined with Dashboard Filters
  • Maximum 10 dynamic dashboards per org (varies by edition)
  • Underlying reports must use "with sharing" data — no system-mode access
  • Each viewer must have access to the underlying report
What is a Cross Filter in a report — show a mortgage example?REPORTS▼

Cross Filters let you filter report results based on whether related records EXIST or DON'T EXIST. They answer questions that regular filters cannot — "Show me Loans that have NO uploaded appraisal document."

In Report Builder: Add Filter → Cross Filter → "[Object] with/without [Related Object]"

  • "Loans WITHOUT ContentDocumentLink where Title contains 'Appraisal'" — loans missing appraisal
  • "Applications WITHOUT Loan__c where Status = Active" — applications with no active loans
  • "Contacts who HAVE Loan_Borrower__c where Loan Status = Funded" — all funded borrowers
  • "Accounts WITHOUT Opportunities WHERE CloseDate is this year" — no closed business this year
Compliance use case

For TRID compliance: "Show all Loans where ClosingDate is in next 3 days WITHOUT a ContentDocumentLink where Title = 'Closing Disclosure'" — loans approaching closing without the required CD document uploaded. This becomes a daily compliance report.

How do you run a Salesforce report from Apex and process the results?REPORTS▼
// Run report synchronously (max 2,000 rows)
Reports.ReportResults results = Reports.ReportManager.runReport('00O5g000004xyzA', true); // true = detail rows

Reports.ReportFactWithDetails facts = (Reports.ReportFactWithDetails) results.getFactMap().get('T!T');
List<Reports.ReportDetailRow> rows = facts.getRows();

for (Reports.ReportDetailRow row : rows) {
  List<Reports.ReportDataCell> cells = row.getDataCells();
  String loanName   = (String)  cells[0].getValue();
  Decimal amount    = (Decimal) cells[1].getValue();
  String status     = (String)  cells[2].getValue();
  System.debug(loanName + ': $' + amount + ' (' + status + ')');
}

// Run asynchronously (for reports >2,000 rows)
String jobId = Reports.ReportManager.runAsyncReport('00O5g000004xyzA', true);
// Poll for completion:
Reports.ReportInstance instance = Reports.ReportManager.getReportInstance(jobId);
while (instance.getStatus() != 'Success') {
  // wait and poll (in practice, use a scheduled job to check)
  instance = Reports.ReportManager.getReportInstance(jobId);
}
Reports.ReportResults asyncResults = instance.getReportResults();
How do you build a report that shows data from custom objects with complex relationships?REPORTS▼

When standard report types don't include the object or relationship you need, create a Custom Report Type (CRT).

  • Step 1 — Setup → Report Types → New Custom Report Type
  • Step 2 — Select primary object: Loan__c
  • Step 3 — Add related objects: Account (borrower), Loan_Document__c (documents), Loan_Officer__r (owner's User record)
  • Step 4 — Choose relationship type: 'A may or may not have B' (outer join — shows loans even without documents)
  • Step 5 — Add fields to layout: drag all fields you want available in reports to the field layout
  • Step 6 — Publish and assign to appropriate profiles
Outer vs Inner join

'A must have B' = inner join — only records with a related record appear. 'A may or may not have B' = outer join — all primary records appear. For reports showing loans regardless of whether they have documents, use 'may or may not have'.

What are Bucket Columns in reports — when are they more useful than formula fields?REPORTS▼

Bucket Columns let you categorise field values into groups directly in the report — without creating a formula field on the object. Available for number, text, and picklist fields.

  • Use Bucket for — ad-hoc grouping that only applies to this report. No object schema change needed.
  • Example: Loan Amount Buckets — Small (<100K), Medium (100K–500K), Large (500K+)
  • Example: Credit Score Tiers — Excellent (750+), Good (700-749), Fair (620-699), Poor (<620)
  • Use Formula Field instead when — grouping is used in many reports, needs to appear on record page, or the calculation is complex
// Bucket Column config in Report Builder (UI only — not in Apex):
// Field: Amount__c
// Bucket name: Loan Size
// Rule 1: Amount__c < 100000 → 'Small'
// Rule 2: Amount__c >= 100000 AND <= 500000 → 'Medium'
// Rule 3: Amount__c > 500000 → 'Large'
// After bucketing: can group by Loan Size and show count/sum per bucket
How do you create a dashboard that refreshes on a schedule and emails to stakeholders?REPORTS▼
  • Dashboard refresh — Dashboards refresh automatically when viewed if last refresh >24h old. For scheduled refresh: Setup → Dashboard → Subscribe → set schedule
