  • Subscribe to dashboard — users can subscribe to receive dashboard snapshots via email. Set frequency: daily/weekly. Sends a PDF snapshot of the dashboard.
  • Report subscriptions — From Report → Subscribe → set schedule and email format. Can send CSV, Excel, or formatted email. Filter conditions: only send if results meet criteria (e.g., only alert if loans past due > 0)
  • Conditional alerts — Reports → Subscribe → Add Filter: 'Run report only if row count > 0'. Useful for exception reporting — only email when there is something to act on.
  • Salesforce Flow scheduled reports — create a Scheduled Flow that calls a Report in Apex and emails results in a custom format with additional business logic
Dashboard data is cached

Dashboards show data from when they were last refreshed — not real-time. If a stakeholder needs live data, point them to the underlying report (always shows current data) or use a custom LWC dashboard connected to @wire.

What is CRM Analytics (Einstein Analytics) — how does it differ from standard Reports?REPORTS▼
FeatureStandard ReportsCRM Analytics
Data limit~250K rows per reportBillions of rows — separate analytics database
Real-timeYes — queries liveNear-real-time — data synced via dataflow
External dataNoYes — connect to external databases, CSV, Salesforce
AI/MLNoBuilt-in predictions, Einstein Discovery
ComponentsCharts, tables, filtersLenses, dashboards, stories, Einstein Predictions
CostIncluded in SalesforceRequires separate license
Developer customizationLimited — UI onlySAQL (custom analytics query language), JSON dashboard config
When CRM Analytics makes sense

When reporting on tens of millions of records, when you need cross-cloud analytics (Salesforce + external data warehouse), when stakeholders want interactive 'slice and dice' exploration rather than static reports.

How do you export Salesforce report data programmatically using the Analytics REST API?REPORTS▼
// Analytics REST API — access reports via HTTP callout (from external system or Apex)
// Endpoint: /services/data/v59.0/analytics/reports/{reportId}
// Must authenticate with OAuth access token

// From external system (Python example pattern):
// GET /services/data/v59.0/analytics/reports/00O5g000004xyzA
// Returns JSON with column metadata and row data

// From Apex (for inter-org or testing scenarios):
HttpRequest req = new HttpRequest();
req.setEndpoint('callout:Self_Named_Credential/services/data/v59.0/analytics/reports/00O5g000004xyzA');
req.setMethod('GET');
req.setHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');
HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req);

Map<String,Object> report = (Map<String,Object>) JSON.deserializeUntyped(res.getBody());
Map<String,Object> factMap = (Map<String,Object>) report.get('factMap');
Map<String,Object> total  = (Map<String,Object>) factMap.get('T!T');
List<Object> rows  = (List<Object>) total.get('rows');

for (Object rowObj : rows) {
  Map<String,Object> row   = (Map<String,Object>) rowObj;
  List<Object> cells = (List<Object>) row.get('dataCells');
  String value = (String) ((Map<String,Object>) cells[0]).get('label');
}
Agentforce — 10 Scenario Questions
Real interview questions about Agentforce for 2025-2026 — architecture, actions, grounding, Trust Layer
What is Agentforce — explain the architecture at a senior developer level?AGENTFORCE▼

Agentforce is Salesforce's autonomous AI agent platform (GA: Fall 2024). Agents can reason, act, and complete multi-step tasks without constant human input. As a developer, you extend agents by building Apex @InvocableMethod actions, Flows, and Prompt Templates.

ComponentWhat It IsDeveloper Builds
AgentAI entity with Role, Goals, Instructions, TopicsConfigure in Agent Builder
LLMThe reasoning engine — GPT-4o, Claude, xGen etc.Select in LLM Gateway
TopicsLogical groups of related Actions (e.g. "Loan Status")Define scope + which actions belong
ActionsWhat agent CAN do — Flow, Apex, CRM, External API@InvocableMethod Apex classes
GroundingHow agent accesses real data — Data Cloud, Knowledge, CRMDesign SOQL access strategy
Einstein Trust LayerPII masking, zero data retention, audit trailConfigure masking rules in Setup
Key developer skill

The most important new skill: write excellent @InvocableMethod descriptions. The description is what the LLM reads to decide WHEN to call your action. Vague description = wrong action called. Write it as: "Use this action when [intent]. Returns [what]. Requires [input]."

How do you build an Apex Action for Agentforce — what makes a good action description?AGENTFORCE▼
public class AgentLoanStatusAction {

    public class Request {
        @InvocableVariable(label='Borrower Email' required=true
            description='Email address of the borrower asking about their loan')
        public String borrowerEmail;
    }

    public class Response {
        @InvocableVariable(label='Status Summary')
        public String statusSummary;
        @InvocableVariable(label='Next Steps')
        public String nextSteps;
        @InvocableVariable(label='Found')
        public Boolean found;
    }

    // THE DESCRIPTION IS CRITICAL — this is what the LLM reads to decide WHEN to call this
    @InvocableMethod(
        label='Get Loan Status for Borrower'
        description='Use this action when a borrower asks about their loan status, application progress, what stage their loan is in, or what happens next. This action looks up the borrower''s active loan by email and returns the current status and next steps. Requires the borrower''s email address.'
        category='Loan Processing'
    )
    public static List<Response> getLoanStatus(List<Request> requests) {
        List<Response> responses = new List<Response>();
        for(Request req : requests) {
            Response resp = new Response();
            List<Loan__c> loans = [
                SELECT Id, Name, Status__c, Next_Steps__c, LoanOfficer__r.Name
                FROM Loan__c
                WHERE BorrowerEmail__c = :req.borrowerEmail
                AND Status__c NOT IN ('Closed', 'Denied')
                WITH USER_MODE
                ORDER BY CreatedDate DESC LIMIT 1
            ];
            if(loans.isEmpty()) {
                resp.found = false;
                resp.statusSummary = 'No active loan application found for this email address.';
                resp.nextSteps = 'Please contact your loan officer or call our main number.';
            } else {
                Loan__c l = loans[0];
                resp.found = true;
                resp.statusSummary = 'Your loan ' + l.Name + ' is currently in ' + l.Status__c + ' status. Your loan officer is ' + l.LoanOfficer__r.Name + '.';
                resp.nextSteps = String.isNotBlank(l.Next_Steps__c) ? l.Next_Steps__c : 'Your loan officer will contact you with the next steps shortly.';
            }
            responses.add(resp);
        }
        return responses;
    }
}
What is Grounding in Agentforce — how does it access real CRM data and why is it important?AGENTFORCE▼

Grounding connects the LLM to real, current data. Without grounding, the LLM only knows what was in its training data — potentially outdated or wrong for your business. Grounding makes responses factually accurate.

  • CRM Grounding: Agent calls a Standard CRM Action or Apex Action that queries Salesforce records. The result is returned as context the LLM reads before generating its response
  • Knowledge Article Grounding: Agent searches your Salesforce Knowledge Base via vector search. Retrieved articles become context for answering policy/FAQ questions accurately
  • Data Cloud Grounding: Agent accesses unified customer profiles and calculated insights from Data Cloud via semantic vector search (RAG — Retrieval Augmented Generation)
  • External Grounding via Apex: Apex Action calls an external API (e.g., FRED for mortgage rates) and returns the data as a string the LLM uses to ground its response in real-time data
Why grounding matters in mortgage

Without grounding, if a borrower asks "What is the current 30-year fixed rate?" the LLM might answer with its training data from 2023. With Apex grounding calling the FRED API, the agent answers with today's actual rate. Grounding is what makes AI responses trustworthy in a regulated financial services context.

What is the Einstein Trust Layer and why is it essential for financial services?AGENTFORCE▼
  • Zero Data Retention: External LLM providers (OpenAI, Anthropic) are contractually prevented from storing or training on Salesforce customer data. Data is used for one response only
  • PII Masking: SSN, credit card numbers, and other PII are automatically detected and replaced with tokens before reaching the LLM. The LLM never sees raw borrower PII
  • Toxicity Detection: LLM output is scanned before shown to users. Harmful content is blocked
  • Audit Trail: All AI interactions are logged in Salesforce for compliance review. For ECOA/FCRA regulated environments, this audit trail is required
  • Data Residency: Data stays within configured geographic boundaries — EU data doesn't leave EU
// Configure PII masking in Setup → Einstein → Einstein Trust Layer → Data Masking Rules
// Add custom rule for sensitive fields:
// Object: Loan__c, Field: SSN__c → Masking: Replace with [MASKED_SSN]

// What LLM receives instead of real data:
// Original: "Borrower SSN: 123-45-6789, FICO: 720"
// After masking: "Borrower SSN: [MASKED_SSN], FICO: 720"
// The LLM can still answer about FICO but never sees the actual SSN

// Query audit trail:
List<EinsteinAIAuditEvent> auditLog = [
    SELECT Id, UserId, ActionType, CreatedDate
    FROM EinsteinAIAuditEvent
    WHERE CreatedDate = TODAY
    ORDER BY CreatedDate DESC
];
What are the current limitations of Agentforce a developer should know for interviews?AGENTFORCE▼
  • Response latency: Agent reasoning + grounding + LLM generation adds 2–10 seconds. Not suitable for real-time sub-second interactions
  • Non-deterministic: Same input may produce slightly different outputs. Critical business logic must remain in deterministic Apex/Flow — not in LLM reasoning
  • Hallucination risk: Even with grounding, LLMs can occasionally produce incorrect information. Always validate critical outputs
  • Context window limits: Very long conversations or large grounded documents may exceed LLM context window, causing truncation
  • No direct DML: The LLM itself doesn't write to Salesforce. It calls Actions, which then perform DML. This adds a step but maintains data integrity
  • Einstein AI credits: High-volume deployments need capacity planning — each agent interaction consumes credits
  • Testing challenges: Non-deterministic behavior means more end-to-end testing needed. Test Apex actions independently (they're just InvocableMethods) and test full agent flows in Agent Builder sandbox
How does Agentforce determine which action to call — explain topics and instructions?AGENTFORCE SCENARIOS▼

Agent Topics are categories of user intent. Each topic has natural language instructions telling the agent when to handle that type of request.

  • Topic — 'Loan Status Inquiries'. Instructions: 'Handle when user asks about loan status, loan progress, what stage their loan is in, or when their loan will close.'
  • Agent Actions within a Topic — GetLoanStatus, GetEstimatedCloseDate, GetRequiredDocuments. The agent picks the right action based on the user's specific ask.
  • Topic instructions format — natural language, 1-2 sentences per instruction. Tell the agent what the topic covers, what it should NOT handle (hand-off triggers), and how to behave.
  • Example boundary instruction — 'If the user asks about rates, interest calculations, or pre-approval decisions, escalate to a human loan officer rather than answering.'
  • Tone instructions — 'Always address the user by first name. Be empathetic when delivering declined or on-hold status. Never speculate about approval likelihood.'
Good topic design

Well-defined topics with clear boundaries prevent hallucination. If the agent knows exactly what it should and should not handle, it stays within its lane and escalates appropriately rather than guessing.

What is the difference between Agentforce Service Agent, Sales Agent, and custom agents?AGENTFORCE SCENARIOS▼
Agent TypePrimary UsePre-built TopicsCustom?
Service AgentCustomer service — answer FAQs, case status, routingCase status, FAQ answering, human escalationAdd custom topics + actions
Sales Agent (SDR)Prospect outreach, follow-up, pipeline managementEmail drafting, meeting scheduling, lead qualificationAdd custom topics + actions
Copilot (Employee-facing)Internal productivity — summarize, draft, lookupRecord summaries, email drafting, task creationHighly customizable
Custom Agent (from scratch)Fully bespoke — your own persona, topics, actionsNone — you define everythingFully custom
Start with pre-built

In an interview, show you know the pre-built agents exist and their use cases. Demonstrate you'd evaluate pre-built first before building from scratch — shows business judgment. Custom agents require more maintenance.

How do you test and evaluate an Agentforce agent before going to production?AGENTFORCE SCENARIOS▼
  • Agent Builder Testing panel — in Setup → Agent Builder, test conversations directly. See which topic was selected, which action was called, and what data was returned.
  • Test conversation transcripts — run 20+ realistic test conversations covering expected user inputs, edge cases, and out-of-scope queries. Verify the agent handles each correctly.
  • Boundary testing — deliberately ask questions outside the agent's topics. Verify it escalates rather than hallucinating an answer.
  • Action testing — for each Apex Action, verify: correct data returned, handles 'not found' gracefully, FLS respected (agent running as correct user context), no SOQL/DML errors.
  • User acceptance testing — deploy to a sandbox, have actual loan officers test realistic questions. Their natural language will be different from what the developer tested.
  • Monitoring in production — use Conversation Logs (Setup → Bot Conversation Logs) to review real conversations. Identify patterns where the agent fails and refine topics/instructions.
What is Einstein Copilot for Developers (Code Generation) — how does it work?AGENTFORCE SCENARIOS▼

Einstein for Developers is an AI coding assistant built into VS Code (Salesforce Extension Pack) and the Developer Console. It generates Apex, LWC, SOQL, and test code from natural language.

  • Generate Apex from comment — write a comment describing what you want, press a shortcut, get code. Example: /* Create a method that finds all loans past due date and updates status to Late */
  • Explain code — select code → ask Einstein to explain it. Useful for understanding inherited code.
  • Generate test class — select an Apex class → ask Einstein to generate a test class with positive, negative, and bulk test cases.
  • Fix errors — paste a compile error → Einstein suggests the fix.
  • SOQL generation — describe what you want to query in plain English → get SOQL.
Always review AI-generated code

Einstein-generated code may have security issues (missing WITH SECURITY_ENFORCED), performance issues (SOQL in loops), or logic errors. Treat it as a starting draft, not a finished solution. Run code review and tests as normal.

How would you design an Agentforce agent for a mortgage company — complete architecture?AGENTFORCE SCENARIOS▼

Business requirement: Borrowers need self-service access to loan status, document requirements, and appointment scheduling — currently handled by 3 loan officers spending 2 hours each per day on these repetitive queries.

Agent design:

  • Agent persona — 'Mortgage Assistant'. Friendly, professional, empathetic. Always addresses borrower by first name.
  • Topic 1: Loan Status — Action: GetLoanStatus (Apex). Input: loan number or borrower name. Output: status, stage, next steps, estimated close date.
  • Topic 2: Document Requirements — Action: GetRequiredDocuments (Apex). Input: loan ID. Output: list of required documents, which are received, which are outstanding.
  • Topic 3: Appointment Scheduling — Action: GetAvailableSlots + ScheduleAppointment (Apex). Integrates with loan officer calendar.
  • Topic 4: Out of Scope — Escalation topic. Any question about rates, approval decisions, legal advice → 'I'll connect you with your loan officer for that.'
  • Channel — Messaging for In-App and Web (Experience Cloud portal), SMS via Salesforce Messaging.
  • Grounding — Agent queries Loan__c, Borrower__c, Loan_Document__c via Apex Actions. No hallucination risk on factual data.
ROI framing for interview

Frame the design in business terms: 'This agent handles 80% of routine borrower inquiries, freeing loan officers to focus on complex cases and new applications — reducing cost per loan and improving borrower NPS.'

Architecture & Mixed Scenarios — 10 Questions
Senior-level architectural decision questions — explain your reasoning, not just the answer
How do you decide between Flow vs Apex Trigger vs Process Builder for a new automation requirement?ARCHITECTURE▼
// DECISION FRAMEWORK — ask these questions in order:

// 1. Is this logic admin-maintainable and simple enough for Flow?
//    YES + small data volumes → USE FLOW (Record-Triggered)
//    YES but complex logic → CONSIDER Apex with @InvocableMethod from Flow

// 2. Does it involve bulk operations (200+ records at once)?
//    YES → USE APEX TRIGGER (Flow is risky at scale)

// 3. Does it require external API callouts?
//    YES → USE APEX (Queueable from trigger, or @InvocableMethod from Flow)

// 4. Is performance critical?
//    YES → USE APEX (triggers are faster than Flow for bulk operations)

// 5. Is it Process Builder or Workflow?
//    ALWAYS MIGRATE TO FLOW — both are deprecated/retiring

// NEVER use:
// ❌ Process Builder for new logic — deprecated, replacing with Flow
// ❌ Workflow Rules for new logic — retiring 2025, replace with Flow

// Summary table:
// Simple field default on same record → Before Save Flow (fastest)
// Send notification email → After Save Flow or Apex
// Create related record → After Save Flow or After trigger
// Call external API → Apex Queueable (from trigger) or Invocable (from Flow)
// Process 1000+ records at once → Apex Trigger + Batch
When do you choose @future vs Queueable vs Batch vs Scheduled Apex — complete decision matrix?ARCHITECTURE▼
Async TypeUse WhenCannot DoBest For
@futureSimple callout after trigger DML. Mixed DML fix.sObject params. Chaining. No monitoring.Quick fire-and-forget async
QueueableNeed sObject params. Chaining jobs. Job monitoring.More complex setup than @futureCredit check → OFAC → DocuSign chain
BatchProcessing thousands to millions of recordsSlower to start than QueueableNightly loan status updates, mass recalculation
ScheduledRecurring timed jobs (nightly, weekly)Event-driven — only time-based triggerSchedule a Batch job to run nightly
// Combined pattern most used in mortgage systems:
// Scheduled → starts Batch → Batch chains Queueable for callouts

// Scheduled — runs at 2 AM nightly
public class NightlyLoanSchedule implements Schedulable {
    public void execute(SchedulableContext ctx) {
        Database.executeBatch(new LoanStatusBatch(), 200);
    }
}

// Batch — processes all active loans
public class LoanStatusBatch implements Database.Batchable<SObject>, Database.Stateful {
    public Integer processed = 0;
    public Database.QueryLocator start(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
        return Database.getQueryLocator('SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c = \'Active\'');
    }
    public void execute(Database.BatchableContext bc, List<SObject> scope) {
        processed += scope.size();
        // Update statuses
    }
    public void finish(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
        // Chain Queueable for post-batch notification callout
        System.enqueueJob(new BatchCompleteNotificationQueueable(processed));
    }
}
How do you design the sharing model for a mortgage company with branch offices, roles, and broker partners?ARCHITECTURE▼
  • Step 1 — OWD: Loan__c = Private. Loan officers only see their own loans by default. This is the most restrictive correct starting point.
  • Step 2 — Role Hierarchy: CEO → Regional VP → Branch Manager → Senior Loan Officer → Loan Officer → Loan Processor. Records visible UP the hierarchy — Branch Manager sees all loans under their branch automatically.
  • Step 3 — Sharing Rules: Criteria-based: "Share all Loans in Underwriting status with the Compliance Team (public group) — Read Only." Ownership-based: "Share loans owned by the Southeast Region role with Southeast Branch Managers."
  • Step 4 — Broker Partner Access: External broker partners need access to their specific loans only. Use Apex Managed Sharing — when a loan is assigned to a broker partner user, create a Loan__Share record with the partner's user ID. Remove the share when the broker is replaced.
  • Step 5 — Experience Cloud site: If brokers access through Experience Cloud, configure the site's sharing settings. Experience Cloud users need at least Read on Loan__c object, plus record-level access via sharing.
Architecture principle

Always start with the most restrictive OWD and open up access — never start with Public and try to restrict down. Every access grant should have a clear, documented business justification that maps to FCRA and data privacy requirements.

How would you architect a bidirectional sync between Salesforce and an external Loan Origination System?ARCHITECTURE▼

Salesforce → LOS (outbound):

  • After Save Record-Triggered Flow or Apex trigger detects change on Loan__c
  • Publishes Loan_Sync_Request__e Platform Event (decouples the loan save from LOS call)
  • Platform Event subscriber trigger enqueues Queueable job
  • Queueable makes REST callout to LOS API — updates loan record in LOS
  • On failure: writes to Sync_Retry_Queue__c custom object. Scheduled Apex retries failed syncs every 15 minutes up to 3 attempts

LOS → Salesforce (inbound):

  • LOS sends webhook to Salesforce REST endpoint: POST /services/apexrest/v1/loanSync
  • Apex @RestResource validates HMAC signature (security), upserts using LOS_ID__c External ID
  • Returns HTTP 200 on success, 400 on bad payload, 500 on error

Conflict resolution: Use Last_Sync_Source__c field (LOS or SFDC) and Last_Sync_Timestamp__c. Business rule: Salesforce wins for status changes, LOS wins for rate locks and financial figures.

How do you handle Large Data Volumes (50M records) in a Salesforce org — design considerations?ARCHITECTURE▼
  • Selective SOQL queries: Every query on large objects must use indexed fields in WHERE clause. Indexed by default: Id, Name, OwnerId, Master-Detail fields, External IDs, fields marked as indexed in setup
  • Query Plan Tool: Developer Console → run EXPLAIN in front of any SOQL. "TableScan" on a large object = that query will be slow. Fix: add indexed field to WHERE clause
  • Avoid LIKE '%text%' on large objects: This forces a full table scan. Use SOSL for text search instead — it uses a search index
  • Skinny Tables: Contact Salesforce support for very frequently queried large objects. Skinny tables are optimized copies of specific field combinations — dramatically faster for those specific queries
  • Archiving with Big Objects: Move records older than 2 years to a Big Object (can store billions of records cheaply). Historical queries go to Big Object, operational queries go to standard Loan__c
  • Batch scope sizing: For 50M records: Database.executeBatch(job, 200). QueryLocator supports up to 50M rows. Never try to UPDATE 50M records in one transaction — always use Batch
  • Hard delete for cleanup: Soft-deleted records still count against storage. Run Database.emptyRecycleBin() or schedule regular recycle bin cleanup
What is Salesforce DX and SFDX CLI — how does it change your development workflow?ARCHITECTURE▼

Salesforce DX is a source-driven development methodology with CLI tooling. Key concepts:

  • Scratch Orgs: Disposable developer orgs. Create/delete in minutes. No more shared sandboxes with conflicts. Each developer gets their own isolated environment
  • Source Format: Metadata stored as individual files (not monolithic XML). Works properly with Git — meaningful diffs, proper merge conflict resolution
  • Salesforce CLI (sf): Command-line interface for all development operations — deploy, retrieve, run tests, create scratch orgs
  • CI/CD: Integrates with GitHub Actions, Copado, Gearset for automated testing and deployment pipelines
# Key daily commands:
sf org login web --alias myDevOrg           # authenticate
sf org create scratch --definition-file config/project-scratch-def.json --alias myScratch --duration-days 7
sf project deploy start                      # push local → scratch org
sf project retrieve start                    # pull changes ← scratch org
sf apex run test --synchronous               # run all tests
sf apex run test --class-names LoanTriggerTest --synchronous  # specific test class
sf project deploy start --target-org prodAlias --test-level RunLocalTests  # deploy to prod
How do you approach performance testing before a large Salesforce deployment?ARCHITECTURE▼
  • Query Plan analysis: Run all SOQL from triggers and LWC wire calls through Developer Console with EXPLAIN. Fix any TableScan before deployment
  • Bulk trigger test at 200 records: ALWAYS test triggers inserting exactly 200 records. If test only uses 1 record, governor limit issues will not surface until production
  • Batch at scale in Full Sandbox: Full Sandbox = copy of production data. Run batch with scope=1, then scope=50, then scope=200. Monitor governor limit consumption at each step
  • LWC with realistic data: Test datatable components with the maximum realistic row count (100, 500, 1000 rows). A datatable with 1000 rows renders very differently than one with 10
  • Limits.getCpuTime() profiling: Add CPU time checks at key points in complex Apex to identify bottlenecks before they hit the 10,000ms limit in production
  • Debug log analysis: Enable debug logs during load tests. Look for: slow queries (>200ms), repeated queries inside loops, unexpected governor consumption
// CPU time profiling in Apex
Long startCpu = Limits.getCpuTime();
// ... some operation ...
Long elapsed = Limits.getCpuTime() - startCpu;
System.debug('CPU used for operation: ' + elapsed + 'ms of ' + Limits.getLimitCpuTime() + 'ms total');
How do you manage technical debt in an existing Salesforce org with outdated automation?ARCHITECTURE▼
  • Audit with Salesforce Optimizer: Run the free Salesforce Optimizer report (Setup → Optimizer). It identifies unused fields, inactive flows, low-coverage Apex, duplicate rules, excessive objects
  • Migrate Process Builder and Workflow to Flow: Both are deprecated. Salesforce retirement dates are announced — start migration before forced retirement causes failures
  • Refactor triggers to handler pattern: Any org with logic directly in .trigger files (not handler classes) is a debt item. Prioritize the most-changed objects first
  • Coverage baseline: Any Apex class below 75% coverage = untested code that will fail. Treat each low-coverage class as a debt bug to fix
  • Dead code removal: Use "Where is this used?" for custom fields. Fields used in 0 automations, 0 layouts, 0 reports can be candidates for removal (verify with business first)
  • Tech debt as backlog items: Frame debt in business terms — "Refactoring Account trigger reduces deployment time from 4 hours to 45 minutes due to eliminated merge conflicts"
  • Dedicated cleanup time: Reserve 10–20% of each sprint for debt reduction. Without dedicated time, debt only accumulates
How do you stay current with Salesforce releases as a senior developer?ARCHITECTURE▼

Salesforce releases 3 major updates per year: Spring (February), Summer (June), Winter (October/November).

  • Release Notes: Read for every release. Focus on: Apex API changes, LWC new capabilities, Flow enhancements, deprecated features and their timelines
  • Pre-release orgs: Salesforce makes preview orgs available 4–6 weeks before each release. Test existing code against the new release before it hits production
  • Trailhead Release modules: 1–2 new Trailhead modules released with each major release — completing them is the fastest way to learn what changed
  • Certification maintenance: Salesforce certs require annual maintenance exams for each release. These force you to learn what changed — make them part of your professional development
  • Salesforce Developer Blog: Official technical announcements. Follow on Trailblazer Community. Subscribe to the developer newsletter
  • Deprecation tracking: Keep a personal deprecation timeline — when does Process Builder retire? When does With SECURITY_ENFORCED become the wrong choice? Plan migrations proactively
Interview answer

Say: "I stay current through the official release notes and Salesforce Developer Blog, and I test major features in sandbox before they reach production. I also track the Process Builder and Workflow deprecation timeline because we have existing automations that need migration to Flow — I want to stay ahead of forced retirements rather than scramble at the deadline."

Design a real-time loan status notification system from scratch — architect the complete solutionARCHITECTURE▼

Requirements: send email, SMS, and push notifications when loan status changes. Multiple loan types. Configurable rules per status change.

Architecture decision — Why NOT direct in trigger: The trigger would need to know about every notification channel, every loan type's rules, and every recipient configuration. That is too tightly coupled.

Decoupled design:

  • Trigger: After update on Loan__c — if Status__c changed → publish Loan_Status_Changed__e Platform Event (loanId, oldStatus, newStatus). Nothing else in the trigger.
  • Configuration: Notification_Config__mdt (Custom Metadata) — rows defining: LoanType, FromStatus, ToStatus, Channels (Email/SMS/Push), RecipientType (Borrower/LO/Manager). No code change needed to add/change rules.
  • Router class: Platform Event trigger subscribes to Loan_Status_Changed__e. Queries Notification_Config__mdt for matching rules. For each matching rule, calls the appropriate channel adapter via INotificationChannel interface.
  • Channel adapters: EmailAdapter (Salesforce Messaging), SMSAdapter (Twilio via Named Credential callout), PushAdapter (Salesforce Notification Builder).
  • Error handling: Every notification attempt logged to Notification_Log__c. Failed sends retried by scheduled Apex up to 3 times.
Patterns demonstrated

Platform Events (decoupling), Custom Metadata (configuration-driven, deploy without code change), Strategy Pattern (INotificationChannel), Error logging, Retry logic. This answer shows senior architect thinking — decoupling, configuration-driven design, error handling, retry logic.

Company Interview Q&A — Arago & Morgan Stanley
Real questions from actual interviews. Study these patterns — interviewers at different companies often ask the same core questions with slight variations.

⟩ ARAGO — Salesforce Developer Interview (4 Years Experience)

How do you control trigger execution order if multiple triggers exist on the same object?ARAGO▼

Salesforce does NOT guarantee execution order when multiple triggers exist on the same object. The only correct solution is to maintain one trigger per object and use a Trigger Framework.

Framework structure: Trigger → Handler → Service → Helper → DAO

  • One .trigger file per object — it is a dispatcher only, contains zero logic
  • TriggerHandler class routes events: onBeforeInsert, onAfterUpdate etc.
  • Service classes contain the actual business logic, called from the handler
  • Helper/DAO classes handle queries and utility operations
// The ONLY correct answer — one trigger, handler pattern
trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (before insert, before update, after insert, after update) {
    new LoanTriggerHandler().run(); // dispatcher — zero logic here
}

// Handler routes to the right method
public class LoanTriggerHandler extends TriggerHandler {
    private List<Loan__c> newLoans = (List<Loan__c>) Trigger.new;
    private Map<Id,Loan__c> oldMap  = (Map<Id,Loan__c>) Trigger.oldMap;

    public override void onBeforeInsert() { LoanValidationService.validate(newLoans); }
    public override void onAfterUpdate()  { LoanStatusService.handleChange(newLoans, oldMap); }
}
Interview answer

Say: 'Salesforce doesn't guarantee order across multiple triggers, so I always enforce one trigger per object using a handler framework. Within the framework I control execution order through method call sequence in the handler class.'

How do you handle bulk insert/update operations efficiently in triggers?ARAGO▼

Core rule: zero SOQL and zero DML inside any loop.

// BAD — hits governor limits with 101+ records
trigger BadTrigger on Loan__c (after insert) {
    for (Loan__c loan : Trigger.new) {
        Account acc = [SELECT Id, Loan_Count__c FROM Account WHERE Id = :loan.Account__c]; // SOQL IN LOOP!
        acc.Loan_Count__c++;
        update acc; // DML IN LOOP!
    }
}

// GOOD — bulkified correctly
trigger GoodTrigger on Loan__c (after insert) {
    // 1. Collect all IDs first
    Set<Id> accountIds = new Set<Id>();
    for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) if (l.Account__c != null) accountIds.add(l.Account__c);

    // 2. ONE SOQL for all records
    Map<Id, Account> accountMap = new Map<Id, Account>(
        [SELECT Id, Loan_Count__c FROM Account WHERE Id IN :accountIds]
    );

    // 3. Process in memory
    for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new)
        if (accountMap.containsKey(l.Account__c))
            accountMap.get(l.Account__c).Loan_Count__c++;

    // 4. ONE DML for all accounts
    update accountMap.values();
}
  • Collect all needed IDs into a Set before querying
  • Use Map<Id, SObject> for O(1) lookups — never nested loops
  • Query once outside the loop with WHERE Id IN :mySet
  • Collect all records to update in a List, then single DML after loop
  • Test always with exactly 200 records — this is when governor limits surface
Explain the difference between before and after triggers with examples.ARAGO▼
Before TriggerAfter Trigger
When it runsBefore record is saved to DBAfter record is saved to DB
Record ID available?No (on insert)Yes — always
Can modify Trigger.new?Yes — no extra DML neededNo — must use DML to update
Use forSet defaults, validate, derive fields on same recordCreate related records, send notifications, callouts
Extra DML cost?No — changes saved with the recordYes — separate DML statement needed
// BEFORE INSERT — set default field (no extra DML)
trigger LoanBefore on Loan__c (before insert) {
    for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) {
        if (l.Interest_Rate__c == null) l.Interest_Rate__c = 6.5; // set directly — free
        if (l.Application_Date__c == null) l.Application_Date__c = Date.today();
    }
}

// AFTER INSERT — create related record (needs DML — ID is now available)
trigger LoanAfter on Loan__c (after insert) {
    List<Loan_Checklist__c> checklists = new List<Loan_Checklist__c>();
    for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) {
        checklists.add(new Loan_Checklist__c(Loan__c = l.Id)); // l.Id available after insert
    }
    insert checklists;
}
How can you prevent recursion in triggers?ARAGO▼

Recursion happens when a trigger's DML fires the trigger again — infinite loop until CPU limit is hit.

Pattern 1 — Simple Boolean flag:

public class TriggerHelper {
    public static Boolean loanTriggerRan = false;
}

trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (after update) {
    if (TriggerHelper.loanTriggerRan) return; // exit if already ran this transaction
    TriggerHelper.loanTriggerRan = true;
    LoanTriggerHandler.onAfterUpdate(Trigger.new, Trigger.oldMap);
    // flag stays true for rest of transaction — prevents re-entry
}

Pattern 2 — Set of processed IDs (handles workflow re-entry per record):

public class TriggerHelper {
    public static Set<Id> processedIds = new Set<Id>();
}

trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (after update) {
    List<Loan__c> toProcess = new List<Loan__c>();
    for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) {
        if (!TriggerHelper.processedIds.contains(l.Id)) {
            toProcess.add(l);
            TriggerHelper.processedIds.add(l.Id);
        }
    }
    if (!toProcess.isEmpty()) LoanTriggerHandler.onAfterUpdate(toProcess, Trigger.oldMap);
}
Pattern 2 is better

Pattern 1 blocks all re-entry. Pattern 2 allows the trigger to re-run for NEW records that haven't been processed yet — important when a transaction involves multiple sets of records.

What is a trigger execution context and what context variables are available?ARAGO▼

The trigger execution context defines what DML event fired the trigger and which phase (before/after) is currently executing. Salesforce provides Boolean context variables to detect this.

VariableTypeUse to detect
Trigger.isInsertBooleanINSERT operation
Trigger.isUpdateBooleanUPDATE operation
Trigger.isDeleteBooleanDELETE operation
Trigger.isUndeleteBooleanUNDELETE operation
Trigger.isBeforeBooleanBefore phase — record not yet saved
Trigger.isAfterBooleanAfter phase — record saved
Trigger.newList<SObject>New/updated record values
Trigger.oldList<SObject>Old record values (update/delete only)
Trigger.newMapMap<Id,SObject>Id to new record map
Trigger.oldMapMap<Id,SObject>Id to old record map
Trigger.sizeIntegerTotal records in this trigger batch
// Using context variables correctly
trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (before insert, after update) {
    if (Trigger.isBefore && Trigger.isInsert) {
        // Set defaults — Trigger.new is writable here
        for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) l.Status__c = 'Applied';
    }
    if (Trigger.isAfter && Trigger.isUpdate) {
        // Detect field change using oldMap
        for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) {
            if (l.Status__c != Trigger.oldMap.get(l.Id).Status__c) {
                // Status changed — do something
            }
        }
    }
}
How would you structure a complete Trigger Framework?ARAGO▼

Layer structure: Trigger → Handler → Service → Helper/DAO

// Layer 1: Trigger — dispatcher only, one per object
trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (before insert, before update, after insert, after update, after delete) {
    new LoanTriggerHandler().run();
}

// Layer 2: Handler — routes events, extends virtual base
public class LoanTriggerHandler extends TriggerHandler {
    private List<Loan__c> newLoans = (List<Loan__c>) Trigger.new;
    private Map<Id,Loan__c> oldMap  = (Map<Id,Loan__c>) Trigger.oldMap;

    public override void onBeforeInsert() {
        LoanValidationService.validate(newLoans);
        LoanDefaultsService.setDefaults(newLoans);
    }
    public override void onAfterUpdate() {
        LoanStatusService.handleStatusChange(newLoans, oldMap);
        LoanNotificationService.notifyOnApproval(newLoans, oldMap);
    }
}

// Layer 3: Service — business logic (reusable from anywhere)
public with sharing class LoanStatusService {
    public static void handleStatusChange(List<Loan__c> loans, Map<Id,Loan__c> oldMap) {
        List<Loan__c> changed = new List<Loan__c>();
        for (Loan__c l : loans)
            if (l.Status__c != oldMap.get(l.Id).Status__c) changed.add(l);
        if (!changed.isEmpty()) LoanSyncHelper.syncToLOS(changed);
    }
}

// Layer 4: Helper/DAO — SOQL queries and utility methods
public class LoanSyncHelper {
    public static void syncToLOS(List<Loan__c> loans) {
        Set<Id> ids = new Map<Id,Loan__c>(loans).keySet();
        List<Loan__c> fullLoans = [SELECT Id, Status__c, External_Id__c FROM Loan__c WHERE Id IN :ids];
        // callout logic
    }
}
Separation of concerns

Each layer has one job. The trigger dispatches. The handler routes. The service holds business rules. The DAO queries data. When requirements change, you modify only the relevant layer — nothing else breaks.

When would you choose Flow over Apex — and when would you choose Apex over Flow?ARAGO▼
ScenarioChoose FlowChoose Apex
Simple field update on record save✓ Before-Save flow — no DML costOverkill
Send email on status change✓ After-Save flow + email actionPossible but more code
Process 1M+ records in bulkNo✓ Batch Apex
External system callout✓ After-Save async path✓ Queueable or @future
Complex conditional logicLimited✓ Apex has full language power
Non-developer to maintain✓ Flow is clicks, no deploymentTechnical risk
CPU-heavy calculationMay hit limits✓ Apex with async option
Needs unit test coverageNo tests needed✓ Required, but ensures quality

Real scenario from interview answer:

A Flow was failing with CPU limit errors during a large data load (10,000 records updated via Data Loader). Flow is not designed for bulk operations from external tools. Replaced the After-Save Flow with a Batch Apex job triggered by a Platform Event — resolved the CPU limit issue completely and added retry logic.

How do you avoid SOQL injection in dynamic queries?ARAGO▼

SOQL injection is the same class of vulnerability as SQL injection — user-controlled input manipulates the query structure to return unauthorized data.

// VULNERABLE — never do this:
String userInput = ApexPages.currentPage().getParameters().get('status');
String query = 'SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c = '' + userInput + ''';
// Attack: userInput = "' OR Id != null OR Status__c = '"
// Result: returns ALL loans — data breach!

// FIX 1 — Bind variables (best, always prefer)
List<Loan__c> loans = Database.query('SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c = :userInput');
// Bind variables are always safe — never interpolated into the string

// FIX 2 — escapeSingleQuotes (when bind vars not possible)
String safe = String.escapeSingleQuotes(userInput);
String query = 'SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c = '' + safe + ''';

// FIX 3 — Validate against allowlist before using in query
Set<String> validStatuses = new Set<String>{'Applied', 'Approved', 'Funded', 'Declined'};
if (!validStatuses.contains(userInput)) throw new QueryException('Invalid status');
Rule of thumb

If a string came from any user-controlled source (URL parameter, LWC input, API request body) — NEVER concatenate it directly into a SOQL query. Always bind or escape.

What is the difference between SOQL and SOSL?ARAGO▼
FeatureSOQLSOSL
Full nameSalesforce Object Query LanguageSalesforce Object Search Language
SearchesOne object at a timeMultiple objects simultaneously
Index typeDatabase columnsFull-text search index
WildcardsTrailing % only in LIKELeading and trailing * supported
Governor limit100 sync / 200 async20 sync / 100 async
Best forStructured queries with WHERE filtersFree-text search (like a search bar)
ReturnsList<SObject>List<List<SObject>>
// SOQL — query specific object with conditions
List<Loan__c> loans = [SELECT Id, Name, Status__c FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c = 'Active' AND OwnerId = :userId];

// SOSL — search 'Johnson' across Contact AND Lead simultaneously
List<List<SObject>> results = [
    FIND 'Johnson*' IN NAME FIELDS
    RETURNING Contact(Id, Name, Email), Lead(Id, Name, Company)
    LIMIT 20
];
List<Contact> contacts = (List<Contact>) results[0];
List<Lead>    leads    = (List<Lead>)    results[1];
Interview answer

Say: 'I use SOQL when I know the exact object and field to filter on. I use SOSL when I need to search a user-typed keyword across multiple objects or multiple text fields simultaneously — like a global search feature.'

How do you query parent-child relationships in SOQL?ARAGO▼
// Child → Parent (dot notation — up to 5 levels)
SELECT Id, Name, Account__r.Name, Account__r.Owner.Name
FROM Loan__c
WHERE Status__c = 'Active'
// Access: loan.Account__r.Name

// Parent → Child (subquery in SELECT)
SELECT Id, Name,
       (SELECT Id, Name, Status__c, Amount__c FROM Loans__r)  // child relationship name
FROM Account
WHERE Id IN :accountIds
// Access: account.Loans__r — returns List<Loan__c>

// Custom vs Standard relationship naming:
// Custom lookup field: Account__c on Loan__c → parent: Account__r, child: Loans__r
// Standard field: AccountId on Contact → parent: Account, child: Contacts (no __r)

// Example: Account with Contacts (standard relationship)
SELECT Id, Name, (SELECT Id, Name, Email FROM Contacts) FROM Account
What is the difference between Custom Metadata Types and Custom Settings?ARAGO▼
FeatureCustom Metadata (CMDT)Custom Settings
Included in deployments?Yes — deployed with change sets/packagesNo — data stays in org
SOQL governor limits?No — free query (cached)No — in-memory cache
Subscriber package?YesYes (List type only)
Use from Formula fields?YesYes (Hierarchy type)
Best forConfig deployed with code: rate tables, API endpoints, feature flagsOrg/user preferences not shipped with code
// Custom Metadata — no SOQL limit cost, deployed with code
Loan_Config__mdt config = [SELECT Max_Amount__c, Base_Rate__c FROM Loan_Config__mdt
    WHERE Loan_Type__c = 'FHA' LIMIT 1]; // does NOT count against 100 SOQL limit

// Custom Settings — also cached, but not deployable with code
Loan_Settings__c settings = Loan_Settings__c.getOrgDefaults();
Decimal maxAmount = settings.Max_Loan_Amount__c;
Modern recommendation

Always prefer Custom Metadata over Custom Settings for new implementations. CMDT is deployable, package-friendly, supports approval/versioning in source control, and works in sandboxes identically to production.

What is the difference between DML statements and Database class methods?ARAGO▼
FeatureDML StatementDatabase Method
Syntaxinsert myList;Database.insert(myList, false)
On failureThrows exception — ALL records rollbackPartial success — failed records logged
ReturnsvoidList<Database.SaveResult>
Error accesscatch (DmlException e)result.getErrors()
Use whenAll records must succeed togetherSome records may fail — log and continue
// DML — all or nothing
try {
    insert loanList; // if ANY record fails, ALL rollback
} catch (DmlException e) {
    System.debug('Failed: ' + e.getDmlMessage(0));
}

// Database method — partial success
List<Database.SaveResult> results = Database.insert(loanList, false); // false = allow partial
for (Integer i = 0; i < results.size(); i++) {
    if (!results[i].isSuccess()) {
        String err = results[i].getErrors()[0].getMessage();
        insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c = err, Loan__c = loanList[i].Id);
    }
}
What is a Savepoint and when do you use Database.rollback()?ARAGO▼

A Savepoint marks a point in a transaction. If something fails later, you can rollback to that point — undoing all DML that happened after the savepoint was set.

// Pattern: try a multi-step operation, rollback to savepoint if any step fails
Savepoint sp = Database.setSavepoint(); // mark this point

try {
    Loan__c loan = new Loan__c(Status__c='Processing', Amount__c=250000);
    insert loan; // DML 1

    LoanDocument__c doc = new LoanDocument__c(Loan__c=loan.Id, Type__c='Application');
    insert doc;  // DML 2

    makeExternalCallout(loan.Id); // might throw CalloutException

} catch (Exception e) {
    Database.rollback(sp); // undo BOTH inserts — back to the savepoint state
    // Can still do DML after rollback in the same transaction
    insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c='Loan creation failed: ' + e.getMessage());
}
Savepoints + callouts

You cannot use a savepoint after a callout. And you cannot make a callout after DML in the same transaction. Order must be: callout → then DML. Or use @future/Queueable to separate them.

Explain OOP concepts in Apex with Salesforce examples.ARAGO▼
ConceptDefinitionSalesforce Example
EncapsulationBundle data + methods together; control access with modifiersprivate fields in LoanService with public methods only
InheritanceChild class extends parent, inherits and can override behaviourLoanTriggerHandler extends TriggerHandler
PolymorphismOne interface, multiple implementations used interchangeablyILoanProcessor: ConventionalProcessor, FHAProcessor, VAProcessor
AbstractionHide complexity, expose only what's neededLoanApplicationFacade.submit() hides 6 service calls
// Encapsulation
public class LoanService {
    private Decimal baseRate = 6.5; // private — hidden
    public Decimal getRate() { return baseRate; } // controlled access

// Inheritance
public class LoanTriggerHandler extends TriggerHandler { // inherits run()
    public override void onBeforeInsert() { /* custom logic */ }
}

// Polymorphism — interface with multiple implementations
public interface ILoanProcessor { void validate(Loan__c l); }
public class FHAProcessor implements ILoanProcessor {
    public void validate(Loan__c l) { if (l.Credit_Score__c < 580) l.addError('FHA needs 580+'); }
}
public class ConventionalProcessor implements ILoanProcessor {
    public void validate(Loan__c l) { if (l.Credit_Score__c < 620) l.addError('Conventional needs 620+'); }
}
// Caller uses interface — doesn't know which processor:
ILoanProcessor proc = LoanProcessorFactory.get(loan.Loan_Type__c);
proc.validate(loan); // polymorphic call
What are the types of sandboxes and their key differences?ARAGO▼
Sandbox TypeStorageData CopiedRefresh IntervalBest For
Developer200 MB data, 200 MB filesNo data1 dayIndividual developer coding
Developer Pro1 GB data, 1 GB filesNo data1 dayLarger development/testing
Partial Copy5 GB dataSample (up to 10K records per object)5 daysQA, integration testing
FullSame as productionAll data29 daysUAT, performance, load testing

You cannot create a Sandbox in a Developer Edition org — Developer Orgs are standalone free orgs, not production orgs. Sandboxes are always copies of a production org and require a paid Salesforce subscription.

Which to use when

Developer for daily coding. Developer Pro when you need larger metadata. Partial Copy for QA — real data samples without waiting for a Full refresh. Full Sandbox for pre-production UAT and performance testing with real data volume.

How do you analyze debug logs to diagnose performance issues?ARAGO▼

Go to Setup → Debug Logs → set log level → reproduce the issue → open the log.

  • CPU Time — top of log and each entry shows cumulative CPU. If >8,000ms, you're close to the 10,000ms limit. Look for expensive operations inside loops.
  • SOQL Count — search for 'SOQL_EXECUTE_BEGIN'. Count how many appear and inside which methods. Any inside a loop = problem.
  • DML Count — search for 'DML_BEGIN'. More than 3-4 DML in a trigger usually indicates non-bulkified code.
  • Heap Size — search for 'HEAP_ALLOCATE'. Near 6MB = memory problem. Large result sets stored in variables.
  • Flow/Process executions — search for 'FLOW_START'. Unexpected re-entries = recursion.
  • Developer Console Query Plan — paste SOQL in Developer Console, click Query Plan before running. 'TableScan' = slow query.
// Limits class — programmatic profiling inside Apex
Long startCpu = Limits.getCpuTime();
// ... expensive operation ...
System.debug('CPU used: ' + (Limits.getCpuTime() - startCpu) + 'ms of ' + Limits.getLimitCpuTime() + 'ms');
System.debug('SOQL used: ' + Limits.getQueries() + ' of ' + Limits.getLimitQueries());
System.debug('DML used: ' + Limits.getDmlStatements() + ' of ' + Limits.getLimitDmlStatements());
What are the four types of async Apex — when do you use each?ARAGO▼
TypeTriggerCan chain?Can callout?Use for
@futureDirect call from sync ApexNoYes (callout=true)Simple one-off callouts from trigger context
QueueableSystem.enqueueJob()Yes — chain self or anotherYes (AllowsCallouts)SObject params, chaining, job monitoring
BatchDatabase.executeBatch()Via finish()Yes (AllowsCallouts)Processing millions of records
SchedulableSystem.schedule() or SetupLaunches Batch/QueueableVia Batch/QueueableTime-triggered recurring jobs
// @future — simple, limited
@future(callout=true)
public static void syncToLOS(Id loanId) { /* callout logic */ }

// Queueable — SObject params + chaining
public class CreditCheckQueueable implements Queueable, Database.AllowsCallouts {
    private Loan__c loan;
    public CreditCheckQueueable(Loan__c l) { this.loan = l; }
    public void execute(QueueableContext ctx) {
        /* callout */
        System.enqueueJob(new OfacCheckQueueable(loan)); // chain
    }
}

// Batch — millions of records
public class NightlyBatch implements Database.Batchable<SObject> {
    public Database.QueryLocator start(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
        return Database.getQueryLocator([SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c='Active']);
    }
    public void execute(Database.BatchableContext bc, List<SObject> scope) { /* process */ }
    public void finish(Database.BatchableContext bc) { System.enqueueJob(new PostBatchJob()); }
}

// Schedulable — nightly at 2AM
System.schedule('Nightly Loan Sync', '0 0 2 * * ?', new NightlyLoanSync());
What are Shadow DOM, @wire limitations, and LWC component communication patterns?ARAGO▼

Shadow DOM — LWC wraps each component's DOM in an isolated shadow root. CSS from parent cannot reach into child, and vice versa. External querySelector cannot access component internals.

// Shadow DOM impact on CSS and querySelector
// Parent CSS: c-child-cmp .my-class { color: red } — BLOCKED by shadow DOM
// Component CSS: .my-class { color: red } — only applies inside THIS component's shadow root
this.template.querySelector('.my-class');  // CORRECT — scoped to this shadow root
document.querySelector('.my-class');       // WRONG — shadow DOM hides it

@wire limitations:

  • @wire is read-only — never use cacheable=true methods for DML operations
  • Reactive parameters must be prefixed with $ to re-call on change
  • Call refreshApex(this.wiredResult) after a mutation to force re-fetch
  • Wire results are cached — calling with same params returns cached data

Component communication:

  • Parent → Child: @api properties (data down)
  • Child → Parent: CustomEvent + dispatchEvent (events up)
  • Unrelated components: Lightning Message Service (publish/subscribe)
How do you design large-scale async processing for bulk data operations?ARAGO▼

Architecture for processing millions of records reliably:

  • Batch Apex + QueryLocator — handles up to 50M records via QueryLocator, each chunk (200 records) is an independent transaction with fresh governor limits
  • Database.Stateful — preserve counters and error lists across chunks for finish() summary
  • Database.AllowsCallouts — implement when chunks need to call external APIs
  • Error handling per chunk — wrap execute() in try-catch, log failures without stopping other chunks
  • Retry pattern — store failed record IDs in Error_Log__c, scheduled Apex retries them nightly
  • Queueable chaining — for sequential multi-step processing (credit check → OFAC → LOS sync)
  • Platform Events — for decoupled fan-out (one batch completion triggers multiple downstream jobs)
public class LoanSyncBatch implements Database.Batchable<SObject>, Database.Stateful, Database.AllowsCallouts {
    public Integer processed = 0, errors = 0;
    public List<Id> failedIds = new List<Id>();

    public Database.QueryLocator start(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
        return Database.getQueryLocator([SELECT Id, External_Id__c FROM Loan__c WHERE Sync_Status__c='Pending']);
    }
    public void execute(Database.BatchableContext bc, List<SObject> scope) {
        List<Loan__c> loans = (List<Loan__c>) scope;
        for (Loan__c l : loans) {
            try { LOSService.sync(l); processed++; }
            catch (Exception e) { errors++; failedIds.add(l.Id); }
        }
    }
    public void finish(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
        // Email completion summary, chain post-processing
        System.enqueueJob(new NotifyAdminQueueable(processed, errors, failedIds));
    }
}

⟩ MORGAN STANLEY — Salesforce Developer Interview (Multi-Round)

Round 1: What happens if a child dispatches an event before the parent is rendered?MORGAN STANLEY R1▼

The event will not be captured by the parent. LWC events propagate through the existing DOM tree only. If the parent hasn't been inserted into the DOM yet, it has no event listener registered, so the event is fired and lost.

Why this matters:

  • LWC lifecycle: parent connectedCallback fires BEFORE children are created — parent is in DOM before children
  • Child events bubble UP to parent — so by the time child fires, parent is already in DOM
  • The problematic scenario: a child fires an event in its own constructor() before the parent's connectedCallback has set up its handler
  • Fix: fire events in connectedCallback or renderedCallback — never in constructor
// WRONG — event in constructor fires before parent listener is set up
constructor() {
    super();
    this.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('ready')); // parent may not be listening yet
}

// CORRECT — fire in connectedCallback (DOM is established)
connectedCallback() {
    this.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('ready')); // parent's onready handler is registered
}
Round 1: How is a component affected when it re-renders inside a for:each loop?MORGAN STANLEY R1▼

Re-rendering behaviour inside for:each depends entirely on the key attribute.

  • Same key — LWC recognises it's the same logical item. Only the changed data is updated (efficient patch — like React's reconciliation). The component instance is reused.
  • Different key — LWC treats it as a different item. The old component is destroyed (disconnectedCallback fires) and a new one is created (constructor + connectedCallback fire). Expensive.
  • No key — LWC uses index. Inserting/removing items causes all subsequent items to destroy and recreate. Never do this for mutable lists.
// Template
<template for:each={loans} for:item="loan">
    <c-loan-card key={loan.Id} loan-data={loan}></c-loan-card>
</template>
// Good key: loan.Id — stable, unique. When loan data changes, component patches in place.
// Bad key: index — inserting at position 0 forces ALL components to destroy + recreate.
Performance rule

Always use a stable, unique business key (Id, externalId) as the for:each key. Never use the loop index for mutable lists. This is the single biggest LWC performance optimisation for lists.

Round 1: How does Salesforce handle callout responses that arrive after a timeout?MORGAN STANLEY R1▼

Once the timeout is reached, Salesforce marks the request as failed and throws a CalloutException. Even if the external server eventually sends a response, Salesforce ignores it — the connection is already closed.

  • Default timeout: 10 seconds. Maximum timeout: 120 seconds (req.setTimeout(120000))
  • The CalloutException is thrown in the Apex code at the point of new Http().send(req)
  • The external server may continue processing and complete the operation — Salesforce will never know
  • This is why idempotency matters: if you retry after a timeout, you must be able to safely re-send the same request without creating duplicates
try {
    req.setTimeout(30000); // 30 seconds max
    HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req);
} catch (CalloutException e) {
    // Timeout OR network failure — we don't know if server received and processed it
    // Safe retry: include Idempotency-Key header so server deduplicates
    scheduleRetry(loanId); // retry via Queueable with same idempotency key
    insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c='Callout timeout: ' + e.getMessage());
}
Round 1: Why can the same SOQL query return different results within one transaction?MORGAN STANLEY R1▼

Because SOQL queries within a transaction can see uncommitted changes made earlier in the same transaction.

// Transaction example:
Loan__c loan = new Loan__c(Status__c='Applied', Amount__c=250000);
insert loan; // inserted but NOT committed yet

// Query WITHIN SAME TRANSACTION — sees the uncommitted insert
List<Loan__c> result = [SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c='Applied'];
// loan IS in the result even though the transaction hasn't committed!

// This is called "read your own writes" — a feature, not a bug
// Practical use: trigger after insert can query the just-inserted record
// Practical trap: a test that queries before and after a DML in the same context
//   will see different results — first query misses the new records

Also: if your trigger fires multiple times in one transaction (recursion), each pass can see DML from earlier passes — leading to unexpected query results.

Test implication

This is why Test.startTest() / Test.stopTest() matters. They create isolated governor limit contexts but share the same transaction — queries across the boundary see each other's DML.

Round 1: What happens if a @future method is invoked from another async context?MORGAN STANLEY R1▼

Salesforce throws a runtime exception if you try to call a @future method from another async context. This is enforced by the platform.

Calling fromCan call @future?Alternative
Synchronous Apex✓ Yes—
@future method✗ No — exceptionUse Queueable instead
Queueable✗ No — exceptionChain another Queueable
Batch execute()✗ No — exceptionEnqueue a Queueable from execute()
Batch finish()✓ Yes (special case)Can also enqueue Queueable
Scheduled Apex✗ No — exceptionLaunch a Batch or Queueable

The correct pattern for chaining async work is Queueable — it supports chaining (System.enqueueJob() inside execute()), SObject parameters, and job monitoring.

Common mistake

Calling @future from inside a Batch execute() chunk is a frequent bug. It compiles fine but throws at runtime: 'Future method cannot be called from a future or batch method.' Always use Queueable for chaining inside Batch.

Round 1: Why are callouts not allowed after DML operations in the same transaction?MORGAN STANLEY R1▼

Salesforce enforces: callouts must happen BEFORE DML in the same transaction. You cannot make an HTTP callout after a DML statement.

Why this rule exists:

  • DML operations acquire record locks in the database — these locks are held until the transaction commits
  • If you make a callout while holding DB locks, the callout can take seconds or minutes
  • During that wait, the locked records are inaccessible to other users — a serious scalability problem
  • Salesforce prevents this by throwing a CalloutException if you attempt a callout after DML
// WRONG — throws CalloutException
Loan__c loan = new Loan__c(Status__c='Processing');
insert loan; // acquires DB lock
HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req); // EXCEPTION: callout after uncommitted DML!

// CORRECT — callout BEFORE DML
HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req); // callout first — no locks held
Loan__c loan = new Loan__c(Status__c='Processing');
insert loan; // DML after callout — fine

// For trigger context (can't callout from before/after trigger):
// Use @future(callout=true) or Queueable + AllowsCallouts
Trigger pattern

Never make HTTP callouts directly from a trigger. Always use @future(callout=true) or Queueable + Database.AllowsCallouts. The trigger dispatches the async job; the async job makes the callout — no lock conflict.

Round 2: What happens if a Batch Apex job is aborted while execute() is in progress?MORGAN STANLEY R2▼

When System.abortJob(jobId) is called on a running Batch job:

  • The currently executing execute() chunk completes — it cannot be interrupted mid-transaction
  • No further execute() chunks are dispatched — the batch stops after the current chunk
  • finish() is NOT called — this is important because post-processing (emails, cleanup, chaining) won't happen
  • Records in chunks that never ran are left unprocessed — no automatic rollback of already-processed chunks
  • Job status becomes 'Aborted' in AsyncApexJob

Design implication:

Your batch must be restartable. If it's aborted partway through, you must be able to rerun it without duplicating work already done. Typical pattern: query only records with a 'Pending' sync status, update each record to 'Processed' as part of the execute() chunk.

finish() safety

If finish() contains critical logic (sending notifications, chaining the next job), monitor for Aborted status and trigger finish() logic manually if needed. Or use a monitoring Scheduled Apex that checks for stuck/aborted jobs.

Round 2: Why does a before insert trigger not have record IDs, but after insert does?MORGAN STANLEY R2▼

Record IDs are generated by the database at save time. The before insert trigger runs before the record is written to the database — so the database hasn't created the ID yet.

  • Before insert: record exists in memory only. No database row. No ID. Trigger.new[0].Id == null.
  • After insert: record has been written to DB. Database generated and assigned the ID. Trigger.new[0].Id is now populated.
  • This is why related record creation must go in after insert — you need the Id to set the lookup field on child records.
  • Setting field defaults should go in before insert — no extra DML needed, Id not required.
trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (before insert, after insert) {
    if (Trigger.isBefore && Trigger.isInsert) {
        System.debug(Trigger.new[0].Id); // NULL — ID doesn't exist yet
        // Use before insert for defaults:
        for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) l.Status__c = 'Applied'; // set directly, no DML
    }
    if (Trigger.isAfter && Trigger.isInsert) {
        System.debug(Trigger.new[0].Id); // '0a0ABC...' — ID is now available
        // Use after insert for related records:
        List<Loan_Task__c> tasks = new List<Loan_Task__c>();
        for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new)
            tasks.add(new Loan_Task__c(Loan__c = l.Id, Task_Name__c='Initial Review'));
        insert tasks;
    }
}
Round 2: LWC tracked object — what happens if the component reassigns the same reference?MORGAN STANLEY R2▼

The UI will NOT re-render. LWC's reactivity system detects changes by reference equality. If you reassign the same object reference, the reference hasn't changed — LWC sees no change.

import { LightningElement, track } from 'lwc';

export default class LoanCard extends LightningElement {
    @track loanData = { status: 'Applied', amount: 250000 };

    updateStatus() {
        // WRONG — same reference — UI does NOT update
        this.loanData.status = 'Approved'; // mutation, not reassignment
        // With @track: this DOES work for @track specifically
        // Without @track: this does NOT trigger re-render

        // CORRECT (always works, with or without @track) — new reference
        this.loanData = { ...this.loanData, status: 'Approved' }; // spread creates new object ref
        // New reference → LWC detects change → re-renders
    }

    // For @track specifically:
    // @track detects DEEP mutations (property changes on the object)
    // Without @track: only reference change triggers re-render
    // Modern LWC (API v39+): @track not needed for primitive props — they're reactive by default
}
Modern LWC guidance

In modern LWC, @track is rarely needed. Primitive properties are reactive by default. For objects/arrays, create a new reference (spread operator or Object.assign) to guarantee re-render. This is cleaner and more predictable than relying on @track deep tracking.

Round 2: External API changes response format without notice — how do you adapt?MORGAN STANLEY R2▼

This is a real-world integration challenge. The answer covers both defensive coding and operational monitoring.

Defensive parsing — never use strict typed deserialization for external APIs:

// FRAGILE — throws if any expected field is missing or type changes
ExpireanResponse resp = (ExpireanResponse) JSON.deserialize(body, ExpireanResponse.class);

// RESILIENT — handles missing/renamed fields gracefully
Map<String,Object> rawMap = (Map<String,Object>) JSON.deserializeUntyped(body);
Integer score = rawMap.containsKey('creditScore')
    ? (Integer) rawMap.get('creditScore')
    : rawMap.containsKey('credit_score')        // try alternate field name
        ? (Integer) rawMap.get('credit_score')
        : null;                                  // handle missing gracefully
if (score == null) {
    insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c='creditScore field missing from response. Raw: '+body.abbreviate(1000));
    return; // fail safe — don't process with null data
}
  • Versioned API calls — include Accept-Version header in requests; monitor which version the API returns
  • Schema validation — assert required fields exist before processing; log raw body when unexpected structure received
  • Monitoring alerts — track callout success rates; spike in failures = API changed without notice
  • Contract testing — if API provides OpenAPI spec, validate responses against it in staging
  • Vendor relationship — escalate immediately for pre-notification of changes in future
Round 2: What happens if a trigger on a Platform Event performs DML?MORGAN STANLEY R2▼

It is fully allowed. Platform Event triggers run asynchronously (after insert on the PE object), which means they operate in their own separate transaction with async governor limits.

  • PE triggers run in an async context — they get async limits (200 SOQL, 150 DML, 60s CPU)
  • The original transaction that published the event is completely separate — it has already committed
  • If the PE trigger's DML fails, the Platform Event is NOT rolled back — it already fired
  • If the PE trigger DML fails and throws, Salesforce will retry the trigger up to the platform retry limit
  • Use try-catch in PE triggers to handle errors explicitly and prevent uncontrolled retries
// Platform Event trigger — DML is fine here
trigger LoanStatusChangeTrigger on Loan_Status_Change__e (after insert) {
    List<Notification_Log__c> logs = new List<Notification_Log__c>();
    for (Loan_Status_Change__e evt : Trigger.new) {
        logs.add(new Notification_Log__c(
            Loan_Id__c = evt.Loan_Id__c,
            New_Status__c = evt.New_Status__c,
            Processed_At__c = DateTime.now()
        ));
    }
    insert logs; // DML in PE trigger — perfectly fine, runs in async context
    // Also fine: System.enqueueJob(new SyncQueueable(evt.Loan_Id__c));
}
Round 2: What happens if finish() enqueues another Batch or Queueable job?MORGAN STANLEY R2▼

It is fully allowed and commonly used for sequential job chaining. This is the standard pattern for processing large datasets in multiple stages.

public class Stage1Batch implements Database.Batchable<SObject> {
    public Database.QueryLocator start(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
        return Database.getQueryLocator([SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Stage1_Done__c = false]);
    }
    public void execute(Database.BatchableContext bc, List<SObject> scope) {
        // Stage 1 processing
        for (SObject s : scope) ((Loan__c)s).Stage1_Done__c = true;
        update scope;
    }
    public void finish(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
        // Chain Stage 2 batch when Stage 1 completes
        Database.executeBatch(new Stage2Batch(), 200);
        // OR: enqueue a Queueable for post-processing
        System.enqueueJob(new Stage1CompletionQueueable(bc.getJobId()));
    }
}
  • finish() runs ONCE after all execute() chunks complete — it's the right place for chaining
  • You can enqueue Queueable OR start another Batch from finish()
  • The chained job is a NEW async job with fresh governor limits
  • This is the correct alternative to trying to chain @future (which is not allowed from async context)
Common pattern

Stage 1 Batch validates records → finish() chains Stage 2 Batch that processes → finish() chains Stage 3 Batch that archives → finish() sends completion notification via Queueable. Sequential pipeline with full governor limit resets at each stage.

Round 3: How do you handle a production issue under pressure?MORGAN STANLEY R3 BEHAVIORAL▼

Structure your answer using this framework:

  • Detect — How did you find out? (monitoring alert, user report, stakeholder message)
  • Isolate — How did you narrow down the cause? (debug logs, error messages, affected scope)
  • Communicate — Who did you tell and how quickly? (stakeholders need status, not silence)
  • Fix — What was the immediate mitigation vs permanent fix?
  • Learn — What monitoring/safeguard did you add to prevent recurrence?

Example answer:

'In a production deployment, a trigger we had tested in sandbox began hitting CPU limit errors for loan records updated via Data Loader (which sends 200 records per batch). In sandbox our test data was small and never hit the limit.' I first checked the debug logs and identified a formula field recalculation happening in the trigger context that was O(n²). I immediately communicated to the project manager and client that we had identified the issue and estimated 2 hours to resolve it.' The immediate fix was to disable the trigger via Custom Metadata (we had a bypass flag), which stopped the errors in 5 minutes. The proper fix — rewriting the calculation to use a map instead of nested loop — was deployed that evening after testing.' We added a nightly scheduled Apex that checks for CPU time spikes in recent jobs and alerts via email before they become production incidents.'

Key elements

Speed of communication matters as much as technical skill. Stakeholders who hear nothing for 2 hours assume the worst. Give a status update every 30 minutes even if it's just 'still investigating, ETA 1 hour.'

Round 3: How do you explain technical solutions to non-technical stakeholders?MORGAN STANLEY R3 BEHAVIORAL▼

The ability to translate between technical and business language is a senior developer skill, not just a soft skill.

  • Lead with business impact, not implementation — 'This change reduces loan processing time from 2 hours to 10 minutes' beats 'I refactored the batch job to use Queueable chaining'
  • Use analogies from their domain — a mortgage banker understands the underwriting pipeline better than they understand API retry logic
  • Avoid jargon entirely — if you say 'governor limits', follow immediately with '— Salesforce's usage quotas that prevent any one customer from overloading the shared platform'
  • Quantify the risk and benefit — 'Without this fix, 3% of loan status updates silently fail. With it, the failure rate drops to 0%.'
  • Show, don't just tell — a 2-minute demo is worth 10 minutes of explanation

Example analogy for Platform Events:

'Think of it like a hospital PA system. When a patient's status changes, the doctor doesn't personally run to every department. They announce it on the PA, and every department that needs to know reacts independently — pharmacy, billing, nursing. That's exactly what Platform Events do for our loan system.'

Round 3: How do you handle unrealistic client expectations on delivery timelines?MORGAN STANLEY R3 BEHAVIORAL▼

This tests your negotiation, communication, and project management skills.

  • Don't just say no — saying 'that's not possible' without an alternative is unhelpful and damages the relationship
  • Break down the scope — ask which features are must-have for the deadline vs nice-to-have. Often clients don't need everything they asked for by that date.
  • Show the work — a visible task breakdown (story points, days) makes the timeline conversation factual, not emotional
  • Propose phased delivery — 'We can deliver X and Y by your date. Z would be 2 weeks after.'
  • Identify the real constraint — often the deadline is tied to a business event (board presentation, contract renewal). Understanding the real driver helps find creative solutions.

Example answer:

'A client wanted a full LOS integration delivered in 3 weeks — based on scope it was an 8-week effort. I asked what was driving the 3-week date and learned they had a board presentation. I proposed: in 3 weeks, deliver a working demo of the core loan sync feature with real data from a sandbox. Full production integration in 8 weeks. They accepted because the board presentation need was met without compromising quality for production.'

Round 3: How do you manage deadlines when multiple teams have conflicting priorities?MORGAN STANLEY R3 BEHAVIORAL▼

Conflicting priorities are a leadership challenge, not just a scheduling problem.

  • Escalate to a decision maker, not between teams — two teams can't resolve their own conflict fairly. Bring it to the person who owns both priorities and ask them to choose.
  • Make the trade-off explicit — 'If we prioritise Team A's integration this sprint, Team B's report will slip 1 week. If we prioritise Team B, Team A slips 1 sprint. Which matters more to the business right now?'
  • Separate urgent from important — often one team's 'urgent' is actually 'important'. Help stakeholders understand the difference.
  • Look for parallel workstreams — can one team's work be done by another developer while you focus on the conflict item?
  • Document the decision — once the priority is set, write it down and send to all teams. This prevents re-litigation next week.

Example answer:

'Two business teams both needed their Salesforce feature by end of sprint — one was a compliance requirement, one was a sales tool. I documented both requirements with business impact and time estimate, then set up a 30-minute call with the CTO. She chose compliance first. I communicated the decision to the sales team with a specific commitment for the following sprint. Both teams felt heard because I had documented their case fairly.'

Additional: LWC lifecycle order — constructor to renderedCallback?ADDITIONAL▼
OrderHookDOM ready?Props available?Use for
1constructor()NoNoPrivate variable init only. Call super() first.
2connectedCallback()YesYesApex calls, subscribe channels, event listeners
3render()——Returns template. Rarely overridden.
4@wire resolutionYesYesWire adapters fire after render
5renderedCallback()YesYesDOM manipulation. Use initialized flag for once-only logic.
6disconnectedCallback()No—Cleanup: unsubscribe, cancel timers.
export default class LoanDashboard extends LightningElement {
    initialized = false;

    constructor() { super(); /* no DOM, no props, no Apex here */ }

    connectedCallback() {
        this.subscription = subscribe(this.msgCtx, CHANNEL, this.handleMsg);
        this.loadInitialData(); // Apex imperative call OK here
    }

    renderedCallback() {
        if (this.initialized) return; // run once only
        this.initialized = true;
        const canvas = this.template.querySelector('.chart'); // DOM access OK here
        this.initChart(canvas);
    }

    disconnectedCallback() { unsubscribe(this.subscription); }
}
Additional: How do you prevent Account deletion when Amount > 1 Billion?ADDITIONAL▼

Use a before delete trigger on Account. Check related Opportunity or Loan amounts and call addError() to block the delete.

trigger PreventAccountDeletion on Account (before delete) {
    // Collect all Account IDs being deleted
    Set<Id> accountIds = new Map<Id,Account>(Trigger.old).keySet();

    // Query related Opportunities with large amounts
    Map<Id, Decimal> accountTotalMap = new Map<Id, Decimal>();
    for (AggregateResult ar : [
        SELECT AccountId accId, SUM(Amount) total
        FROM Opportunity
        WHERE AccountId IN :accountIds AND StageName != 'Closed Lost'
        GROUP BY AccountId
    ]) {
        accountTotalMap.put((Id)ar.get('accId'), (Decimal)ar.get('total'));
    }

    // Block deletion for accounts with >$1B in opportunities
    for (Account acc : Trigger.old) {
        Decimal total = accountTotalMap.get(acc.Id) ?? 0;
        if (total > 1000000000) {
            acc.addError('Cannot delete account with over $1 billion in active opportunities. '
                + 'Current total: $' + total.format());
        }
    }
}
Additional: What is the difference between Entitlement and Milestone in Salesforce?ADDITIONAL▼
FeatureEntitlementMilestone
DefinitionAgreement on what level of support a customer is entitled toA required step within an Entitlement Process
