PurposeDefines SLA — response time, resolution time, support hoursTracks whether specific time targets are met
Configured onAccount, Contact, Asset, Service ContractEntitlement Process (Setup)
ExampleGold Support: 2-hour response, 24/7 availabilityFirst Response milestone: must respond within 2 hours
ViolationEntitlement Process defines what happens when milestone is breachedMilestone Action fires on breach (email, escalation, field update)
ObjectEntitlement (standard object)Case Milestone (junction between Case and Milestone)
Interview memory hook

Entitlement = the PROMISE (what level of service the customer gets). Milestone = the MEASUREMENT (are we meeting that promise at each step).

Additional: What is the execution order of SOQL clauses?ADDITIONAL▼

SOQL has a logical processing order (same concept as SQL). Understanding this helps you write correct HAVING clauses and avoid referencing aliases in the wrong place.

OrderClauseWhat it does
1FROMIdentifies the object to query
2WHEREFilters individual rows before grouping
3GROUP BYGroups rows for aggregate functions
4HAVINGFilters groups AFTER aggregation (uses aggregate values)
5SELECTReturns the specified fields and calculated values
6ORDER BYSorts the result set
7LIMIT / OFFSETConstrains the number of returned rows
// Correct: HAVING filters on aggregate (applied after GROUP BY)
SELECT Status__c, COUNT(Id) cnt, SUM(Amount__c) total
FROM Loan__c
WHERE CreatedDate = THIS_YEAR    -- WHERE: filter rows first
GROUP BY Status__c               -- GROUP BY: group the filtered rows
HAVING COUNT(Id) > 10           -- HAVING: filter groups by aggregate
ORDER BY SUM(Amount__c) DESC     -- ORDER BY: sort the result
LIMIT 5                          -- LIMIT: return top 5 only
HAVING vs WHERE

WHERE filters individual records (before grouping). HAVING filters groups (after aggregation). You cannot use HAVING without GROUP BY, and you cannot use aggregate functions in WHERE.

Company Interview Questions
Real questions from Arago (4 Years exp) & Morgan Stanley — with complete model answers. Every question exactly as asked.
🏢 ARAGO — Senior Salesforce Developer (4 Years)
27 core technical questions from the actual interview
How do you control trigger execution order if multiple triggers exist on the same object?ARAGO▼

Salesforce does not guarantee execution order when multiple triggers exist on the same object. The only reliable solution is the one trigger per object rule.

// One trigger — acts as dispatcher only
trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (before insert, before update, after insert, after update, after delete) {
    new LoanTriggerHandler().run();
}

// Handler controls execution order explicitly via ordered method calls
public class LoanTriggerHandler extends TriggerHandler {
    public override void onBeforeInsert() {
        LoanValidationService.validate(Trigger.new);   // 1st
        LoanDefaultsService.setDefaults(Trigger.new);  // 2nd — order guaranteed
    }
    public override void onAfterInsert() {
        LoanNotificationService.sendWelcome(Trigger.new); // 1st
        LoanLOSService.syncToLOS(Trigger.new);            // 2nd
    }
}
Interview answer

Say: 'I enforce one trigger per object in every project. Execution order is controlled within the handler class — the order method calls are made is explicit and fully predictable.'

How do you handle bulk insert/update operations efficiently in triggers?ARAGO▼

Core rule: never put SOQL or DML inside a for loop. Always process the full Trigger.new batch collectively.

// BAD — hits 101-query limit with 101 records
for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) {
    Account a = [SELECT Id FROM Account WHERE Id = :l.Account__c]; // SOQL IN LOOP
    a.Total_Loans__c++; update a; // DML IN LOOP
}

// GOOD — ONE SOQL + ONE DML for entire batch
Set<Id> accIds = new Set<Id>();
for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) if (l.Account__c != null) accIds.add(l.Account__c);

Map<Id,Account> accMap = new Map<Id,Account>(
    [SELECT Id, Total_Loans__c FROM Account WHERE Id IN :accIds]);

for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new)
    if (accMap.containsKey(l.Account__c)) accMap.get(l.Account__c).Total_Loans__c++;

update accMap.values(); // one DML for all accounts
  • Use Set to collect unique IDs
  • Use Map<Id,SObject> for O(1) lookup
  • Single SOQL outside loop
  • Single DML outside loop on full collection
Explain the difference between before and after triggers with an example.ARAGO▼
Before TriggerAfter Trigger
WhenBefore record saved to DBAfter record saved to DB
Record Id available?No (Insert) / Yes (Update)Yes always
Can modify Trigger.new?Yes — auto-savedNo — must use DML
Primary useSet defaults, validate, derive fieldsCreate child records, callouts, events
Extra DML?No — changes saved automaticallyYes — explicit DML required
// Before insert — no DML needed
trigger BeforeEx on Loan__c (before insert) {
    for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) {
        if (l.Status__c == null) l.Status__c = 'Applied'; // auto-saved
    }
}
// After insert — Id needed for child record
trigger AfterEx on Loan__c (after insert) {
    List<Loan_Checklist__c> list = new List<Loan_Checklist__c>();
    for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new)
        list.add(new Loan_Checklist__c(Loan__c = l.Id)); // Id available after insert
    insert list;
}
How can you prevent recursion in triggers?ARAGO▼

Pattern 1 — Static boolean (simplest):

public class TriggerHelper { public static Boolean loanTriggerRan = false; }
trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (after update) {
    if (TriggerHelper.loanTriggerRan) return;
    TriggerHelper.loanTriggerRan = true;
    LoanTriggerHandler.onAfterUpdate(Trigger.new, Trigger.oldMap);
}

Pattern 2 — Set of processed IDs (more precise):

public class TriggerHelper { public static Set<Id> processedIds = new Set<Id>(); }
trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (after update) {
    List<Loan__c> unprocessed = new List<Loan__c>();
    for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new)
        if (!TriggerHelper.processedIds.contains(l.Id)) { unprocessed.add(l); TriggerHelper.processedIds.add(l.Id); }
    if (!unprocessed.isEmpty()) LoanTriggerHandler.onAfterUpdate(unprocessed, Trigger.oldMap);
}
Why it works

Static variables persist for the entire transaction but reset between transactions. A workflow re-entry sees the same static variable — the guard stops the loop.

What is a trigger execution context?ARAGO▼

The execution context defines which DML event fired the trigger and which phase (before/after) is running.

VariableTrue when
Trigger.isInsertINSERT DML
Trigger.isUpdateUPDATE DML
Trigger.isDeleteDELETE DML
Trigger.isUndeleteRecord restored
Trigger.isBeforeBefore DB save
Trigger.isAfterAfter DB save
Trigger.sizeCount of records in batch
trigger Ex on Loan__c (before insert, after update) {
    if (Trigger.isBefore && Trigger.isInsert) { /* set defaults */ }
    if (Trigger.isAfter && Trigger.isUpdate) {
        for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new)
            if (l.Status__c != Trigger.oldMap.get(l.Id).Status__c) { /* status changed */ }
    }
}
How would you structure a Trigger Framework?ARAGO▼

Layers: Trigger → Handler → Service → Selector → Helper

// Trigger — dispatcher only, no business logic
trigger LoanTrigger on Loan__c (before insert, before update, after insert, after update, after delete) {
    new LoanTriggerHandler().run();
}
// Handler — routes events, calls services
public class LoanTriggerHandler extends TriggerHandler {
    public override void onBeforeInsert() { LoanValidationService.validate(Trigger.new); }
    public override void onAfterUpdate()  { LoanStatusService.handleChange(Trigger.new, Trigger.oldMap); }
}
// Service — business logic, callable from trigger/LWC/batch/API
public with sharing class LoanStatusService {
    public static void handleChange(List<Loan__c> loans, Map<Id,Loan__c> oldMap) { /* logic */ }
}
// Selector — all SOQL in one place
public with sharing class LoansSelector {
    public static List<Loan__c> getById(Set<Id> ids) {
        return [SELECT Id, Name, Status__c FROM Loan__c WHERE Id IN :ids WITH SECURITY_ENFORCED];
    }
}
Best practices for reusable and maintainable triggers?ARAGO▼
  • One trigger per object — eliminates ordering ambiguity
  • Fully bulkified — no SOQL/DML in loops, always works with collections
  • No hardcoding — use Custom Metadata for config (rates, endpoints, feature flags)
  • Handler/service pattern — trigger is dispatcher, logic lives in classes
  • Recursion protection — static boolean or Set-based guard
  • WITH SECURITY_ENFORCED in all SOQL — enforce FLS
  • Proper naming — LoanTrigger, LoanTriggerHandler, LoanService, LoansSelector
  • 90%+ test coverage — bulk test (200 records), positive + negative paths
When would you choose Flow over Apex?ARAGO▼
ScenarioFlowApex
Simple field update✓ Before-Save FlowOverkill
Email on status change✓ After-Save + Email ActionMore code
Admin-maintainable✓✗
Complex SOQL/logic✗✓
Millions of recordsBatch-limited✓ Batch Apex
External API (complex)✗✓

Real scenario: A Flow failed with CPU limit errors during a 50,000-record data load. Replaced with Batch Apex — no more CPU failures.

Salesforce guidance

Flow-first. Use Apex when logic is too complex for Flow, performance is critical, or integration patterns require it.

How can you avoid SOQL injection?ARAGO▼
// VULNERABLE — raw concatenation
String q = 'SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Name = '' + userInput + ''';
// Attack: userInput = "' OR Id != null OR Name = '"  →  returns ALL records

// SAFE 1 — bind variables (always preferred)
List<Loan__c> loans = Database.query('SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Name = :name');

// SAFE 2 — escapeSingleQuotes
String safe = String.escapeSingleQuotes(userInput);
String q2 = 'SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Name = '' + safe + ''';

// SAFE 3 — validate object/field names via Schema
if (!Schema.getGlobalDescribe().containsKey(objectName))
    throw new QueryException('Invalid object: ' + objectName);
Bind variables are safest

They're handled directly by Salesforce's query engine — never interpreted as SOQL syntax regardless of content.

Difference between SOQL and SOSL?ARAGO▼
SOQLSOSL
QueriesOne object at a timeMultiple objects simultaneously
IndexDatabase columnsFull-text search index
Best forStructured WHERE filtersFree-text search across fields/objects
Governor limit100 sync / 200 async20 sync / 100 async
// SOQL — specific structured query
[SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c='Active' AND Amount__c > 100000]

// SOSL — search 'Johnson' across Contact AND Lead simultaneously
List<List<SObject>> r = [FIND 'Johnson*' IN NAME FIELDS
    RETURNING Contact(Id,Name), Lead(Id,Name) LIMIT 20];
How to query parent-child relationships in SOQL?ARAGO▼
// Child → Parent (dot notation — up to 5 levels)
SELECT Id, Account.Name, Account.Owner.Name FROM Contact  // standard field AccountId → Account
SELECT Id, Account__r.Name FROM Loan__c  // custom field Account__c → Account__r

// Parent → Child (subquery — child relationship name)
SELECT Id, Name, (SELECT Id, Name FROM Contacts) FROM Account  // standard
SELECT Id, Name, (SELECT Id, Status__c FROM Loans__r) FROM Account  // custom

// Access in Apex
for (Account acc : [SELECT Id,(SELECT Id FROM Loans__r) FROM Account]) {
    List<Loan__c> loans = acc.Loans__r;
}
Difference between Custom Metadata Types and Custom Settings?ARAGO▼
FeatureCustom MetadataCustom Settings
Deployable?✓ Yes — moves with code✗ No — data stays
Free SOQL?✓ Yes✓ Yes (cached)
Profile/user overrides?✗ No✓ Hierarchy type
Best forConfig deployed with codePer-user/org preferences
Loan_Config__mdt cfg = [SELECT Base_Rate__c FROM Loan_Config__mdt WHERE Loan_Type__c='FHA' LIMIT 1];
Loan_Settings__c s = Loan_Settings__c.getInstance(); // hierarchy — per user
Difference between DML statements and Database methods?ARAGO▼
DMLDatabase Method
On errorThrows — ALL rollbackReturns SaveResult[] — partial success
Partial successNoYes (false param)
Use whenAll must succeedSome may fail
insert loanList; // all-or-nothing

List<Database.SaveResult> r = Database.insert(loanList, false); // partial success
for (Integer i=0; i<r.size(); i++)
    if (!r[i].isSuccess())
        insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c=r[i].getErrors()[0].getMessage());
How to control partial success with Database methods?ARAGO▼
// false = partial success — failed records skipped, successful commit
List<Database.SaveResult> results = Database.insert(records, false);
// true = same as plain DML — throws on any failure
List<Database.SaveResult> results2 = Database.insert(records, true);

List<Error_Log__c> errors = new List<Error_Log__c>();
for (Integer i=0; i<results.size(); i++) {
    if (!results[i].isSuccess())
        errors.add(new Error_Log__c(
            Record_Name__c=records[i].Name,
            Error_Message__c=results[i].getErrors()[0].getMessage()
        ));
}
if (!errors.isEmpty()) insert errors;
What is a Savepoint and how does rollback work?ARAGO▼
Savepoint sp = Database.setSavepoint();
try {
    Loan__c l = new Loan__c(Status__c='Processing'); insert l;
    LoanDocument__c d = new LoanDocument__c(Loan__c=l.Id); insert d;
    if (failureCondition) throw new LoanException('Failed');
} catch (LoanException e) {
    Database.rollback(sp); // undoes BOTH inserts above
    insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c=e.getMessage()); // still works after rollback
}
Callouts + Savepoints

Cannot callout after DML in same tx. Cannot use savepoint after callout. Order must be: callout → DML, or use async for callout.

Explain OOP concepts in Apex.ARAGO▼
// 1. ENCAPSULATION — hide state, expose via methods
public class LoanCalc {
    private Decimal rate;
    public LoanCalc(Decimal r) { this.rate = r; }
    public Decimal payment(Decimal principal, Integer months) { return principal * rate / months; }
}

// 2. INHERITANCE — reuse and extend
public virtual class TriggerHandler { public virtual void onBeforeInsert() {} }
public class LoanHandler extends TriggerHandler {
    public override void onBeforeInsert() { /* specific logic */ }
}

// 3. POLYMORPHISM — one interface, many implementations
public interface ISender { void send(String to, String msg); }
public class EmailSender implements ISender { public void send(String to, String msg) { /* email */ } }
public class SmsSender   implements ISender { public void send(String to, String msg) { /* sms   */ } }
ISender s = new EmailSender(); s.send('[email protected]', 'Approved');

// 4. ABSTRACTION — define contract without implementation
public abstract class LoanProcessor {
    public abstract void validate(Loan__c l);
    public void process(Loan__c l) { validate(l); } // uses abstract method
}
Difference between static and non-static in Apex?ARAGO▼
StaticNon-Static (Instance)
ScopeShared across all instances in transactionUnique per class instance
AccessClassName.method() — no instance needednew MyClass().method()
Use forUtility methods, tx-wide flags, singletonsObject-specific state
public class LoanHelper {
    public static Integer callCount = 0; // shared across all calls
    public static Decimal calcRate(String type) { callCount++; return type=='FHA'?6.25:6.5; }
    public Decimal instanceRate; // per-instance
    public LoanHelper(Decimal r) { this.instanceRate = r; }
}
LoanHelper.calcRate('FHA'); // static — no instance
new LoanHelper(0.065).instanceRate; // non-static — needs instance
Recursion risk

Improper static boolean flags can suppress legitimate trigger runs. Use Set-based approach for finer control.

What are access modifiers in Apex?ARAGO▼
ModifierAccessible from
privateSame class only
protectedSame class + subclasses
publicAny class in same namespace/org
globalAny namespace — managed packages, external
Rule

Use the most restrictive modifier that still makes your code work. private by default, global only for managed package public APIs.

What are the types of Salesforce sandboxes?ARAGO▼
TypeDataStorageRefreshUse for
DeveloperNone200MB1 dayIndividual dev work
Developer ProNone1GB1 dayLarger dev/testing
Partial CopySubset5GB5 daysQA with realistic data
FullComplete copySame as prod29 daysPerformance, UAT, regression

Can you create a sandbox in a Developer Org? No. Sandboxes are copies of production orgs. Developer Orgs are standalone and cannot have sandboxes.

How do you analyze debug logs?ARAGO▼
  • SOQL count — 'Number of SOQL queries'. Close to 100? Find SOQL in loops.
  • DML count — 'Number of DML statements'. Close to 150? Bulk your DML.
  • CPU time — 'Maximum CPU time'. Near 10,000ms? Find expensive loops.
  • Heap size — 'Maximum heap size'. Near 6MB? Reduce in-memory collections.
  • Execution flow — CODE_UNIT_STARTED/FINISHED trace which classes ran.
// Programmatic limit monitoring
System.debug('SOQL: '+Limits.getQueries()+'/'+Limits.getLimitQueries());
System.debug('CPU:  '+Limits.getCpuTime()+'ms/'+Limits.getLimitCpuTime()+'ms');
System.debug('DML:  '+Limits.getDMLStatements()+'/'+Limits.getLimitDMLStatements());

ChainingNoYesIn finish()Recurring
MonitoringNoAsyncApexJobAsyncApexJobCronTrigger

Best forSimple calloutComplex/chainMillions of recordsRecurring jobs
What are governor limits and how do you work within them?ARAGO▼
LimitSyncAsync
SOQL100200
DML150150
CPU10,000ms60,000ms
Heap6MB12MB
  • Bulkify — no SOQL/DML in loops
  • Batch Apex — fresh limits per 200-record chunk
  • Use Limits class to monitor proactively
  • Move heavy work to async (Queueable/Batch) for 60s CPU
What is Shadow DOM in LWC?ARAGO▼

Browser-native feature that encapsulates each LWC component's HTML, CSS, and JS — preventing leakage between components.

/* CSS in loanCard.css — ONLY applies inside c-loan-card shadow root */
.badge { color: green; }
:host { display: block; }

// querySelector — must be scoped to shadow root
this.template.querySelector('.badge');   // CORRECT
document.querySelector('.badge');        // WRONG — shadow DOM hides it

// Access child — use @api method, not DOM traversal
this.template.querySelector('c-child').refresh(); // @api method — OK
CSS across shadow boundary

Use CSS custom properties (variables). Parent sets --color: blue; child uses var(--color). This is the only cross-shadow styling mechanism by design.

What types of exceptions exist in Apex and how do you handle them?ARAGO▼
TypeCauseCatchable?
DmlExceptionDML fails — validation, required fieldYes
QueryExceptiongetSingleResult() 0 or 2+ rowsYes
NullPointerExceptionAccess on null referenceYes
LimitExceptionGovernor limit exceededNo
CalloutExceptionHTTP timeout or failureYes
AuraHandledExceptionUser-friendly error to LWCYes
public class LoanException extends Exception {}
try {
    Loan__c l = [SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Id=:id]; // QueryException if 0
    update l; // DmlException on validation failure
    callout(l.Id); // CalloutException on timeout
} catch (QueryException e) { throw new LoanException('Not found: '+id); }
  catch (DmlException e)   { throw new LoanException('Save failed: '+e.getDmlMessage(0)); }
  catch (CalloutException e){ insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c=e.getMessage()); }
Explain synchronous vs asynchronous Apex execution.ARAGO▼
SynchronousAsynchronous
CPU limit10,000ms60,000ms
SOQL100200
Heap6MB12MB
Callouts in trigger?NoYes (AllowsCallouts)
TypesTriggers, LWC controllers@future, Queueable, Batch, Schedulable
  • Use async when: callout from trigger, processing large records, long computations, chained multi-step operations
How do you design large-scale async processing?ARAGO▼
// Scheduled → Batch → Queueable chain
public class NightlySync implements Schedulable {
    public void execute(SchedulableContext ctx) { Database.executeBatch(new LoanSyncBatch(), 200); }
}
System.schedule('Nightly Sync', '0 0 2 * * ?', new NightlySync());

public class LoanSyncBatch implements Database.Batchable<SObject>, Database.Stateful, Database.AllowsCallouts {
    public Integer processed=0, failed=0;
    public Database.QueryLocator start(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
        return Database.getQueryLocator([SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c='Active']);
    }
    public void execute(Database.BatchableContext bc, List<SObject> scope) {
        for (Loan__c l : (List<Loan__c>)scope) {
            try { LOSService.sync(l); processed++; }
            catch (Exception e) { failed++; logError(l.Id,e); }
        }
    }
    public void finish(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
        System.enqueueJob(new PostSyncQueueable(processed, failed)); // chain notification
    }
}
  • Database.Stateful — persist counts across chunks
  • AllowsCallouts — enable HTTP in execute()
  • Lower scope for callout-heavy batches (10-50)
  • finish() — post-processing, notifications, chaining
🏦 MORGAN STANLEY — Salesforce Developer Interview
3 Rounds: Technical Round 1 + Technical Round 2 + Managerial/Behavioral
⚡ Round 1 — Technical (Edge Cases & Platform Behavior)
What happens if a child dispatches an event before the parent is rendered?MS ROUND 1▼

The event will not be captured by the parent. Events propagate through an existing, connected DOM tree — if the parent isn't in the DOM yet when the event fires, there is nothing to receive it.

// PROBLEM — event may fire before parent listener is attached
connectedCallback() {
    this.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('dataready', { detail: { id: this.recordId } }));
    // Parent may not have attached its onDataReady listener yet
}

// FIX 1 — defer to next microtask (parent guaranteed connected by then)
connectedCallback() {
    Promise.resolve().then(() => {
        this.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('dataready', { detail: { id: this.recordId } }));
    });
}

// FIX 2 — dispatch from renderedCallback() — parent always rendered before child
renderedCallback() {
    if (!this.initialized) {
        this.initialized = true;
        this.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('dataready', { detail: { id: this.recordId } }));
    }
}
Interview insight

This tests your understanding of LWC's async rendering model — the DOM tree must exist for event propagation to work. Timing matters in component trees.

How is a component affected when it re-renders inside a for:each loop?MS ROUND 1▼
key attributeWhat happensPerformance
key changesComponent destroyed and recreated — full lifecycleSlow
key same, data changesOnly data/props update — component stays mountedFast
item moves in listComponent moves without recreate if key follows itemEfficient
<template for:each={loans} for:item="loan">
  <c-loan-card key={loan.Id} loan-id={loan.Id}></c-loan-card>
</template>

// Update loan.Name → key (loan.Id) unchanged → UPDATE (no recreate)
this.loans = this.loans.map(l => l.Id===id ? {...l, Name:'New'} : l);

// Replace with new Id → key changes → DESTROY + recreate
this.loans = this.loans.map(l => l.Id===id ? {Id:'new-id', Name:'New'} : l);
Never use index as key

key={index} forces all components to re-render on any data change. Always use a stable unique ID like loan.Id.

How does Salesforce handle callout responses that arrive after a timeout?MS ROUND 1▼

Once the timeout is reached Salesforce marks the request failed and throws a CalloutException. Any late response from the server is completely ignored.

  • Max timeout — 120,000ms. Default is 10,000ms if not set.
  • Late response — discarded. No mechanism to receive it.
  • Side effect risk — external system may have already processed the request. Always use idempotency keys — retrying a timed-out request must not create duplicates.
  • Design response — log timeout with correlation ID, let scheduled retry job handle it with same correlation ID
try {
    req.setTimeout(15000);
    HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req);
} catch (CalloutException e) {
    if (e.getMessage().contains('Read timeout')) {
        loan.Sync_Status__c = 'Timeout_Pending';
        loan.Correlation_Id__c = correlationId; // reuse same ID on retry
        update loan; // scheduled job picks up Timeout_Pending records
    }
}
Why can the same SOQL query return different results within one transaction?MS ROUND 1▼

Within a transaction, SOQL reflects uncommitted in-memory changes. Insert or update records in Apex, and the next SOQL query sees those changes — even before commit.

List<Loan__c> before = [SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c='Applied'];
System.debug(before.size()); // 5

Loan__c newLoan = new Loan__c(Status__c='Applied', Amount__c=100000); insert newLoan;

List<Loan__c> after = [SELECT Id FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c='Applied'];
System.debug(after.size()); // 6 — sees the uncommitted insert!
Practical implication

This is why after insert triggers can query their own inserted records. Design triggers carefully — bulk operations may see unexpected query results if you assume only committed data is visible.

What happens if a @future method is invoked from another async context?MS ROUND 1▼

Salesforce throws a runtime exception. @future cannot be called from @future, Batch, or Queueable.

From \ To@futureQueueableBatch
Sync Apex✓✓✓
@future✗ Error✗ Error✗ Error
Queueable✗ Error✓ Chain (1 child)✓
Batch execute()✗ Error✓✗
Batch finish()✗ Error✓✓
Solution

Use Queueable for chaining async operations. It supports System.enqueueJob() from within execute() — that's the modern replacement for chained @future attempts.

Why are callouts not allowed after DML in the same transaction?MS ROUND 1▼
  • Record locking — DML may lock records. A callout can take up to 120 seconds, holding those locks and blocking other users.
  • Inconsistent state risk — if callout never returns, DML already ran — partial committed state.
  • Multi-tenant impact — locked records during a slow callout degrade performance for other orgs on the same server.
// WRONG — DML then callout (throws CalloutException)
update loan;
HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req); // ERROR: uncommitted work pending

// CORRECT — callout first, then DML
HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req); // callout first
loan.Status__c = res.getStatusCode()==200 ? 'Synced' : 'Failed';
update loan; // DML after

// If you MUST DML then callout — use async
// Queueable starts a fresh transaction: no prior DML → callout allowed
The fix

Separate them with async. Trigger does DML → publish Platform Event → Queueable subscribes → fresh transaction → callout allowed.

⚡ Round 2 — Technical (Advanced Platform Behavior)
What happens if a Batch Apex job is aborted while an execute() is in progress?MS ROUND 2▼
  • Current execute() chunk completes — the in-progress chunk finishes its transaction. Not interrupted.
  • No further batches run — engine checks status after current chunk, sees 'Aborted', stops.
  • finish() is NOT called — only called on normal completion.
  • Partial data committed — completed chunks already committed. Design each chunk to be idempotent.
// Design for safe abort — each chunk marks its own records
public void execute(Database.BatchableContext bc, List<SObject> scope) {
    for (Loan__c l : (List<Loan__c>)scope) {
        try   { LOSService.sync(l); l.Sync_Status__c='Completed'; l.Last_Sync_Date__c=DateTime.now(); }
        catch (Exception e) { l.Sync_Status__c='Failed'; l.Error__c=e.getMessage(); }
    }
    update scope; // chunk commits regardless of what happens next
    // After abort: query Sync_Status__c='Completed' to see exactly what processed
}
Why does a before insert trigger not have record IDs but after insert does?MS ROUND 2▼

IDs are generated by the database engine when a record is saved. Before insert runs before the save — no ID exists yet.

PhaseDB stateId in Trigger.new
before insertRecord in memory — not savednull
DB savesDatabase assigns IdId created
after insertRecord committedId populated in Trigger.new
trigger Before on Loan__c (before insert) {
    System.debug(Trigger.new[0].Id); // null
    Trigger.new[0].Status__c = 'Applied'; // can set fields — auto-saved
}
trigger After on Loan__c (after insert) {
    System.debug(Trigger.new[0].Id); // '0a0Bm000002AbcEAB'
    insert new Loan_Checklist__c(Loan__c = Trigger.new[0].Id); // Id needed for child
}
Primary implication

This is THE reason to use after insert for creating child records — you need the parent Id to set the lookup field.

An LWC has a @track object. If you reassign the same reference, will the UI re-render?MS ROUND 2▼

No. LWC tracks changes by object reference. Same reference = no change detected = no re-render.

@track loanData = { status: 'Applied', amount: 250000 };

handleUpdate() {
    // WRONG — same reference, UI will NOT re-render
    this.loanData.status = 'Approved';
    this.loanData = this.loanData; // still same reference

    // CORRECT — new reference, UI WILL re-render
    this.loanData = { ...this.loanData, status: 'Approved' }; // spread = new object
}
Common bug

Developers mutate an object (this.data.field = 'x') and wonder why the UI didn't update. Fix: always create a new reference with spread operator.

An external API changes its response format without notice. How do you adapt?MS ROUND 2▼

Code design + operational resilience — both matter.

// FRAGILE — strict typed deserialization breaks on rename
ExternalResponse r = (ExternalResponse) JSON.deserialize(body, ExternalResponse.class);

// RESILIENT — untyped with defensive fallback
Map<String,Object> raw = (Map<String,Object>) JSON.deserializeUntyped(body);
String status = null;
if      (raw.containsKey('loanStatus')) status = (String) raw.get('loanStatus');
else if (raw.containsKey('status'))     status = (String) raw.get('status');
else logUnknownFormat('status field missing', body); // alert ops, don't crash
  • Check API version headers — alert on version change
  • Response schema validation — compare received fields against expected, log mismatches
  • Fallback logic — if critical field missing, fail gracefully with logged error
  • Monitoring alerts — ops team notified on parsing anomaly
What happens if a trigger on a Platform Event performs DML?MS ROUND 2▼
  • DML is allowed — PE triggers run asynchronously with async governor limits (200 SOQL, 150 DML, 60s CPU)
  • Rollback isolation — if DML fails it does NOT roll back the Platform Event publish. Event already committed.
  • Retry behavior — if trigger throws unhandled exception, Salesforce retries up to 3 times. After 3 failures, event is marked failed and skipped.
  • ReplayId preserved — same ReplayId on retries — subscribers can detect replays.
trigger LoanEventTrigger on Loan_Status_Change__e (after insert) {
    List<Notification_Log__c> logs = new List<Notification_Log__c>();
    for (Loan_Status_Change__e e : Trigger.new)
        logs.add(new Notification_Log__c(Loan_Id__c=e.Loan_Id__c, Status__c=e.New_Status__c));
    insert logs; // ALLOWED — async DML. If fails: Salesforce retries trigger up to 3x
}
What happens if finish() enqueues another Batch or Queueable job?MS ROUND 2▼

Fully supported and a common chaining pattern.

public void finish(Database.BatchableContext bc) {
    // Chain to step 2 — runs after ALL of step 1 completes
    Database.executeBatch(new Step2Batch(), 200);
    // OR lightweight notification
    System.enqueueJob(new PostBatchNotificationQueueable());
    // Get step 1 stats for context
    AsyncApexJob job = [SELECT TotalJobItems, NumberOfErrors FROM AsyncApexJob WHERE Id=:bc.getJobId()];
    System.enqueueJob(new PostBatchQueueable(job.TotalJobItems, job.NumberOfErrors));
}
  • Chaining in finish() guarantees step 2 only starts after ALL step 1 chunks complete
  • Cannot start another Batch from execute() — only from finish()
  • Queueable can be enqueued from both execute() and finish()
  • Max 5 concurrent batch jobs in org — check queue before launching chain
💬 Round 3 — Managerial / Behavioral
STAR format: Situation → Task → Action → Result
Tell me about a time you handled a production issue under pressure.MS BEHAVIORAL▼

Situation: A loan status batch job failed silently on a Friday evening. 200+ loan officers couldn't see correct status updates. Client called asking why borrowers were getting wrong information.

Task: Identify root cause and restore service quickly while keeping stakeholders informed — without a risky hasty fix.

Action: Pulled debug logs immediately — found an unhandled NullPointerException on a field that was null for records migrated from the old system. Communicated to client within 15 minutes: 'Issue identified and isolated. Fix in progress, expected resolution in 45 minutes.' Deployed a tightly scoped hotfix (null check), tested on 5 affected records in staging, pushed to production. Ran a full batch to reprocess all affected records.

Result: Service fully restored in 52 minutes. Zero data corruption. After resolution: implemented null handling as a coding standard and added monitoring alerts to catch this class of error in testing.

Key elements

Speed of diagnosis (logs), stakeholder communication (they care about this), scoped fix (not risky big bang change), and closing with what you learned.

How do you explain technical solutions to non-technical clients?MS BEHAVIORAL▼
  • Lead with business outcome, not implementation — 'This reduces processing time from 3 days to same-day' not 'async Queueable with retry logic'
  • Use analogies from their domain — mortgage professionals understand pipelines, rates, deadlines. Use their language.
  • Avoid unexplained acronyms — define any technical term the first time you use it
  • Visual aids — a simple box-and-arrow diagram communicates a data flow better than 10 minutes of verbal explanation
  • Check understanding — 'Does that make sense so far before I go deeper?'

Example translation: Instead of: 'We publish a Platform Event from the trigger and subscribe via an async Queueable making an HTTP callout via Named Credential.' Say: 'When a loan status changes in Salesforce, a notification automatically goes to your loan system in the background within seconds — neither system slows the other down.'

How would you handle a client with unrealistic delivery expectations?MS BEHAVIORAL▼

Step 1 — Understand before pushing back. Ask: 'Help me understand what's driving this timeline — is there a regulatory deadline, a board presentation, or another dependency?' Sometimes what seems unrealistic has a valid reason that changes everything.

Step 2 — Make scope/time/quality tradeoffs explicit. 'Here is what we can deliver by that date: X and Y. Z needs 2 more weeks. Which is most critical to have first?'

Step 3 — Propose phased delivery. 'We deliver core loan status in week 3 — covers your immediate need. Document management follows in week 5. You get something live sooner.'

Step 4 — Document the agreement in writing. Confirm scope, timeline, what was deprioritized and when it ships.

Never say no without an alternative

'We can't do that in 2 weeks' is not useful. 'Here's what we CAN do in 2 weeks and here's what we need for full scope' is a partnership response.

Describe a situation where you worked with multiple teams with conflicting priorities.MS BEHAVIORAL▼

Situation: During a platform migration, the underwriting team needed credit check integration by month-end for a regulatory audit. Operations needed document upload the same week for a training rollout. Both escalated to the same delivery manager.

Task: Resolve the conflict and keep both deliveries on track — or make an honest recommendation if that was impossible.

Action: Requested one call with both team leads and the delivery manager together — not separate conversations where I'd be the messenger. Presented three options with data: delay document upload one week (lowest risk), bring in a second developer (additional cost), or deliver partial credit check (highest risk). Gave my recommendation: delay document upload, framed in business terms — 'Regulatory audit has a hard compliance consequence. Training rollout can shift one week without comparable impact.'

Result: Credit check delivered on time, passed the audit. Document upload followed exactly one week later. Both teams felt heard because the decision was made with data, transparently, in one room.

What hiring managers want

You can run structured conversations with stakeholders, bring data not just opinions to priority discussions, and don't avoid conflict — you manage it directly.

📋 Additional Questions — Arago Extended Set
What is the SOQL clause execution order?ARAGO▼
  • FROM — identifies object
  • WHERE — filters (applies indexes here)
  • GROUP BY — groups for aggregation
  • HAVING — filters aggregate groups
  • SELECT — retrieves fields
  • ORDER BY — sorts result
  • LIMIT — restricts row count
Why it matters

Explains why you can't reference a SELECT alias in WHERE (WHERE runs before SELECT). Also why HAVING uses aggregate functions while WHERE uses field values.

How do you implement roll-up summary on a Lookup relationship?ARAGO▼

Roll-Up Summary fields are only available on Master-Detail. For Lookup relationships: use Apex Trigger or Flow.

trigger LoanRollup on Loan__c (after insert, after update, after delete, after undelete) {
    Set<Id> accIds = new Set<Id>();
    if (Trigger.new != null) for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) if (l.Account__c!=null) accIds.add(l.Account__c);
    if (Trigger.old != null) for (Loan__c l : Trigger.old) if (l.Account__c!=null) accIds.add(l.Account__c);

    List<AggregateResult> agg = [SELECT Account__c acc, SUM(Amount__c) total, COUNT(Id) cnt
        FROM Loan__c WHERE Account__c IN :accIds AND Status__c!='Declined' GROUP BY Account__c];

    Map<Id,AggregateResult> m = new Map<Id,AggregateResult>();
    for (AggregateResult ar : agg) m.put((Id)ar.get('acc'), ar);

    List<Account> toUpdate = new List<Account>();
    for (Id id : accIds)
        toUpdate.add(new Account(Id=id,
            Total_Loan_Amount__c = m.containsKey(id) ? (Decimal)m.get(id).get('total') : 0,
            Active_Loan_Count__c = m.containsKey(id) ? (Integer)m.get(id).get('cnt') : 0));
    update toUpdate;
}
How does sharing work — Sharing Rules vs Manual Sharing vs Apex Managed Sharing?ARAGO▼
TypeWho controlsAutomatedApex can delete?
Sharing RulesAdmin — criteria/ownershipYesNo
Manual SharingRecord owner — Share buttonNoNo
Apex ManagedDeveloper — Share recordsYesYes (custom RowCause)
// Grant access
Loan__Share share = new Loan__Share(ParentId=loanId, UserOrGroupId=brokerId,
    AccessLevel='Read', RowCause=Schema.Loan__Share.RowCause.Broker_Assignment__c);
Database.insert(share, false);

// Revoke — only custom RowCauses deleteable by Apex
delete [SELECT Id FROM Loan__Share WHERE ParentId=:loanId AND UserOrGroupId=:brokerId
    AND RowCause=Schema.Loan__Share.RowCause.Broker_Assignment__c];
How do you build Case Escalation integration?ARAGO▼
// After update trigger — detect escalation
trigger CaseTrigger on Case (after update) {
    List<Id> escalated = new List<Id>();
    for (Case c : Trigger.new)
        if (c.Status=='Escalated' && Trigger.oldMap.get(c.Id).Status!='Escalated')
            escalated.add(c.Id);
    if (!escalated.isEmpty()) CaseEscalationQueueable.enqueue(escalated);
}

// Queueable — callout in async context
public class CaseEscalationQueueable implements Queueable, Database.AllowsCallouts {
    private List<Id> ids;
    public CaseEscalationQueueable(List<Id> ids) { this.ids=ids; }
    public void execute(QueueableContext ctx) {
        for (Case c : [SELECT CaseNumber,Subject,Priority FROM Case WHERE Id IN :ids]) {
            HttpRequest req = new HttpRequest();
            req.setEndpoint('callout:Ticketing_NC/api/escalations');
            req.setMethod('POST');
            req.setBody(JSON.serialize(new Map<String,Object>{'case'=>c.CaseNumber,'priority'=>c.Priority}));
            HttpResponse res = new Http().send(req);
            if (res.getStatusCode()!=201) insert new Error_Log__c(Message__c='Escalation failed: '+c.CaseNumber);
        }
    }
}
How do you prevent duplicate Contact insertion (same LastName + Email)?ARAGO▼
trigger ContactDuplicateCheck on Contact (before insert, before update) {
    Set<String> emails = new Set<String>();
    for (Contact c : Trigger.new) if (c.Email!=null) emails.add(c.Email.toLowerCase());

    Map<String,Contact> existing = new Map<String,Contact>();
    for (Contact e : [SELECT Id,LastName,Email FROM Contact WHERE Email IN :emails]) {
        existing.put(e.LastName.toLowerCase()+'|'+e.Email.toLowerCase(), e);
    }

    for (Contact c : Trigger.new) {
        if (c.LastName==null || c.Email==null) continue;
        String key = c.LastName.toLowerCase()+'|'+c.Email.toLowerCase();
        if (existing.containsKey(key) && existing.get(key).Id != c.Id)
            c.addError('Contact with this Last Name + Email already exists: '+existing.get(key).Id);
    }
}
Consider native Duplicate Rules

Before writing Apex, check if Setup → Duplicate Rules covers your need. Native rules are admin-configurable, don't use governor limits, and support fuzzy matching. Use Apex only for cross-object or complex multi-field logic.

Named Credentials vs Remote Site Settings — difference?ARAGO▼
FeatureNamed CredentialsRemote Site Settings
Stores credentials?Yes — encryptedNo — URL only
Auth handled?AutomaticManual in code
SecurityNever in code or VCSCredentials must be coded or in Custom Setting
Code syntaxcallout:NC_Name/pathFull URL in code
Best forAll external API callsLegacy, public no-auth endpoints
Always use Named Credentials

It's the Salesforce security best practice. Credentials are encrypted and never visible in Apex code or version control.

Promise vs Promise.all in LWC JavaScript?ARAGO▼
// Sequential — total time = sum of each
async loadSequential() {
    const loan = await getLoan({ loanId: this.id }); // wait
    const docs  = await getDocs({ loanId: this.id }); // then wait
}

// Parallel — total time = max of each (faster)
async loadParallel() {
    const [loan, docs, officer] = await Promise.all([
        getLoan({ loanId: this.id }),
        getDocs({ loanId: this.id }),
        getOfficer({ loanId: this.id })
    ]); // all three start simultaneously
    this.loan=loan; this.docs=docs; this.officer=officer;
}

// Promise.allSettled — parallel, never fails, inspect each result
const results = await Promise.allSettled([getLoan({...}), getDocs({...})]);
results.forEach(r => r.status==='fulfilled' ? use(r.value) : log(r.reason));
Use Promise.all

For multiple independent Apex calls on component load. Instead of sequential awaits (slow), fire all in parallel. Use allSettled when partial failure is acceptable.

How do grandchild-to-grandparent events work in LWC?ARAGO▼
// Grandchild fires with bubbles AND composed
handleClick() {
    this.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('loanselected', {
        detail: { loanId: this.loanId },
        bubbles: true,   // bubbles up through DOM tree
        composed: true   // crosses shadow DOM boundaries (required for LWC)
    }));
}

// Grandparent template listens
// <c-parent onloanselected={handleLoanSelected}></c-parent>
// Grandparent JS
handleLoanSelected(event) {
    const loanId = event.detail.loanId; // event.target = grandchild
}
bubbles vs composed

bubbles:true alone only propagates within the same shadow root. composed:true is required to cross shadow DOM boundaries. Always set BOTH for grandchild-to-grandparent.

What are LWC limitations compared to Aura?ARAGO▼
  • No Application Events — use Lightning Message Service (LMS) instead
  • Limited inheritance — JS class extension works but HTML templates are not inherited
  • No $A global — use specific imports (NavigationMixin, empApi, etc.)
  • Dynamic components — lwc:component (API 59+) added this, but limited vs Aura's $A.createComponent()
  • Visualforce embedding — LWC cannot be directly embedded in VF pages; needs Aura wrapper
  • No @api method type definitions — Aura had formal aura:method signatures
Net verdict

LWC is the clearly superior choice for all new development. Mention limitations to show you know both platforms deeply — then note that LWC's constraints enforce better architecture.

How to frame your introduction for a screening round

My core expertise is in Apex development, Lightning Web Components, REST and SOAP integrations, and designing scalable trigger frameworks. I have worked extensively in the US mortgage and financial services domain — building a full Mortgage Origination Platform from the ground up, including credit bureau integration with Experian, DocuSign e-signature automation, and bidirectional sync with an external Loan Origination System.

In my most recent role, I worked as the senior developer on a five-person team delivering custom Salesforce solutions end-to-end — from requirement gathering and technical design through deployment and production support. I take ownership of my work and have a strong focus on code quality, governor limit compliance, and maintainability.

📋 Project Explanations
How to explain your 2 main projects clearly
Project 1 — Mortgage Origination Platform (explain to a screening interviewer)PROJECT▼

Keep it to 2-3 minutes. Cover: what it does, your role, key technical decisions, results.

"I was the lead developer on a Mortgage Origination Platform built entirely on Salesforce. The platform handles the complete lifecycle of a mortgage loan — from initial borrower application through underwriting, approval, and funded closing.

Technically, my key contributions were:
First, I designed and built the Apex trigger framework — single trigger per object, handler pattern, service layer — so multiple developers could work simultaneously without merge conflicts.

Second, I built three major integrations: Experian credit bureau for real-time credit scoring, DocuSign for e-signature on loan documents, and a bidirectional sync with the external Loan Origination System using Platform Events and Queueable Apex.

Third, I built the borrower-facing LWC components — loan application wizard, document upload portal, and a real-time loan status dashboard using empApi for live Platform Event updates.

The outcome: We reduced the average loan processing time from 12 days to 4 days. The platform now processes 200+ active loans per month with zero production incidents in the past 6 months."

Structure

What does it do (1 sentence) → Your specific technical role → 3 key technical achievements → Measurable result. Interviewers want to hear WHAT you built, not just that you worked on a project.

Project 2 — OpenAI + Salesforce AI Integration (explain to a screening interviewer)PROJECT▼

This demonstrates your AI/modern technology experience — a strong differentiator in 2025.

"My second significant project was integrating OpenAI's GPT API with Salesforce to automate loan document analysis and borrower communication.

The problem we were solving: underwriters were spending 2-3 hours manually reviewing uploaded loan documents for completeness before beginning analysis. We automated this using AI.

Technical design:
When a borrower uploaded a document, a Salesforce trigger published a Platform Event. A Queueable job retrieved the document as base64, sent it to OpenAI's Vision API via Named Credential callout, and received a structured JSON response identifying the document type, completeness score, and missing information.

Results were stored back on the Loan Document record and surfaced to underwriters through an LWC dashboard showing a completeness checklist.

Result: Reduced document review time from 2.5 hours to 8 minutes on average. Underwriter capacity for new loans increased by 40%."

Why this project lands well

It shows: AI/modern API integration, complex async patterns (Platform Events + Queueable), LWC UI, and measurable business impact. Even if they don't ask about AI, volunteering this project shows you're current with 2025 technology.

🖥 LWC — Basics to Advanced
All LWC topics asked in Mobigic/PWC screening
LWC basics — what are the core files and their purpose?LWC BASICS▼

Every LWC component is a folder with up to 5 files:

FilePurposeRequired?
componentName.htmlTemplate — markup, data binding, conditionalsYes
componentName.jsController — logic, event handlers, Apex callsYes
componentName.js-meta.xmlConfiguration — where component can be used, targetsYes
componentName.cssScoped styles — only applies inside this componentNo
componentName.svgCustom icon for App BuilderNo
// loanCard.html — template
<template>
  <div class="card">
    <p>{loanName}</p>
    <template if:true={isActive}>
      <lightning-badge label="Active"></lightning-badge>
    </template>
    <template for:each={contacts} for:item="contact">
      <p key={contact.Id}>{contact.Name}</p>
    </template>
  </div>
</template>

// loanCard.js — controller
import { LightningElement, api, wire } from 'lwc';
import getContacts from '@salesforce/apex/LoanController.getContacts';
export default class LoanCard extends LightningElement {
  @api loanId;
  @wire(getContacts, { loanId: '$loanId' }) contacts;
  get loanName() { return 'Loan-' + this.loanId; }
  get isActive() { return true; }
}

// loanCard.js-meta.xml — make visible in App Builder
<?xml version="1.0"?>
<LightningComponentBundle xmlns="http://soap.sforce.com/2006/04/metadata">
  <apiVersion>59.0</apiVersion>
  <isExposed>true</isExposed>
  <targets>
    <target>lightning__RecordPage</target>
    <target>lightning__AppPage</target>
  </targets>
</LightningComponentBundle>
NavigationMixin — how to use it to navigate in LWC?LWC STANDARD▼

NavigationMixin adds navigation capability to any LWC component. Import it, extend your class with it, then call this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]().

import { LightningElement, api } from 'lwc';
import { NavigationMixin } from 'lightning/navigation';

export default class LoanNavigator extends NavigationMixin(LightningElement) {
  @api recordId;

  // 1. Navigate to a record's View page
  openRecord() {
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
      type: 'standard__recordPage',
      attributes: { recordId: this.recordId, objectApiName: 'Loan__c', actionName: 'view' }
    });
  }

  // 2. Open Edit page
  editRecord() {
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
      type: 'standard__recordPage',
      attributes: { recordId: this.recordId, objectApiName: 'Loan__c', actionName: 'edit' }
    });
  }

  // 3. Open New record form
  createLoan() {
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
      type: 'standard__objectPage',
      attributes: { objectApiName: 'Loan__c', actionName: 'new' }
    });
  }

  // 4. Navigate to a custom tab
  openDashboard() {
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
      type: 'standard__navItemPage',
      attributes: { apiName: 'Loan_Dashboard' }
    });
  }

  // 5. Open external URL
  openExternalLink() {
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
      type: 'standard__webPage',
      attributes: { url: 'https://portal.experian.com' }
    });
  }

  // 6. Generate URL without navigating (for links, sharing)
  async copyLink() {
    const url = await this[NavigationMixin.GenerateUrl]({
      type: 'standard__recordPage',
      attributes: { recordId: this.recordId, actionName: 'view' }
    });
    navigator.clipboard.writeText(url);
  }
}
Interview tip

Always say: 'I extend NavigationMixin(LightningElement) — not LightningElement directly. If you forget the mixin, the navigate method doesn't exist on the component.'

How do you call an LWC component from a record page and open a record from within LWC?LWC STANDARD▼

Part 1: Add LWC to a record page

// js-meta.xml — expose the component to App Builder
<LightningComponentBundle xmlns="http://soap.sforce.com/2006/04/metadata">
  <apiVersion>59.0</apiVersion>
  <isExposed>true</isExposed>
  <targets>
    <target>lightning__RecordPage</target>  <!-- enables it for record pages -->
  </targets>
  <targetConfigs>
    <targetConfig targets="lightning__RecordPage">
      <property name="cardTitle" type="String" label="Card Title" default="Loan Details"/>
    </targetConfig>
  </targetConfigs>
</LightningComponentBundle>

// In the JS — get the current record's Id automatically
import { LightningElement, api } from 'lwc';
export default class LoanDetails extends LightningElement {
  @api recordId;  // Salesforce automatically injects the record page's record Id
  @api objectApiName; // automatically injected — 'Loan__c'
}

Part 2: Open a record from within LWC (NavigationMixin)

import { NavigationMixin } from 'lightning/navigation';
export default class LoanList extends NavigationMixin(LightningElement) {

  handleRowAction(event) {
    const loanId = event.detail.row.Id;
    // Open the record page
    this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({
      type: 'standard__recordPage',
      attributes: { recordId: loanId, objectApiName: 'Loan__c', actionName: 'view' }
    });
  }
}
Communication between LWC components — all patterns explained?LWC COMM▼

4 patterns depending on the relationship between components:

PatternDirectionWhen to use
@api propertyParent → ChildPass data down to child
@api methodParent → Child (call)Trigger action on child from parent
Custom EventChild → ParentChild notifies parent of action/data
Lightning Message Service (LMS)Any → AnyUnrelated components on same page
// 1. Parent → Child via @api property
// child.js:  @api loanId;
// parent.html: <c-child loan-id={selectedId}></c-child>

// 2. Parent calls @api method on child
// child.js: @api refresh() { this.loadData(); }
// parent.js: this.template.querySelector('c-child').refresh();

// 3. Child → Parent via Custom Event
// child.js
handleSelect() {
  this.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('loanselected', {
    detail: { loanId: this.loanId, loanName: this.loanName }
  }));
}
// parent.html: <c-child onloanselected={handleLoanSelected}></c-child>
// parent.js: handleLoanSelected(event) { const id = event.detail.loanId; }

// 4. LMS — unrelated components (different regions of the page)
// Publisher:
import { publish, MessageContext } from 'lightning/messageService';
import LOAN_CHANNEL from '@salesforce/messageChannel/LoanChannel__c';
@wire(MessageContext) messageContext;
publishLoan() { publish(this.messageContext, LOAN_CHANNEL, { loanId: this.loanId }); }

// Subscriber:
import { subscribe, unsubscribe, MessageContext } from 'lightning/messageService';
@wire(MessageContext) messageContext;
connectedCallback() {
  this.sub = subscribe(this.messageContext, LOAN_CHANNEL, (msg) => { this.loadLoan(msg.loanId); });
}
disconnectedCallback() { unsubscribe(this.sub); }
Grandchild to grandparent

Add bubbles:true and composed:true to the CustomEvent. It will bubble up through all ancestors automatically.

Apex Collections — Map, Set, List — when to use each?APEX BASICS▼
CollectionOrdered?Duplicates?Key lookup?Best for
ListYes — indexedYesBy index (list[0])Ordered data, DML (insert/update take List)
SetNoNo — unique onlyNo direct lookupStoring unique IDs to avoid SOQL duplicates
MapNoKeys uniqueYes — O(1) by keyFast record lookup by Id or other key
// LIST — ordered, allows duplicates, required for DML
List<Loan__c> loansToUpdate = new List<Loan__c>();
loansToUpdate.add(new Loan__c(Id=id1, Status__c='Approved'));
loansToUpdate.add(new Loan__c(Id=id2, Status__c='Approved'));
update loansToUpdate; // DML takes List

// SET — unique values, fast contains() check
Set<Id> processedIds = new Set<Id>();
for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) {
    if (!processedIds.contains(l.Account__c)) {
        processedIds.add(l.Account__c); // no duplicates stored
    }
}
// Query using Set as bind variable
List<Account> accounts = [SELECT Id FROM Account WHERE Id IN :processedIds];

// MAP — key-value pairs, O(1) lookup by key
Map<Id, Account> accountMap = new Map<Id, Account>(
    [SELECT Id, Name, Total_Loans__c FROM Account WHERE Id IN :processedIds]
);
// Use in trigger — fast lookup without nested loop
for (Loan__c l : Trigger.new) {
    Account acc = accountMap.get(l.Account__c); // O(1) — no nested loop needed
    if (acc != null) acc.Total_Loans__c++;
}
update accountMap.values();
Pattern to remember

Collect IDs into a SET (unique), query into a MAP (fast lookup), process with loop, store results in LIST (for DML). This is the standard bulkification pattern.

Sales Cloud — complete overview for screening roundSALES CLOUD▼

Sales Cloud is Salesforce's CRM solution for managing the complete sales process from lead to closed deal.

ObjectPurposeKey fields
LeadUnqualified prospect not yet a customerCompany, Email, Phone, Status, LeadSource
AccountCompany/organization — customer or prospectName, Industry, AnnualRevenue, Type
ContactIndividual person associated with AccountFirstName, LastName, Email, AccountId
OpportunityPotential deal/sale in progressName, Amount, CloseDate, StageName, AccountId
Product2Product catalog itemName, ProductCode, IsActive
PricebookEntryPrice of a product in a pricebookUnitPrice, Pricebook2Id, Product2Id
QuoteFormal price quote sent to customerTotalPrice, ExpirationDate, OpportunityId
ContractFormal agreement with customerStartDate, ContractTerm, AccountId

Lead Conversion process:

  • Lead created (via web form, manual entry, or import)
  • SDR qualifies the lead — MQL (Marketing Qualified) → SQL (Sales Qualified)
  • Lead converted → creates Account + Contact + Opportunity automatically
  • Sales rep works the Opportunity through stages: Prospecting → Qualification → Proposal → Negotiation → Closed Won/Lost
  • Key metric: Opportunity pipeline by stage, win rate, average deal size
Screening answer

Mention: Lead-to-Cash lifecycle, Opportunity stages, CPQ concepts (Configure Price Quote), and any Einstein AI features like Lead Scoring or Opportunity Scoring if asked about modern Sales Cloud.

Service Cloud — complete overview for screening roundSERVICE CLOUD▼

Service Cloud manages customer support — from case creation to resolution.

ObjectPurposeKey fields
CaseCustomer issue or support requestSubject, Status, Priority, Origin, AccountId
EntitlementSLA definition for a customerName, AccountId, StartDate, EndDate
MilestoneTime-based SLA checkpoint on a caseMilestoneName, CompletionDate, IsCompleted
Knowledge ArticleDocumented solution/FAQTitle, UrlName, ArticleType, PublishStatus
Live Agent / MessagingReal-time chat with customersLiveChatTranscript, MessagingSession

Key Service Cloud features:

  • Case Assignment Rules — auto-assign cases to right agent/queue based on criteria
  • Case Escalation Rules — auto-escalate if case not resolved within SLA time
  • Entitlement Management — define SLA terms per account/product, track milestones
  • Omni-Channel — route work (cases, chats, calls) to agents based on availability and skills
  • Knowledge Base — agents search articles to resolve cases faster; deflection metric
  • CTI Integration — connect phone system to Salesforce via Open CTI for screen pops
  • Einstein Bots — AI-powered chatbots for first-line deflection before routing to agent
  • Service Console — agent productivity UI with split view, keyboard shortcuts, macros
Key interview point

Connect Entitlement → Milestone → Escalation as a chain: 'Entitlement defines the SLA. Milestones are checkpoints within the SLA (e.g., first response in 2 hours). Escalation Rules fire if milestone is not met — reassign and notify manager.'

LWC @wire decorator — how does it work with Apex?LWC WIRE▼
// Apex method must be @AuraEnabled(cacheable=true) for @wire
@AuraEnabled(cacheable=true)
public static List<Loan__c> getLoansByStatus(String status) {
    return [SELECT Id, Name, Amount__c FROM Loan__c WHERE Status__c = :status WITH SECURITY_ENFORCED];
}

// LWC — wire to Apex (reactive: re-calls when status changes)
import getLoansByStatus from '@salesforce/apex/LoanController.getLoansByStatus';

export default class LoanList extends LightningElement {
  status = 'Active';

  // Wire as function — handle data and error explicitly
  @wire(getLoansByStatus, { status: '$status' })
  wiredLoans({ data, error }) {
    if (data)  { this.loans = data;           this.error = undefined; }
    if (error) { this.error = error.body.message; this.loans = undefined; }
  }

  // Wire as property — simpler but less error handling
  @wire(getLoansByStatus, { status: 'Active' })
  activeLoans; // access as this.activeLoans.data / this.activeLoans.error

  // Refresh after a mutation (wire results are cached)
  async handleSave() {
    await saveLoan({ loan: this.loanData });
    refreshApex(this.wiredLoans); // force re-fetch from server
  }
}
cacheable=true is required for @wire

If the Apex method doesn't have cacheable=true, you cannot use @wire — you must call it imperatively with async/await instead.

LWC one-way vs two-way data binding?LWC BASICS▼

LWC only supports one-way data binding — data flows from JavaScript to the HTML template, not automatically back.

// ONE-WAY binding — JS value → HTML (standard LWC)
// loanCard.html
<template>
  <p>{loanName}</p>              <!-- reads JS property -->
  <input value={amount}></input>  <!-- shows JS value, but typing doesn't update JS -->
</template>

// loanCard.js
loanName = 'LOAN-001';
amount = 250000;
// Changing loanName in JS → template updates automatically (one-way ✓)
// User typing in input → JS amount does NOT update automatically (no two-way ✗)

// TO ACHIEVE TWO-WAY (manually handle the event):
handleAmountChange(event) {
  this.amount = event.target.value; // update JS from UI event
}
// template: <input value={amount} onchange={handleAmountChange}></input>
// Now: JS → UI (binding) + UI → JS (event handler) = effectively two-way
Interview answer

Say: 'LWC uses one-way data binding — property changes in JS automatically update the template. To update JS from user input, I handle the change event. This is more explicit and predictable than Angular-style two-way binding.'

LWC template directives — if:true, for:each, iterator?LWC BASICS▼
<template>
  <!-- CONDITIONAL — show/hide based on boolean -->
  <template if:true={isLoading}>
    <lightning-spinner></lightning-spinner>
  </template>
  <template if:false={isLoading}>
    <p>Content loaded</p>
  </template>

  <!-- FOR:EACH — iterate array (key required on immediate child) -->
  <template for:each={loans} for:item="loan" for:index="idx">
    <c-loan-card key={loan.Id} loan-id={loan.Id} loan-name={loan.Name}></c-loan-card>
  </template>

  <!-- ITERATOR — iterate with first/last metadata -->
  <template iterator:it={loans}>
    <div key={it.value.Id}>
      <template if:true={it.first}><hr></template>  <!-- top border on first item -->
      <p>{it.value.Name}</p>
      <template if:true={it.last}><hr></template>   <!-- bottom border on last item -->
    </div>
  </template>
</template>
key attribute is mandatory

for:each requires a unique key on the direct child element. Without it, LWC throws an error. Always use a stable unique ID — never use the array index.

LWC with standard components — lightning-record-form, lightning-datatable, lightning-combobox?LWC STANDARD▼
<!-- 1. lightning-record-form — auto CRUD for a record -->
<lightning-record-form
  record-id={recordId}
  object-api-name="Loan__c"
  fields={fields}
  mode="edit"
  onsuccess={handleSuccess}
  onerror={handleError}>
</lightning-record-form>

// js:
fields = ['Name', 'Status__c', 'Amount__c', 'CloseDate__c'];
handleSuccess(event) { this.dispatchEvent(new ShowToastEvent({title:'Saved',variant:'success'})); }

<!-- 2. lightning-datatable — display records in table -->
<lightning-datatable
  data={loans}
  columns={columns}
  key-field="Id"
  onrowaction={handleRowAction}>
</lightning-datatable>
// js:
columns = [
  { label: 'Name',   fieldName: 'Name',      type: 'text' },
  { label: 'Amount', fieldName: 'Amount__c',  type: 'currency' },
  { label: 'Status', fieldName: 'Status__c',  type: 'text' },
  { type: 'action',  typeAttributes: { rowActions: [{label:'View',name:'view'},{label:'Edit',name:'edit'}] } }
];
handleRowAction(event) {
  const action = event.detail.action.name;
  const row    = event.detail.row;
  if (action === 'view') this[NavigationMixin.Navigate]({type:'standard__recordPage', attributes:{recordId:row.Id,actionName:'view'}});
}

<!-- 3. lightning-combobox — dropdown select -->
<lightning-combobox
  label="Loan Status"
  value={selectedStatus}
  options={statusOptions}
  onchange={handleStatusChange}>
</lightning-combobox>
// js:
statusOptions = [
  { label: 'Applied', value: 'Applied' },
  { label: 'Approved', value: 'Approved' },
  { label: 'Funded', value: 'Funded' }
];
handleStatusChange(event) { this.selectedStatus = event.detail.value; }
LWC Lifecycle hooks — constructor, connectedCallback, renderedCallback?LWC LIFECYCLE▼
HookWhenUse for
constructor()Component created, DOM not readyInitialize private variables. Must call super() first.
connectedCallback()Component inserted into DOM, @api props setApex calls, subscribe to message channels, set up listeners
renderedCallback()After every renderDOM manipulation, init third-party libs. Use initialized flag for once-only logic.
disconnectedCallback()Component removed from DOMUnsubscribe channels, cancel timers, clean up
errorCallback(err,stack)Child lifecycle errorError boundary — log, show fallback UI
export default class LoanDashboard extends LightningElement {
  initialized = false;
  subscription = null;

  constructor() {
    super(); // must be first
    this.privateData = []; // OK — no DOM/props access here
  }

  connectedCallback() {
    this.loadLoanData(); // Apex call
    this.subscription = subscribe(this.msgCtx, CHANNEL, this.handleMsg);
  }

  renderedCallback() {
    if (this.initialized) return;
    this.initialized = true;
    const canvas = this.template.querySelector('.chart');
    this.initChart(canvas); // DOM access safe here
  }

  disconnectedCallback() {
    unsubscribe(this.subscription); // cleanup
  }
}

💻 Coding Challenge 1 — Parent/Child LWC with Account Dropdown + Contacts
Build two LWC components — parent shows Account dropdown, child shows related ContactsCODING CHALLENGE▼

Requirement: Parent LWC shows a dropdown of Accounts. When user selects an Account, child LWC displays that account's related Contacts list.

// ── APEX CONTROLLER ────────────────────────────────────────────────────
public with sharing class AccountContactController {
  @AuraEnabled(cacheable=true)
  public static List<Account> getAllAccounts() {
    return [SELECT Id, Name FROM Account ORDER BY Name LIMIT 200 WITH SECURITY_ENFORCED];
  }

  @AuraEnabled(cacheable=true)
  public static List<Contact> getContactsByAccount(Id accountId) {
    return [SELECT Id, Name, Email, Phone, Title FROM Contact
            WHERE AccountId = :accountId WITH SECURITY_ENFORCED ORDER BY Name];
  }
}
// ── PARENT COMPONENT: accountSelector.html ────────────────────────────
<template>
  <lightning-card title="Account Selector">

      <lightning-combobox
        label="Select Account"
        placeholder="-- Select an Account --"
        value={selectedAccountId}
        options={accountOptions}
        onchange={handleAccountChange}>
      </lightning-combobox>
      <template if:true={selectedAccountId}>
        <c-contact-list account-id={selectedAccountId}></c-contact-list>
      </template>
    </div>
  </lightning-card>
</template>

// ── PARENT: accountSelector.js ──────────────────────────────────────────
import { LightningElement, wire, track } from 'lwc';
import getAllAccounts from '@salesforce/apex/AccountContactController.getAllAccounts';

export default class AccountSelector extends LightningElement {
  @track selectedAccountId = '';
  accountOptions = [];

  @wire(getAllAccounts)
  wiredAccounts({ data, error }) {
    if (data) {
      this.accountOptions = data.map(acc => ({ label: acc.Name, value: acc.Id }));
    } else if (error) {
      console.error('Error loading accounts:', error);
    }
  }

  handleAccountChange(event) {
    this.selectedAccountId = event.detail.value;
  }
}
// ── CHILD COMPONENT: contactList.html ──────────────────────────────────
<template>
  <lightning-card title="Related Contacts">
    <template if:true={isLoading}>
      <lightning-spinner alternative-text="Loading contacts..."></lightning-spinner>
    </template>
    <template if:false={isLoading}>
      <template if:true={hasContacts}>
        <lightning-datatable
          data={contacts}
          columns={columns}
          key-field="Id">
        </lightning-datatable>
      </template>
      <template if:false={hasContacts}>
        <p class="slds-p-around_medium slds-text-color_weak">No contacts found for this account.</p>
      </template>
      <template if:true={errorMessage}>
        <p class="slds-text-color_error">{errorMessage}</p>
      </template>
    </template>
  </lightning-card>
</template>

// ── CHILD: contactList.js ───────────────────────────────────────────────
import { LightningElement, api, wire, track } from 'lwc';
import getContactsByAccount from '@salesforce/apex/AccountContactController.getContactsByAccount';

export default class ContactList extends LightningElement {
  @api accountId;   // receives selected Account Id from parent
  @track contacts = [];
  @track isLoading = false;
  @track errorMessage = '';

  columns = [
    { label: 'Name',  fieldName: 'Name',  type: 'text' },
    { label: 'Email', fieldName: 'Email', type: 'email' },
    { label: 'Phone', fieldName: 'Phone', type: 'phone' },
    { label: 'Title', fieldName: 'Title', type: 'text' }
  ];

  @wire(getContactsByAccount, { accountId: '$accountId' })
  wiredContacts({ data, error }) {
    this.isLoading = false;
    if (data) {
      this.contacts     = data;
      this.errorMessage = '';
    } else if (error) {
      this.errorMessage = error.body?.message || 'Error loading contacts';
      this.contacts     = [];
    }
  }

  get hasContacts() { return this.contacts && this.contacts.length > 0; }
}

💻 Coding Challenge 2 — Opportunity Count on Account + Email to Owner's Manager
Show Opportunity count on Account and send email notification to owner's managerCODING CHALLENGE▼

Requirement: When Opportunities are created/updated/deleted, update a total count field on the Account. Then send an email notification to the Opportunity owner's manager.

// ── STEP 1: Custom field on Account ────────────────────────────────────
// Create: Account.Total_Opportunities__c  (Number, 0 decimal places)

// ── STEP 2: Trigger ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────
trigger OpportunityTrigger on Opportunity (after insert, after update, after delete, after undelete) {
  OpportunityTriggerHandler.handle(
    Trigger.new, Trigger.old, Trigger.operationType
  );
}

// ── STEP 3: Handler + Service ───────────────────────────────────────────
public class OpportunityTriggerHandler {
  public static void handle(List<Opportunity> newList, List<Opportunity> oldList,
                             System.TriggerOperation opType) {
    Set<Id> affectedAccountIds = new Set<Id>();

    if (newList != null) for (Opportunity o : newList) if (o.AccountId != null) affectedAccountIds.add(o.AccountId);
    if (oldList != null) for (Opportunity o : oldList) if (o.AccountId != null) affectedAccountIds.add(o.AccountId);

    if (affectedAccountIds.isEmpty()) return;

    OpportunityRollupService.updateOppCount(affectedAccountIds);

    // Send email only on new Opportunities
    if (opType == System.TriggerOperation.AFTER_INSERT) {
      OpportunityEmailService.notifyManagers(newList);
    }
  }
}

// ── STEP 4: Rollup Service ──────────────────────────────────────────────
public class OpportunityRollupService {
  public static void updateOppCount(Set<Id> accountIds) {
    // Aggregate count per account
    Map<Id, Integer> countMap = new Map<Id, Integer>();
    for (Id accId : accountIds) countMap.put(accId, 0); // default 0

    for (AggregateResult ar : [
        SELECT AccountId accId, COUNT(Id) cnt
        FROM Opportunity
        WHERE AccountId IN :accountIds AND StageName != 'Closed Lost'
        GROUP BY AccountId
    ]) {
      countMap.put((Id) ar.get('accId'), (Integer) ar.get('cnt'));
    }

    List<Account> toUpdate = new List<Account>();
    for (Id accId : accountIds) {
      toUpdate.add(new Account(Id=accId, Total_Opportunities__c=countMap.get(accId)));
    }
    update toUpdate;
  }
}

// ── STEP 5: Email Notification Service ─────────────────────────────────
public class OpportunityEmailService {
  public static void notifyManagers(List<Opportunity> opps) {
    // Get Owner IDs
    Set<Id> ownerIds = new Set<Id>();
    for (Opportunity o : opps) ownerIds.add(o.OwnerId);

    // Get Owner + Manager details
    Map<Id, User> userMap = new Map<Id, User>(
      [SELECT Id, Name, Email, ManagerId, Manager.Name, Manager.Email
       FROM User WHERE Id IN :ownerIds AND ManagerId != null]
    );

    // Build emails — one per Opportunity
    List<Messaging.SingleEmailMessage> emails = new List<Messaging.SingleEmailMessage>();
    for (Opportunity o : opps) {
      User owner = userMap.get(o.OwnerId);
      if (owner == null || owner.ManagerId == null) continue; // skip if no manager

      Messaging.SingleEmailMessage mail = new Messaging.SingleEmailMessage();
      mail.setToAddresses(new String[]{ owner.Manager.Email });
      mail.setSubject('New Opportunity Created: ' + o.Name);
      mail.setPlainTextBody(
        'Hello ' + owner.Manager.Name + ',

' +
        'A new Opportunity has been created by your team member ' + owner.Name + ':

' +
        'Opportunity Name: ' + o.Name + '
' +
        'Amount: $' + (o.Amount != null ? String.valueOf(o.Amount) : 'Not set') + '
' +
        'Stage: ' + o.StageName + '
' +
        'Close Date: ' + String.valueOf(o.CloseDate) + '

' +
        'Please review in Salesforce.

Regards,
Salesforce Automation'
      );
      emails.add(mail);
    }

    if (!emails.isEmpty()) Messaging.sendEmail(emails);
  }
}
Why this design

Separating rollup logic (OpportunityRollupService) from email logic (OpportunityEmailService) follows the Single Responsibility principle — each can be tested and changed independently.

// Key Sales Cloud SOQL patterns
// Lead conversion rate
SELECT LeadSource, COUNT(Id) total, SUM(IsConverted) converted
FROM Lead GROUP BY LeadSource

// Pipeline by stage
SELECT StageName, COUNT(Id) cnt, SUM(Amount) total
FROM Opportunity WHERE IsClosed = false GROUP BY StageName ORDER BY SUM(Amount) DESC

// Opportunity with Products
SELECT Id, Name, Amount,
  (SELECT Id, Product2.Name, UnitPrice, Quantity FROM OpportunityLineItems)
FROM Opportunity WHERE Id = :oppId
Key differentiator

Know the difference between Forecast Category and Stage. A stage is where the deal IS in the process. Forecast Category is the REVENUE recognition expectation: Pipeline, Best Case, Commit, Omitted, Closed. They're related but different.

🎧 Service Cloud — In Depth
Service Cloud — complete deep dive for technical roundSERVICE CLOUD▼

Complete Case lifecycle and Service Cloud architecture:

  • Case Origins — Email-to-Case (inbound email creates Case), Web-to-Case (web form), Omni-Channel (chat, social, phone), manual creation
  • Case Assignment Rules — route Cases to right queue/agent based on criteria (product, priority, skill)
  • Case Escalation Rules — auto-escalate if not responded to within SLA window; reassign + notify manager
  • SLA with Entitlement + Milestones — Entitlement defines SLA terms; Milestones are time targets within the SLA (first response ≤ 2 hrs, resolution ≤ 8 hrs)
  • Omni-Channel — intelligent routing across channels (chat, email, case, custom objects) based on agent availability and capacity
  • Knowledge Management — Knowledge Articles (FAQ, how-to), search from case to suggest articles, CSAT deflection metrics
  • Service Console — split-view UI, utility bar, keyboard shortcuts, macros for agent productivity
  • CTI (Computer Telephony Integration) — Open CTI SDK connects phone system; screen pop shows caller's Account/Case
// Case with Entitlement pattern
// 1. Create Entitlement for Account
Entitlement ent = new Entitlement(
  Name='Premium SLA', AccountId=accId, StartDate=Date.today(),
  EndDate=Date.today().addYears(1), SlaProcessId=slaId
);
insert ent;

// 2. Link Case to Entitlement (auto-applies SLA milestones)
Case c = new Case(Subject='Integration down', AccountId=accId,
  EntitlementId=ent.Id, Priority='High');
insert c; // SLA milestones automatically created and tracked

// 3. Query Case Milestones
List<CaseMilestone> milestones = [
  SELECT Id, MilestoneType.Name, CompletionDate, IsCompleted, RemainingTimeInMins
  FROM CaseMilestone WHERE CaseId = :c.Id
];
Escalation vs Assignment

Assignment Rule = routes new Cases to the right team/person. Escalation Rule = reassigns/notifies if Case is NOT resolved within the SLA time. Both are setup-based, not code-based.

⏰ Cron Expressions in Salesforce
Cron expressions in Salesforce Scheduled Apex — complete referenceSCHEDULED APEX▼

Salesforce cron expression has 7 positions (not 5 like standard Unix cron):

// Position:  Seconds  Minutes  Hours  Day-of-Month  Month  Day-of-Week  Year
// Format:    0-59     0-59     0-23   1-31          1-12   1-7 or SUN-SAT  (optional)

// Special characters:
// *  = any value
// ?  = no specific value (use for Day-of-Month OR Day-of-Week — not both)
// -  = range (e.g., MON-FRI)
// ,  = list (e.g., MON,WED,FRI)
// /  = increment (e.g., 0/15 = every 15 starting from 0)
// L  = last (e.g., L in Day-of-Month = last day of month)

// COMMON EXAMPLES:
'0 0 2 * * ?'           // Every day at 2:00 AM
'0 0 2 ? * MON'         // Every Monday at 2:00 AM
'0 0 2 1 * ?'           // First day of every month at 2:00 AM
'0 0 0 1 1 ? *'         // January 1st every year at midnight
'0 0/30 * * * ?'        // Every 30 minutes (avoid — use PE instead)
'0 0 8-17 ? * MON-FRI'  // Every hour 8AM-5PM Mon-Fri
'0 0 2 L * ?'           // Last day of every month at 2AM

// SCHEDULE AN APEX JOB:
String cronExpr = '0 0 2 * * ?'; // 2AM daily
String jobName  = 'Nightly Loan Sync';
System.schedule(jobName, cronExpr, new NightlyLoanSyncSchedule());

// CHECK SCHEDULED JOBS:
List<CronTrigger> jobs = [
  SELECT Id, CronJobDetail.Name, CronExpression, State, NextFireTime
  FROM CronTrigger WHERE CronJobDetail.Name = :jobName
];

// ABORT A SCHEDULED JOB:
for (CronTrigger ct : jobs) System.abortJob(ct.Id);

// QUERY ALL ACTIVE SCHEDULED JOBS:
[SELECT Id, CronJobDetail.Name, NextFireTime, State FROM CronTrigger
 WHERE State NOT IN ('DELETED','COMPLETE') ORDER BY NextFireTime]
Frequency limit

Do not schedule jobs more frequently than once per hour using Scheduled Apex. For higher frequency automation, use Platform Events + trigger subscribers. Salesforce limits orgs to 100 scheduled jobs total.

🤖 Agentforce — In Depth
Agentforce complete architecture — everything a developer needs to knowAGENTFORCE▼

Agentforce = Salesforce's autonomous AI agent platform (GA: Fall 2024). Agents reason, plan, and execute multi-step tasks.

ComponentWhat it isDeveloper role

TopicCategory of intent the agent handlesDefine instructions + which actions belong
Agent ActionSpecific operation the agent can performBuild Apex @InvocableMethod or Flow
Prompt TemplateReusable AI prompts with merge fieldsBuild in Prompt Builder (Setup)
